PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 24 of 200
Question ID: 610015
Project initiation is complete, and the project manager is about to begin project planning. The
company has completed similar projects in the past, but the project manager was not involved
with those projects. The project manager has reviewed the project charter to gain a high-level
understanding of the project as a starting point for project planning.
What should the project manager do next?
- **A Consult with a project manager who managed similar past projects**
- **B Prepare for project planning by performing the Manage Project Knowledge process**
- **C Review the lessons learned register**
- **D Search the organizational process assets for information on similar projects completed**
previously
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where are the lessons learned from past projects found?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The lessons learned repository is an organizational process asset that serves as a store of
historical information about lessons learned from projects. The question indicates that the
company has completed similar projects in the past, but the project manager of the current
project was not involved in those projects. Therefore, of the choices provided, the next logical
step for the project manager to take is to search the organizational process assets for relevant
information contained in the lessons learned repository as this information may prove helpful in
planning the current project.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Consult with a project manager who managed similar past projects**
Incorrect. While the project manager of similar past projects may have some relevant
information, this information reflects only one opinion. Checking the organizational
process assets is a better answer choice because the lessons learned are likely to have more
complete and accurate information that reflect the views of all project team members.
- **B Prepare for project planning by performing the Manage Project Knowledge process**
Incorrect. The question states that project planning is about to start. The Manage Project
Knowledge process is part of the Executing Process Group, which is not performed until
project planning is complete.
- **C Review the lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register is a source for information on the current project. At
this stage of the project, there is likely to be little or no information available to be
captured in the lessons learned register. Information on past projects is contained in the
lessons learned repository rather than the lessons learned register.
- **D Search the organizational process assets for information on similar projects completed**
previously
Correct. The question indicates that the company has completed similar projects in the
past, but the project manager of the current project was not involved in those projects.
Therefore, the next logical step for the project manager to take is to search the
organizational process assets for relevant information contained in the lessons learned
repository.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 84, 104

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 25 of 200
Question ID: 612397
You meet with the project sponsor to discuss the sponsor's idea which triggered the project. Even
though the concept for the project is new and untested, the sponsor believes that the company's
development team is prepared to execute her vision. You start documenting the reasons the
sponsor thinks the company is capable to deliver this untested concept.
Which project document is being created?
- **A Communications management plan**
- **B Assumption log**
- **C Requirements documentation**
- **D Lessons learned register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In which process group are the activities described being performed?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

There are a couple of ways you can determine the correct answer in this scenario. In one method,
you would need to understand that the project management activities described in this scenario
are part of the Initiating Process Group, and that the assumption log is the only project document
of the four answer choices that is an output of a process in the Initiating Process Group, making
the assumption log the only viable answer. The second method relies on knowing the meaning of
an assumption. An assumption is a factor in the planning process that is considered to be true,
real, or certain, without proof or demonstration. The assumption in this scenario is the sponsor's
belief that the development team has the capabilities to deliver an untested concept.
Documenting this assumption implies that the assumption log is being created, making the
assumption log the best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Communications management plan**
Incorrect. The communications management plan describes how, when, and by whom
project information will be handled and distributed. First, the communications
management plan would not include assumptions. Secondly, the communications
management plan is created in the Planning Process Group, while the situation described
implies the project is in initiating. In addition, the communications management plan is not
a project document as asked by the question, but a component of the project management
plan. Considering these reasons, the communications management plan is not the best
answer choice.
- **B Assumption log**
Correct. The assumption log is a project document used to document assumptions and
constraints expected to be in place or to be in evidence during the project. A project's
assumption log is first created as an output of the Develop Project Charter process in the
Initiating Process Group, which according to the scenario is described in the question.
Therefore, of the choices provided, the assumption log is the best answer to the question
asked.
- **C Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. Requirements documentation is a project document that describes how individual
requirements meet the business need for the project. Requirements documentation does not
include the assumptions nor is it developed during project initiation which is the situation
implied by the scenario.
- **D Lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register is a project document that captures information
about a situation encountered during the project to help improve the performance of the
project and to avoid repeating mistakes. The lessons learned register does not capture
presumed truths (i.e., assumptions) about a project, but documents situations and their
resolutions that occur throughout the project life cycle. Also, the lessons learned register is
first created as an output of the Manage Project Knowledge process in the Executing
Process Group, while the scenario describes a situation that takes place in the Initiating
Process Group.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 81
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 26 of 200
Question ID: 612089
The project you are leading is behind schedule. A team member suggests a change that may help
bring the project back on track. You agree with the team member and issue a request for
corrective action.
This request would be an outcome of which of the following processes?
- **A Develop Project Management Plan**
- **B Develop Project Charter**
- **C Perform Integrated Change Control**
- **D Monitor and Control Project Work**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Issuing a corrective action is the same as issuing a change request. What process of the listed
above has change requests as one of its outputs?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes a project that falls behind schedule. Such a determination could have
been a result of comparing the actual project performance with the schedule baseline. Reviewing
the differences between planned and actual project performance is known as variance analysis.
Variance analysis is one of the tools and techniques of the Monitor and Control Project Work
process. When issues are found during the Monitor and Control Project Work process, change
requests are submitted to rectify the problem. Therefore, in this scenario, submitting a change
request has occurred in the Monitor and Control Project Work process. In other words, corrective
action is an outcome of the Monitor and Control Project Work process.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Develop Project Management Plan**
Incorrect. Develop Project Management Plan is the process that involves preparing a
document that defines all the project work. This would be done during the Planning process
group. Corrective actions are issued after the project has begun execution, making this
choice an incorrect answer.
- **B Develop Project Charter**
Incorrect. Develop Project Charter is the process of drafting a document that when
approved, will formally initiate the project. The Develop Project Charter process is part of
the Initiating Process Group, while your project is already in execution.
- **C Perform Integrated Change Control**
Incorrect. Changes such as corrective actions can be requested as a result of performing
project work or comparing actual project performance with the baselines. In other words,
changes can be requested while carrying out project management processes such as Direct
and Manage Project Work or Monitor and Control Project Work, but not the Perform
Integrated Change Control process. Rather, the Perform Integrated Change Control
process is used to review, approve, and manage changes on the project.
- **D Monitor and Control Project Work**
Correct. Monitor and Control Project Work is the process of tracking and analyzing project
performance to ensure the project is progressing according to the project management
plan. One of the activities performed in this process is comparing actual project
performance to the baselines. As a result of the project falling behind schedule, you have
submitted a request for a corrective action. Therefore, the request becomes an output of the
Monitor and Control Project Work process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 112
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 27 of 200
Question ID: 612655
- **A project with a tight budget to update an inventory control system is underway. A key**
stakeholder submits a request to replace all barcode scanners. The request is rejected by the
CCB. The stakeholder contacts the project manager and insists that replacing all the scanners is
necessary as some of the existing units are broken. The project manager is concerned that the
stakeholder may become resistant to the project if the issue is not addressed promptly.
What is the best course of action?
- **A Offering to assist the stakeholder by submitting a change request to replace only the**
broken scanners
- **B Explaining that the project budget does not include funds for the replacement of the**
scanners
- **C Referring the stakeholder to the project sponsor since the issue is beyond the authority of**
the project manager
- **D Promising the key stakeholder that the replacement of the scanners will be included in the**
next project
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice represents an action within the project manager's scope of authority that
might resolve the issue?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the project manager is performing the Manage Stakeholder
Engagement process and needs to resolve an issue for a stakeholder to retain their support.
Negotiation is one of the tools and techniques which may be useful during the Manage
Stakeholder Engagement process. It is best to negotiate a reasonable solution to the problem
described in the question to retain the stakeholder's support for the project. Since the change

---

request to replace all of the barcode scanners was denied, there is no point in resubmitting the
same request. However, just replacing the broken scanners seems like a reasonable solution that
might be best for the stakeholder and the project. The change control board (CCB) might
approve replacing the broken scanners even if they denied replacing all of the scanners
previously. Therefore, of the available choices, the best course of action is to offer to assist the
stakeholder by submitting a change request to replace only the broken scanners.
Note that the concern raised by the key stakeholder should be captured in the issue log as well.
However, updating the issue log was not listed as an answer choice. On the real exam, the PMP
aspirant will likely encounter situations where the obvious answer is not listed as an option, and
the 'best' answer must be selected from the available choices.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Offering to assist the stakeholder by submitting a change request to replace only the**
broken scanners
Correct. This answer choice represents the interpersonal and team skill of negotiation. It is
best to negotiate a reasonable solution to the concern raised by the stakeholder to retain
their support for the project.
- **B Explaining that the project budget does not include funds for the replacement of the**
scanners
Incorrect. While the question describes a project with a tight budget, the scenario does not
provide the reason for the rejection of the change request. If it did, explaining the rationale
for the denial may be necessary. However, it does not resolve the stakeholder's concern.
- **C Referring the stakeholder to the project sponsor since the issue is beyond the authority of**
the project manager
Incorrect. Issues beyond the authority of the project manager will likely be addressed by the
project sponsor. However, the project sponsor should only be involved when other
alternatives that are under the control of the project manager have been exploited. There is
another answer choice that describes a plausible option without the need of escalating to
the project sponsor.
- **D Promising the key stakeholder that the replacement of the scanners will be included in the**
next project
Incorrect. The project manager may not be able to keep this commitment. The replacement
of scanners may or may not be relevant to the next project. More importantly, the project

---

manager does not secure funding or approve project management plans and baselines for
projects. The project manager is not likely to have the authority to ensure the replacement
scanners can be included in the scope of the next project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 527
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 28 of 200
Question ID: 626039
During project execution, significant volumes of work performance data are being generated.
The project manager wishes to select some of this data to be reviewed and analyzed in the
controlling processes to assess project performance.
Which of the following examples of work performance data is the project manager most likely to
select for such an analysis?
- **A The number of the project team members**
- **B Story points completed**
- **C Estimated activity durations**
- **D Planned costs**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Information that is available or developed during the project planning is not considered work
performance data.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

To answer this question properly, one needs to understand what is considered work performance
data. Work performance data are the raw observations and measurements identified during
activities being performed to carry out the project work. This data is generated during project
execution and feeds or flows into various controlling processes. The controlling processes
compare the work performance data with the established project baselines to assess project
performance. Information available or developed during project planning is not considered work
performance data. Examples of work performance data include work completed, key
performance indicators, technical performance measures, actual start and finish dates of schedule

---

activities, story points completed, deliverables status, etc. Of the choices provided, only story
points completed qualifies as work performance data.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The number of the project team members**
Incorrect. A number of the project team members is typically already known during the
project planning and is not data generated during the project execution. Therefore,
knowing the number of the project team members will not help the project manager in
assessing the project performance.
- **B Story points completed**
Correct. Story points completed is an example of the work performance data generated
during the project execution and therefore can be used in the controlling processes by the
project manager to assess project performance. Other examples include key performance
indicators, actual start and finish dates, etc.
- **C Estimated activity durations**
Incorrect. Estimated activity durations are developed during project planning and not
during execution. It is the actual, not the ‘estimated’ activity durations, that are generated
during project execution and can be used in the controlling processes for further analysis of
project performance.
- **D Planned costs**
Incorrect. Planned costs are developed during project planning. It is the actual and not the
planned costs that are generated during project execution and can be used in the
controlling processes for further analysis of project performance.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 95
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 29 of 200
Question ID: 651312
Your new project is very similar to others conducted within your company. You want to review
comparable project quality standards to measure quality performance in your new project.
Which tool or technique is best for you to use?
- **A Benchmarking**
- **B Brainstorming**
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
- **D Analogous estimating**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is being compared?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

When planning your project’s quality, you can benchmark your project against those of other
projects. This technique relies on the similarity of your current and historical projects and/or
project deliverables to have a meaningful comparison. In finding comparable project standards
and measurements, your project has a point of comparison, which can aid in setting targets to
aim or associate with, if seeking to meet or surpass another project’s standard.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Benchmarking**

---

Correct. Benchmarking is the tool and technique best used in this situation to capture
metrics and standards from comparable projects. Comparing your project’s quality
standards against similar projects is a good start for establishing a point of comparison.
- **B Brainstorming**
Incorrect. Discussing the standards of other projects and throwing out ideas for this project
may be useful, but it is not the best method to capture results and plans that already exist
from other projects.
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
Incorrect. Cost-benefit analysis is not related to planning the quality management of a
project and its comparison to other similar projects.
- **D Analogous estimating**
Incorrect. When estimating project costs, the project team can use the analogous estimating
technique to assist in acquiring estimates based on other similar projects within the
company. Nonetheless, in this instance, we seek information on how to level or place our
project’s quality standards and metrics to measure against.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 281

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 30 of 200
Question ID: 613141
You are in the process of obtaining the necessary facilities, equipment, and materials for a cargo
ship renovation project. You have just learned that the drydock where you must do the
renovation is not available due to delays with an existing ship construction project.
With the schedule baseline now unattainable, what is your best course of action?
- **A Utilize the contingency reserves to meet the project deadline**
- **B Submit a change request to update the schedule baseline**
- **C Update the schedule baseline as needed**
- **D Terminate the project since the schedule baseline has been invalidated**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is required to update any of the project's baselines?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that during the Acquire Resources process, a key resource is not available
and the resulting delay has made the schedule baseline unattainable. Since the schedule baseline
has been invalidated due to the unavailability of the drydock, an approved change request is
required to update the schedule baseline. If the change request is denied, then the result of that
decision may lead to the termination of the project. If the change request is approved, then the
project can proceed with the updated schedule baseline. Therefore, the best course of action in
this scenario is to submit a change request to update the schedule baseline.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Utilize the contingency reserves to meet the project deadline**
Incorrect. Contingency reserves are included in the schedule baseline. If the schedule
baseline is not attainable, then the contingency reserves are insufficient to cover the delay
caused by the lack of access to the drydock.
- **B Submit a change request to update the schedule baseline**
Correct. Since the schedule baseline has been invalidated due to the unavailability of the
drydock, an approved change request is required to update the schedule baseline.
- **C Update the schedule baseline as needed**
Incorrect. The schedule baseline is always considered a configuration element and requires
an approved change request for any modification.
- **D Terminate the project since the schedule baseline has been invalidated**
Incorrect. In this scenario, the project may or may not be terminated due to the
unavoidable project delays. However, terminating the project at this point is a premature
action. First, a change request should be submitted to update the schedule baseline. If the
change request is denied, then the result of that decision may lead to the termination of the
project. Additionally, a project manager does not have the authority to terminate a project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 334

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 31 of 200
Question ID: 626015
- **A project sponsor asks the project manager how well the project is doing in terms of budget. The**
project manager reviews work performance data and informs the sponsor that the project is doing
well.
What is wrong with the project manager's approach?
- **A Nothing is wrong with the project manager's approach.**
- **B The project manager should have reviewed work performance information.**
- **C The project manager should have reviewed the cost baseline.**
- **D The project manager should have consulted the accounting department.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Work performance data has only out-of-context meaning.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

To determine how well the project is doing in terms of budget, the project manager should have
reviewed the work performance information rather than work performance data. Work
performance data by itself should not be used in the decision-making process as it has only
out-of-context meaning. Work performance information, on the other hand, is correlated and
contextualized, and provides a foundation for project decisions. As an example, the project
manager could have compared the actual project performance, such as funds spent, to the cost
baseline. Such comparison could have provided the project manager with the cost variance, cost
performance indicator, estimate to complete, which would have allowed the project manager to
determine project's health and report back to the project sponsor.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Nothing is wrong with the project manager's approach.**
Incorrect. Work performance data has only out-of-context meaning. To determine the health
of the project, the work performance data should be transformed into contextualized work
performance information which then can be used to reach a conclusion regarding how well
the project is doing.
- **B The project manager should have reviewed work performance information.**
Correct. Work performance information is the project performance data collected from
various processes, analyzed in context, and integrated based on relationships across areas.
Unlike work performance data, work performance information is correlated and
contextualized, and allows the project stakeholders to reach a conclusion regarding project
health.
- **C The project manager should have reviewed the cost baseline.**
Incorrect. Baselines alone do not tell the story. To determine how well the project is doing,
actual project performance should be compared to the planned baselines.
- **D The project manager should have consulted the accounting department.**
Incorrect. The accounting department has little to nothing to do with the performance of
the project. Typically, an accounting department provides accounting services and financial
support to the organization, such as recording accounts payable and receivable, inventory,
payroll, assets, and so on.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 109
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 32 of 200
Question ID: 612665
You work with your team to develop the change management plan for your project. Your
company policy requires the appointment of a change control board (CCB) for all projects.
Which of the following would you not include as an element of the plan?
- **A Information about how seller-created changes will be processed**
- **B The roles and responsibilities of the change control board (CCB)**
- **C The description of how change requests are managed**
- **D A log to record the disposition of changes requested on the project**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The change management plan provides the direction for managing the change control process on
a project.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The change management plan is a component of the project management plan that establishes the
change control board, documents the extent of its authority, and describes how the change
control system will be implemented. The question is asking which of the answer choices would
'not' be included as an element of the change management plan. The disposition of all change
requests is recorded in the change log as a project document update. Project documents updates
are an output of the Perform Integrated Change Control process. The change log is not a part of
the change management plan.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Information about how seller-created changes will be processed**
Incorrect. The change management plan serves as an input into the Control Procurements
process. The change management plan contains information about how changes, including
seller-created, will be processed.
- **B The roles and responsibilities of the change control board (CCB)**
Incorrect. The change management plan provides the direction for managing the change
control process and documents the roles and responsibilities of the CCB.
- **C The description of how change requests are managed**
Incorrect. The change management plan describes how the change requests throughout the
project will be formally authorized and incorporated. In other words, the plan describes
how change requests are managed.
- **D A log to record the disposition of changes requested on the project**
Correct. The disposition of all change requests is recorded in the change log, not the
change management plan, as a project document update.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 88, 116, 120, 495

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 33 of 200
Question ID: 612164
- **A project manager is leading a project with a predictive life cycle. Detailed plans were provided**
by the requesting organization before the start of the project.
What will be the focus of the project manager?
- **A Controlling the schedule by successively adding functionality until the deadline is reached**
- **B Controlling scope to meet schedule and budget**
- **C Determining the scope before the start of each iteration**
- **D Revising cost and time estimates as the project team's understanding of the product**
increases
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Predictive life cycles may also be referred to as a waterfall life cycles.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question describes a project with a predictive life cycle. In a predictive life cycle, the project
scope, time, and cost are determined in the early phases of the life cycle. Any changes to the
scope are carefully managed to achieve the project's objectives of scope, time, and budget. A
predictive or waterfall framework is more likely to be utilized for a project, where the project
scope is well-understood and can be comprehensively decomposed during initial project
planning. Predictive life cycles may also be referred to as waterfall life cycles.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Controlling the schedule by successively adding functionality until the deadline is reached**
Incorrect. In an incremental rather than predictive life cycle, the deliverable is produced
through a series of iterations that successively add functionality within a predetermined
time frame.
- **B Controlling scope to meet schedule and budget**
Correct. In a predictive life cycle, the project scope, time, and cost are determined in the
early phases of the life cycle. Any changes to the scope are carefully managed.
- **C Determining the scope before the start of each iteration**
Incorrect. With an adaptive life cycle, as opposed to a predictive life cycle, the detailed
scope is defined and approved before the start of each iteration. A predictive life cycle
approach does not utilize iterations.
- **D Revising cost and time estimates as the project team's understanding of the product**
increases
Incorrect. In an iterative life cycle, as opposed to the predictive life cycle the project scope
is generally determined early in the project life cycle, but time and cost estimates are
routinely modified as the project team's understanding of the product increases.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 19
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 34 of 200
Question ID: 613798
You are leading a multi-phase project. A project team has just received notification from key
project stakeholders that the deliverables of the current phase are functioning as expected;
however, no formal document confirming this acceptance has been provided.
What process is likely to be your biggest concern before moving into the next project phase?
- **A Control Quality**
- **B Manage Team**
- **C Validate Scope**
- **D Monitor Risks**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of these processes produces an input to the Close Project or Phase process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Validate Scope is the process of formalizing acceptance of the completed or interim project
deliverables. Accepted deliverables are required before a phase, or project can be closed. Without
an accepted deliverable, the project will not be able to move into the next phase. Therefore,
Validate Scope, which yields accepted deliverables as one of its outputs, would be the project
manager's biggest concern.
Note, the Close Project or Phase process should also be performed before the phase can be
closed; however, this answer choice is not provided.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Control Quality**
Incorrect. Control Quality is a process that is concerned with the correctness of the
deliverables and meeting the quality requirements resulting in a verified deliverable. The
project team received confirmation from the key project stakeholders that the system is
functioning as expected. This implies that the Control Quality process for this deliverable
has already been completed earlier, making this choice an incorrect answer.
- **B Manage Team**
Incorrect. Manage Team is the process of tracking team member performance, providing
feedback, resolving issues, and managing team changes to optimize project performance.
While project managers should always strive for managing their teams to optimize project
performance, the scenario surrounds the activities needed to formally accept the
deliverables rather than manage the team.
- **C Validate Scope**
Correct. The Validate Scope process results in accepted deliverables which are a
requirement for the Close Project or Phase process as well as a prerequisite for moving
into the next phase of a project. Therefore, carrying out the Validate Scope process should
be your biggest concern before moving into the next phase.
- **D Monitor Risks**
Incorrect. The process of monitoring risks involves evaluating the risk process effectiveness
throughout the project. In this scenario, the project is moving from one phase to another.
Therefore, it is reasonable to assume that risks relevant to the current phase have already
been monitored and handled. Now your biggest concern should be accepted deliverables
which are an output from the Validate Scope process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 166, 164

Question 35 of 200
Question ID: 612670
The project requirements specify the need to print out latest architectural drawings weekly, at full
size, and in color. The printers needed are large and expensive, and will only be needed at a few
of the project team's many offices, necessitating careful planning for the acquisition and location
of the large-format printers.
Which plan or document can provide the locations where the printers will be needed?
- **A Resource calendars**
- **B Activity attributes**
- **C Scope baseline**
- **D Activity list**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What plan or document goes into great detail to include location information?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario indicates the project is in the Estimate Activity Resources process. Of the various
plans and documents that are inputs to this process, only activity attributes will provide the level
of detail needed to identify locations for each activity. Examples of activity attributes include
resource requirements, imposed dates, activity location, assumptions, and constraints. The
activity list is a close second as it provides the activity description, but it does not specify the
location detail.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Resource calendars**
Incorrect. Resource calendars identify the working days and shifts on which each specific
resource is available but do not contain the specifications for these resources such as
location.
- **B Activity attributes**
Correct. Activity attributes provide the primary data source for use in estimating the team
and physical resources required for each activity on the activity list, including the activity
location.
- **C Scope baseline**
Incorrect. The scope baseline identifies the project and product scope necessary to meet
project objectives. However, it does not provide details at the individual activity or resource
level such as resource location.
- **D Activity list**
Incorrect. The activity list identifies the activities that will need resources. However, it is the
activity attributes that provide the primary data source for use in estimating team and
physical resources, including location.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 322, 186

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 36 of 200
Question ID: 625045
- **A change request to increase the scope of the project has been approved.**
What should the project manager do next?
- **A Revise the scope management plan**
- **B Get an approval from the project sponsor**
- **C Modify the stakeholder register**
- **D Update the performance measurement baseline**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which element of the project management plan should be updated in response to approved
changes in scope, schedule performance, or cost estimates?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The performance measurement baseline (PMB) is a component of the project management plan
that integrates scope, schedule, and cost baselines and is used for comparison to manage,
measure, and control project execution. Updates to the PMB are one of the outputs of the Control
Scope process described in the question. Changes to the performance measurement baseline are
incorporated in response to approved changes in scope, schedule performance, or cost estimates.
In the scenario, a scope change has been approved warranting the update of the performance
measurement baseline.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Revise the scope management plan**
Incorrect. The scope management plan describes how the scope will be defined, developed,
monitored, controlled, and validated. The change request was approved to increase the
scope of the project, not to change the way the scope is managed.
- **B Get an approval from the project sponsor**
Incorrect. The change request has already been approved. There is not enough information
in the question to determine whether an additional approval from the project sponsor is
required when there is a change in project scope.
- **C Modify the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is the project document that captures the identification,
assessment, and classification of project stakeholders. It is possible but highly unlikely that
the scope change may result in new stakeholders to be brought to the project to handle the
change or the information about the current stakeholders to be modified as a result of this
change.
- **D Update the performance measurement baseline**
Correct. The performance measurement baseline (PMB) is the integrated scope, schedule,
and cost baselines used for comparison to manage, measure, and control project execution.
Since the change in scope will likely require an update to the scope baseline, updating the
PMB is the next reasonable step for the project manager to take.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 171, 88

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 37 of 200
Question ID: 612206
The project you are leading is supposed to upgrade the application developed by your company
on desktop computers and mobile devices. Last week, a major supplier of electronics
unexpectedly released a new mobile device. You realize that your application, with a little bit of
modification, can run much faster and more securely on the new device.
What should you do next in regards to this opportunity?
- **A Create a cost forecast and communicate it to stakeholders**
- **B Submit a change request to modify the application**
- **C Update project funding requirements in consideration for the unexpected work**
- **D Conduct variance analysis for an appropriate reserve amount**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Your application upgrade has the opportunity of running faster and with more security. You
should find out if your project resources can support it first.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

In this question, an unexpected opportunity presents itself. The modification of the application to
be upgraded on the new mobile device could have a significant impact on multiple project
constraints, including project scope, schedule, cost, quality, communications, risk, etc. Therefore,
a change request should be submitted and analyzed first before any decision is made. The change
request will have to go thru the organization's change control process established for the project.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Create a cost forecast and communicate it to stakeholders**
Incorrect. A cost forecast contains either a calculated EAC value or bottom-up EAC value
used to inform stakeholders of how much money the project is expected to spend once all
activities have finished. Although the project stakeholders should be made aware of how
much money is likely to be spent by the end of the project, a better answer would have been
first to make a decision of whether to allocate more funds to capture the opportunity or not.
If the funds were approved, a cost forecast may then have been issued to update project
stakeholders of the new EAC taken from the revised cost baseline. However, that answer
choice was not provided. Therefore, creating a forecast is not what you should do next.
- **B Submit a change request to modify the application**
Correct. The question describes an opportunity to modify the application to run faster and
more securely. Capturing this opportunity will likely affect multiple project constraints and
baselines, so a change request should first be submitted and reviewed to understand all of
its impacts. If approved, additional time and money to cover this unplanned work may be
added to the cost and schedule baselines. While an ideal answer would have been to first
conduct a reserve analysis to see how much of a management reserve is available or
needed, followed by a change request, this option is not provided, Therefore, of the choices
given, submitting a change request is the best answer to the question asked.
- **C Update project funding requirements in consideration for the unexpected work**
Incorrect. Project funding requirements are composed of the total funding requirements and
periodic funding requirements for the project. A controlled document, project funding
requirements are derived from the cost baseline and may include the sources of the funding.
Although eventually it will be necessary for the project manager to update the project
funding requirements in consideration for any funds needed to secure the opportunity, this
is not the 'next' step that should be taken. A better answer would have been to update the
project funding requirements only after a change request had been submitted and approved
to incorporate new funds into the cost baseline for the unexpected work, however, that
option was not listed.
- **D Conduct variance analysis for an appropriate reserve amount**
Incorrect. This answer choice mixes up 'variance analysis' with 'reserve analysis'. Reserve
analysis is used to determine if previously created reserves are still required or if additional
reserves should be added. Variance analysis, on the other hand, is the explanation (cause,
impact and corrective actions) for any cost (CV = EV - AC), schedule (SV = EV - PV) or
variance at completion (VAC = BAC - EAC) variances experienced on the project.
Although it is important for the project manager to track and monitor any variances
encountered on the project, conducting variance analysis is not the first step to be taken to

---

capture the opportunity presented. As such, this is not the best answer choice of those
provided.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 113-115

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 38 of 200
Question ID: 651306
- **A project has reached a critical point, and a decision must be made immediately to salvage the**
project from failure. The key project stakeholders are at the meeting that has been running for a
few hours, unable to agree on anything.
What should the project manager do?
- **A Schedule another meeting in a week from now**
- **B Find a solution that works for everybody**
- **C Call in the HR manager to calm everybody down**
- **D Select an option and make a decision**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the best course of action when there is limited time, the situation is an emergency, and a
decision must be made?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario surrounds the Manage Team process. Conflict management is an example of the
interpersonal and team skills tools and techniques that are associated with this process. Based on
the scenario, the situation looks like an emergency. Force/direct is a technique of pushing one's
viewpoint at the expense of others; offering only win-lose solutions, usually enforced through a
power position to resolve an emergency. The project manager should select one of the options
discussed and make a decision. Without a decision, the scenario implies the project would fail.
The decision the project manager would take does not guarantee success either, but not making a
decision at all will likely result in project failure.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Schedule another meeting in a week from now**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the decision must be made immediately to avoid
project failure. Waiting another week does not seem a plausible option.
- **B Find a solution that works for everybody**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents collaborate/problem solve conflict resolution
technique. However, from the question text, the stakeholders have been discussing the issue
for hours to no avail. It sounds as if there is no solution that works for everybody.
- **C Call in the HR manager to calm everybody down**
Incorrect. It is unlikely that the HR manager would be helpful in this situation. The problem
is not that everybody should be calmed down (which would not hurt). The problem is that
the project is in its critical point with a high risk of failure. The decision should be made to
salvage the project rather than to calm down the meeting participants.
- **D Select an option and make a decision**
Correct. Based on the scenario, the situation looks like an emergency. The project manager
should push her viewpoint at the expense of others. Otherwise, no decision would be made
and the project would fail. The decision the project manager would take does not guarantee
success either, but not making a decision at all will likely result in project failure.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 349

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 39 of 200
Question ID: 625047
Gold plating had been an issue with your current software development project. However, you
found that ever since instituting daily stand-up meetings, no more features or functionalities that
the customer did not request have been introduced into the project.
What is your best course of action to prevent gold plating for the remainder of the current project
and on future projects?
- **A Bring up the topic during the project retrospective**
- **B Capture the best practice in the lessons learned register**
- **C Gold plating adds customer value and should not be prevented**
- **D Ensure that the scope management plan includes daily stand-up meetings**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where is knowledge gained during a project recorded?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Daily standup meetings can be used by teams and stakeholders, often on agile projects, to share
and discuss achievements and issues of the previous day as well as plans for the current day's
work. The question suggests that you, as the project manager, have discovered that using daily
standup meetings is beneficial in controlling the project scope. This hybrid project management
practice, traditional scope control approach using agile methods, can be documented in the
lessons learned register, which is a project document used to record knowledge gained during a
project so that it can be used in the current project. At the end of the project or phase, the
information in the lessons learned register is transferred into the lessons learned repository as an
organizational process asset, where it can be used to improve the performance of future projects.
Therefore, of the available choices, capturing the best practice in the lessons learned register is

---

the best way to prevent gold plating for the remainder of the current project and on future
projects.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Bring up the topic during the project retrospective**
Incorrect. A project retrospective is a review scheduled at the end of a project to record
lessons learned in the lessons learned register. While bringing up any best practices during
a project retrospective is a good idea, there is no reason to wait until the end of the project
to capture the best practice in the lessons learned register. Best practices should be
captured in the lessons learned register at the time the knowledge is gained to ensure
performance can be improved for the remainder of the project and then transferred to the
lessons learned repository for use on future projects. Additionally, merely bringing up the
topic during the project retrospective does not guarantee the best practice would be
captured in the lessons learned register.
- **B Capture the best practice in the lessons learned register**
Correct. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge
gained during a project so that it can be used in the current project and entered into the
lessons learned repository, where it can be used to improve the performance of future
projects. Capturing the best practice in the lessons learned register is the best course of
action to prevent gold plating on future projects.
- **C Gold plating adds customer value and should not be prevented**
Incorrect. Gold plating refers to the practice of adding features or functionalities that the
customer did not request. Gold plating is considered a bad practice for project
management and should be avoided as it adds unnecessary risk to the project and
uncontrollably spends project resources.
- **D Ensure that the scope management plan includes daily stand-up meetings**
Incorrect. The scope management plan may or may not be updated to include daily
stand-up meetings as a strategy for controlling the project scope. However, this action is
effective in helping to control scope for the current project but is unlikely to prevent gold
plating on future projects as the scope management plan is specific to the current project.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 171, 364
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 40 of 200
Question ID: 613817
- **A project manager is planning a project to bring a new offshore oil rig online. The project team is**
having difficulty planning the project schedule since they are unsure about the depth and the
density of soil material that they would have to drill through to reach the oil.
Which of the following would be most useful in this situation?
- **A Make an educated guess at the time required for drilling**
- **B Seek advice from the project sponsor**
- **C Use parametric estimating as a method to determine how long it would take to complete**
the drilling process
- **D Check the assumption log to determine if assumptions have been made regarding the**
required drilling depth
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where should the project manager find information regarding factors in the planning process that
are considered to be true, real, or certain without proof or demonstration?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Estimate Activity Durations is underway, and the assumption log is
one of the inputs for this process. The assumption log is a project document used to record all
assumptions and constraints throughout the project life cycle. High-level assumptions are
identified in the business case and flow into the project charter. It is possible that the assumptions
regarding the depth of the oil and soil composition are contained in the business case and project
charter. However, those documents are not listed as possible answer choices. While there is no
guarantee that the relevant assumption exists in the assumption log either, of the available

---

choices, understanding the assumptions that have been made by checking the assumption log is
the best choice for what the project manager should do next.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Make an educated guess at the time required for drilling**
Incorrect. Making a guess is not a good practice in project management. It is a safe
assumption that the company would not invest the money of drilling an oil well if they had
not first made some assumptions regarding the depth of the oil and soil composition, and
the project manager needs to understand those assumptions before estimating the duration
of activities. Therefore, this choice can be eliminated as a correct answer.
- **B Seek advice from the project sponsor**
Incorrect. The assumptions made regarding drilling speed and depth may already be
available from the project documents. The project manager should review the project
information that is readily available before seeking advice from the project sponsor.
Therefore, seeking advice from the sponsor is not what the project manager should do next.
- **C Use parametric estimating as a method to determine how long it would take to complete**
the drilling process
Incorrect. Parametric estimating is an estimating technique in which an algorithm is used
to calculate cost or duration based on historical data and project parameters. There is
nothing in the question that suggests this type of data is available to assist in the
estimation.
- **D Check the assumption log to determine if assumptions have been made regarding the**
required drilling depth
Correct. The assumption log is a project document used to record all assumptions and
constraints throughout the project life cycle. While there is no guarantee that the relevant
assumption exists in the assumption log, among the available choices, understanding the
assumptions that have been made by checking the assumption log is the best choice for
what the project manager should do next.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 81, 198

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 41 of 200
Question ID: 625113
The following table is taken from the project's current performance report. The current cost
performance is expected to remain unchanged for the remainder of the project. The method used
to determine the earned value is based on percent complete.
Based on this information, what is the EAC for the project?
- **A $666,667**
- **B -$166,667**
- **C $550,000**
- **D $500,000**
Question answered incorrectly

---


**Hint:**

When the cost performance is expected to be unchanged for the remainder of the project, the
EAC can be calculated as BAC / CPI.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question is asking for the estimate at completion (EAC) based on the assumption that the
cost performance will not change for the remainder of the project. When the cost performance is
not expected to change, as in the scenario provided, the EAC can be calculated as the budget at
completion (BAC) divided by the cost performance index (CPI). The BAC is provided in the
chart as $500,000 which is the planned value for the project. The formula for CPI is earned value
(EV) divided by actual costs (AC). The EV is the sum of the planned work completed, which, in
this case, is 100% of activity 1, 100% of activity 2, and 50% of activity 3. AC is the sum of the
costs for each of the individual activities as presented by the chart. Note, since the scenario
mentions that the method used to determine the earned value is based on percent complete, the
earned value of a partially completed work package is calculated by multiplying the planned
value of the work package by its the percent complete.
The calculations are shown below:
EV = EV of activity 1 + EV of activity 2 + EV of activity 3 = (1 x $15,000) + (1 x $10,000) +
(0.50 x $250,000) = $150,000
AC = AC of activity 1 + AC of activity 2 + AC of activity 3 = $14,000 + $11,000 + $175,000 =
$200,000
CPI = EV / AC = $150,000 / $200,000 = 0.75
EAC = BAC / CPI = $500,000 / 0.75 = $666,667
Therefore, the estimate at completion (EAC) is $666,667.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A $666,667**
Correct. In order to derive the EAC, the following calculations must be made: EV = (1 x
$15,000) + (1 x $10,000) + (.50 x $250,000) = $150,000. AC is provided in the chart as
$200,000. CPI = EV / AC = $150,000 / $200,000 = 0.75. EAC = BAC / CPI = $500,000 /
.75 = $666,667.

---

- **B -$166,667**
Incorrect. The variance at completion (VAC) can be calculated as the budget at completion
(BAC) minus the estimate at completion (EAC) which is -$166,667. However, the question
is asking for the EAC and not the VAC.
- **C $550,000**
Incorrect. If the future work will be accomplished at the planned rate, the EAC formula is
EAC = AC + BAC - EV. If this formula is used, the EAC is $550,000. However, the question
indicates that the current cost performance should be used and not the planned rate.
- **D $500,000**
Incorrect. The budget at completion (BAC) is the total planned value of the project, which
is $500,000. However, the question is asking for the EAC and not the BAC.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 264-265, 267
Practice Standard for Earned Value Management - Second Edition, Project Management
Institute Inc., 2011, Page(s) 38-39
https://www.project-management-prepcast.com/pmp-formulas
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 42 of 200
Question ID: 612097
With the start of project execution, the project manager begins emailing stakeholders a weekly
project status report generated by an internal project management application. It turns out that
external stakeholders are unable to open the files because they do not have the required project
management software.
What may have prevented this problem from occurring?
- **A Excluding the external stakeholders from the stakeholder register**
- **B Updating the lessons learned register**
- **C Capturing a description of the problem in the issue log**
- **D Tailoring communication technology to the needs of all stakeholders**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

- **A proactive approach is necessary to prevent a problem from occurring.**
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project manager was performing the Monitor Stakeholder
Engagement process when it comes to light that external stakeholders are unable to open the
project status files since they do not have the required software. As it relates to stakeholder
management, the project manager should tailor the way the Project Stakeholder Management
processes are applied. Among these tailoring considerations is communication technology. While
it appears that all of the stakeholders have access to email, the external stakeholders lack the
required software to open the files that were generated by the project management software.
Considering the technology that was available to the external stakeholders, likely would have led
to the selection of a more appropriate file format for the project status updates. The incorrect
answer choices represent actions that are taken after the problem has been realized or are not

---

reasonable. Therefore, of the available choices, tailoring the communication technology to the
needs of all stakeholders is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Excluding the external stakeholders from the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. Excluding the external stakeholders from the stakeholder register is an extreme
action and not necessary to prevent the issue described by the question. Stakeholders can
be internal or external to the project and performing organization. Just because some
individuals or groups are external does not necessarily mean they are not stakeholders, and
that the engagement of these stakeholders does not need to be managed.
- **B Updating the lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register should be updated to capture the knowledge gained
regarding the appropriate file format for project updates. Updating the lessons learned
register is a reactive response and would not have prevented the problem from occurring in
the first place.
- **C Capturing a description of the problem in the issue log**
Incorrect. The problem described by the question should now be captured in the issue log
for follow up and resolution. However, capturing the information in the issue log is a
reactive measure and would not have prevented the problem from occurring.
- **D Tailoring communication technology to the needs of all stakeholders**
Correct. Considering the technology that was available to the external stakeholders, likely
would have led you, as the project manager, to select a more appropriate file format for the
project status updates.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 506

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 43 of 200
Question ID: 612385
- **A project manager is in the process of obtaining administrative closure of the project.**
Which of the following activities will not be performed as part of this process?
- **A Reassignment of personnel**
- **B Release of project resources**
- **C Acceptance of project deliverables**
- **D Archiving project information**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which activity is performed during the Validate Scope process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the project manager is performing the Close Project or Phase process
and asks for the activity which will 'not' be performed during this process. Deliverables that meet
the acceptance criteria are formally signed off and approved by the customer as part of the
Validate Scope process. Accepted deliverables are an output from the Validate Scope process and
an input to the Close Project or Phase process. Formal documentation received from the
customer acknowledging formal acceptance of the project's deliverables is then forwarded to the
Close Project or Phase process.
One may argue that Close Project or Phase is the process of obtaining the customer’s formal
acceptance of the project’s deliverables. According to the PMBOK® Guide, in the Close Project
or Phase process, the customer ‘confirms’ the delivery and formal acceptance of deliverables.
While they sound similar, those are two different things: actual acceptance of the deliverables
(which is done as part of the Validate Scope process) and the confirmation of the acceptance of
the deliverables (which is done as part of the Close Project or Phase process). Thus, of the

---

available choices, only acceptance of the project's deliverables is not performed during the
administrative closure of the project and is, therefore, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reassignment of personnel**
Incorrect. Reassignment of personnel does occur as part of the administrative closure of the
project.
- **B Release of project resources**
Incorrect. The administrative closure of the project includes the release of project
resources.
- **C Acceptance of project deliverables**
Correct. Deliverables that meet the acceptance criteria are formally signed off and
approved by the customer as part of the Validate Scope process rather than the Close
Project or Phase process.
- **D Archiving project information**
Incorrect. During project closure, project information is archived for future use by the
organization.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 121-125, 166
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 44 of 200
Question ID: 610001
An executive wants to begin initiating a project by developing a project charter, but since she has
never sponsored a project before, she is looking for a document to use as a template.
Where should the executive look first?
- **A Project business case**
- **B Enterprise environmental factors**
- **C Benefits management plan**
- **D Organizational process assets**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

If available, it is better to use an approved template.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

- **A project charter template is typically found in the organizational process assets. Even though**
templates can also be found on websites and commercial databases, which are considered
enterprise environmental factors, the first place to check is the organizational process assets to
see if an approved template is available.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project business case**

---

Incorrect. The business case is a documented economic feasibility study used to justify the
project, and it is used as an input into the Develop Project Charter process. However, the
business case is not a source for project templates.
- **B Enterprise environmental factors**
Incorrect. Templates for a project charter can be found on websites and in commercial
databases, which are considered enterprise environmental factors. However, this is not the
first place to check for a template. Although the company in the scenario does not typically
use a project charter, an approved template may still exist as an organizational process
asset.
- **C Benefits management plan**
Incorrect. The benefits management plan is the documented explanation defining the
processes for creating, maximizing, and sustaining the benefits provided by a project. The
benefits management plan is an input for the development of the project charter, but it does
not contain templates.
- **D Organizational process assets**
Correct. A project charter template is typically found in the organizational process assets,
and this is the first place to check and see if an approved template is already available.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 79
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 45 of 200
Question ID: 612993
You are leading a multiphase engineering project. All work planned for the current phase is now
complete.
What should you do before moving on to the next phase?
- **A Confirm objectives for the phase have been met**
- **B Share the work performance report with stakeholders**
- **C Collect historical information from previous projects**
- **D Measure the project's performance against baselines**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the answer choices describes an activity performed during the last process of a project
or phase?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies you begin the Close Project or Phase process for the current phase. Before
moving onto the next phase, you should ensure you have completed all closing activities so that
the phase is formally closed. During the Close Project or Phase process, the activities necessary
for the administrative closure of the phase are performed. You should conduct a review of the
project management plan to ensure all work planned for the current phase is completed and that
the phase has met its objectives. Of the available choices, only one, confirming objectives for the
phase have been met, describes an activity performed during the Close Project or Phase process,
making this choice the best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Confirm objectives for the phase have been met**
Correct. Before starting the next phase of a project, the current phase must be formally
closed which is accomplished during the Close Project or Phase process. One of the
activities of the Close Project or Phase process is verifying that the phase has satisfied its
requirements. Therefore, confirming the objectives for the current phase have been met is
what you should do before moving on to the next phase.
- **B Share the work performance report with stakeholders**
Incorrect. A final report is an output from the Close Project or Phase process. However, a
work performance report described by this answer choice is typically a representation of
work performance data collected throughout project execution and contextualized during
the Monitor and Control Project Work process. The scenario describes a project with one of
its phases moving into closure, suggesting any work performance reports issued would
have already been distributed.
- **C Collect historical information from previous projects**
Incorrect. Collecting historical information from previous projects is typically done during
the planning processes of a project, for example when developing the project management
plan. The scenario suggests the project is in the Close Project or Phase process, therefore
collecting historical information from previous projects would have already been completed
for the current phase and is too early to be started for the next one.
- **D Measure the project's performance against baselines**
Incorrect. Measuring the project's performance against the baselines is performed during
the Monitor and Control Project Work process to determine if any corrective or preventive
actions are indicated. As suggested by the scenario, your current phase is in its closure.
Any variances from the baselines should have already been determined and addressed.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 123

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 46 of 200
Question ID: 612135
On a project, several programmers were hired as independent consultants to supplement the
in-house programmers to ensure the timely completion of the project. Towards the end of the
project, the project manager has performed some analysis and determined that the CPI is 0.8 and
the SPI is 1.2.
What is the best course of action to bring project performance back into alignment with the
project management plan?
- **A Approve the use of overtime for the in-house programmers**
- **B Reduce or eliminate the independent contractors**
- **C Perform fast tracking to address the performance gap**
- **D Eliminate the non-essential features from the project scope**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the best way to address the cost variance?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The key to correctly answering this question lies in the interpretation of the cost performance
index (CPI) and schedule performance index (SPI). A CPI of 0.8 and an SPI of 1.2 indicates that
the project is over budget and ahead of schedule. Therefore, costs must be reduced to meet the
project budget. Reducing or eliminating the independent contractors, to the extent that the project
schedule allows without impacting the schedule baseline, will reduce costs to bring project
performance back into alignment with the project management plan, and that is the best course of
action given the circumstances provided by the question.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Approve the use of overtime for the in-house programmers**
Incorrect. A cost performance index (CPI) of 0.8 indicates that the project is already over
budget and approving overtime will increase costs which will increase the performance gap
rather than correct it.
- **B Reduce or eliminate the independent contractors**
Correct. A cost performance index (CPI) of 0.8 and a schedule performance index (SPI) of
1.2 indicates that the project is over budget and ahead of schedule. Reducing or eliminating
the independent contractors, assuming it is permitted by the contract, will reduce costs to
bring project performance back into alignment with the project management plan.
- **C Perform fast tracking to address the performance gap**
Incorrect. Fast tracking is a schedule compression technique, and the cost performance
index (CPI) of 0.8 is the variance that needs to be addressed. Fast tracking will not reduce
costs and may introduce additional risks for the project.
- **D Eliminate the non-essential features from the project scope**
Incorrect. Reducing the scope might reduce costs to address the performance gap indicated
by the cost performance index (CPI) of 0.8. However, the question is asking for the best
course of action to bring the project back into alignment with the project management plan,
and project scope is part of the project management plan. Therefore, of the available
choices, eliminating non-essential features is not the best answer to the question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 263
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 47 of 200
Question ID: 626003
At the strategy meeting in your organization, the meeting participants are arguing that a good
project management practice means that the knowledge, skills, and processes should always be
applied uniformly on all projects that the organization is about to undertake.
Which of the following is the most accurate regarding the question under debate?
- **A The knowledge, skills, and processes should always be applied uniformly on all projects**
- **B Only the iron triangle related processes should be applied for projects undertaken by an**
organization
- **C The processes used and the degree of rigor for each process should be appropriate for any**
given project
- **D Process analysis techniques, such as Lean or Kanban, should be used before applying any**
process to a project
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This is known as process tailoring.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Project managers and project teams should discuss each process and its inputs and outputs and
decide which processes are applicable to the project they are about to undertake. As stated in the
reference, "Project management processes apply globally and across industry groups. Good
practice means there is general agreement that the application of project management processes
has been shown to enhance the chances of success over a wide range of projects. Good practice
does not mean that the knowledge, skills, and processes should always be applied uniformly on
all projects. For any given project, the project manager, in collaboration with the project team, is

---

always responsible for determining which processes are appropriate, and the appropriate degree
of rigor for each process."

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The knowledge, skills, and processes should always be applied uniformly on all projects**
Incorrect. Answer choices with absolute statements such as 'always', 'never', 'only', etc. are
typically incorrect. The knowledge, skills, and processes should NOT always be applied
uniformly on all projects.
- **B Only the iron triangle related processes should be applied for projects undertaken by an**
organization
Incorrect. The 'iron triangle' (or the Project Management Triangle) is a model of scope,
budget, and schedule constraints. Scope, budget, and schedule processes are NOT the only
processes that should be applied and/or tailored while planning projects. Answer choices
with absolute statements such as 'always', 'never', 'only', etc. are typically incorrect.
- **C The processes used and the degree of rigor for each process should be appropriate for any**
given project
Correct. Good practice does not mean that the knowledge, skills, and processes should
always be applied uniformly on all projects. The processes should be tailored to any given
project.
- **D Process analysis techniques, such as Lean or Kanban, should be used before applying any**
process to a project
Incorrect. Process analysis techniques, such as Lean or Kanban, are among the knowledge
and skills of Domain IV, Monitoring and Controlling, in the PMP Examination Content
Outline. They are not related to the topic of the question, project management processes
tailoring, and are added as a distractor.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 28
