PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 48 of 200
Question ID: 612751
Due to organizational policy, all project messages use a common subject line to differentiate
them from other projects in the organization. The project manager has been using this
communication method to request scope validation sign-offs from key stakeholders. However,
the project has suffered delays due to missing sign-offs.
What should the project manager do to keep this issue from continuing?
- **A Escalate the issue to the stakeholders' managers and ask that more responsive staff be**
assigned to your project.
- **B Formally deliver sign-off requests for scope validation in a weekly event for product**
demonstration and follow up personally with any absent stakeholders.
- **C Instead of a common subject line, make the call to action clear, such as "your sign-off**
requested" to differentiate feedback requests from reports that do not require action.
- **D Schedule a series of automated reminder messages after each sign-off request using**
several communication methods (email, instant message, text, internet dashboard).
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager's most important messages are getting lost. The project manager needs to
raise the profile of the work of the project team.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies the Manage Communications process is underway. Communication skills,
such as presentations, are among the tools and techniques used as part of this process. Clear and
effective presentations of project deliverables to relevant stakeholders can help raise the profile
of the project and the team. Since sign-offs are missing, it appears important requests of scope
validation are getting lost, or perhaps being ignored. The project manager can use presentations
(product demonstration) as a formal platform to engage stakeholders and have them to sign-off

---

the project deliverables. This may help the project manager prevent the issue of missing sign-offs
from continuing.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Escalate the issue to the stakeholders' managers and ask that more responsive staff be**
assigned to your project.
Incorrect. Escalating the issue to the stakeholders' managers without talking to the
stakeholders first is a premature action. Additionally, this may hurt your reputation as a
project manager.
- **B Formally deliver sign-off requests for scope validation in a weekly event for product**
demonstration and follow up personally with any absent stakeholders.
Correct. Scope validation sign-off is critical to project success and deserves a regular event
that the requisite stakeholders make a point of attending (either in person or virtually). The
event provides a forum for inspection, validates that your team has produced quality
deliverables, gives your team an opportunity to be clear on any required corrections, and
allows the relevant stakeholders to sign off on the scope that has been demonstrated.
- **C Instead of a common subject line, make the call to action clear, such as "your sign-off**
requested" to differentiate feedback requests from reports that do not require action.
Incorrect. While it may be helpful to improve basic communication competency and
convention, relying solely on the email channel for something as important as scope
validation sign-off is not the most effective communication plan. Think of how many
messages your stakeholders receive every day. Additionally, according to the scenario
described, using a common subject line is the organizational policy. Changing the policy
cannot be done at will. Therefore, this choice is not the best answer to the question asked.
- **D Schedule a series of automated reminder messages after each sign-off request using**
several communication methods (email, instant message, text, internet dashboard).
Incorrect. Inundating the stakeholders with sign-off reminders would waste time, probably
risk making the stakeholders dislike the project manager, and, most importantly, would miss
the goal of getting the sign-offs.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 384
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 49 of 200
Question ID: 626040
While reviewing the project performance, the project manager determines that a deviation from
one of the project baselines has occurred. If not fixed promptly, the deviation may significantly
impact the project. The project manager considers applying either corrective actions or a
combination of corrective and preventive actions to address the deviation.
In considering how to address the deviations, what technique is the project manager using in this
scenario?
- **A Alternatives analysis**
- **B Earned value analysis**
- **C Risk analysis**
- **D Variance analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

One of these options is specific to determining how to address the deviation once it occurred.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

In the scenario provided, the project manager reviews the project performance. Reviewing
project performance is one of the activities carried out during the Monitor and Control Project
Work process. Data analysis techniques can be used in the Monitor and Control Project Work
process to determine the appropriate action to take when a deviation has occurred. While some
choices help to determine if a specific action should be taken, only alternatives analysis is used
to determine whether corrective actions or a combination of corrective and preventive actions
should be implemented when a deviation occurs. Therefore, alternatives analysis is the best
answer among the choices given.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Alternatives analysis**
Correct. Alternatives analysis is a data analysis technique used to consider and select the
corrective actions or a combination of corrective and preventive actions to implement when
a deviation occurs. In the scenario described, the project manager considers applying
either corrective actions or a combination of corrective and preventive actions to address
the deviation. Therefore, this choice is the best answer to the question asked.
- **B Earned value analysis**
Incorrect. Earned value analysis is a data analysis technique that provides an integrated
perspective on scope, schedule, and cost performance. Earned value analysis is not used to
select corrective actions or a combination of corrective and preventive actions to
implement when a deviation occurs.
- **C Risk analysis**
Incorrect. Risk analysis is a general term used to cover both the Perform Qualitative Risk
Analysis and Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis processes. Risk analysis is used to
determine prioritization and actions required to address identified project risks and not to
determine whether corrective actions or a combination of corrective and preventive actions
need to be implemented when a deviation from a performance baseline occurs. And, on its
own, risk analysis is not a technique associated with the PMBOK® Guide.
- **D Variance analysis**
Incorrect. Variance analysis is a data analysis technique that reviews the differences
between planned and actual performance to determine if a variance has occurred. Variance
analysis is not used to select the corrective actions or a combination of corrective and
preventive actions to implement when a deviation occurs. Further analysis can be
performed to determine whether any corrective or preventive actions needed. However,
such analysis is not the main goal of variance analysis. Alternatives analysis is required to
consider and select the corrective actions or a combination of corrective and preventive
actions to implement when a deviation occurs.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 111

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 50 of 200
Question ID: 612499
- **A project manager is in the process of developing a plan for how risk management activities will**
be structured and performed for a bridge construction project. As part of this process, the chart
below was developed and included as an element of the plan. As the project manager presents
the plan to a group of stakeholders, a stakeholder questions the benefit of using the chart.
How might the project manager respond?

---

- **A It will provide us with a summary of information on individual project risks and the level**
of overall project risk
- **B The chart will provide us with the probability of occurrence of each risk and its impact on**
project objectives if that risk occurs
- **C We will use the chart as a source of information on identified risks, potential risk owners,**
and potential risk responses

---

- **D It will help us consider the full range of sources from which individual risks may arise**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The chart provided by the question is an example of a risk breakdown structure (RBS).
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the risk management plan is being prepared as part of the Plan Risk
Management Process. The chart from the question is an example of a risk breakdown structure
(RBS), which is a hierarchical representation of potential sources of risks. An RBS helps the
project team consider the full range of sources from which individual risks that may arise. The
RBS can be useful when identifying risks or when categorizing identified risks. Therefore,
among the available choices, the most appropriate response to the stakeholder's question is that
the chart will help the project team consider the full range of sources from which individual risks
may arise.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A It will provide us with a summary of information on individual project risks and the level**
of overall project risk
Incorrect. The chart provided in the question is an example of a risk breakdown structure
(RBS). The risk report, rather than the RBS, is a project document developed progressively
throughout the Project Risk Management processes, which summarizes information on
individual project risks and the level of the overall project risk.
- **B The chart will provide us with the probability of occurrence of each risk and its impact on**
project objectives if that risk occurs
Incorrect. The probability and impact matrix is a grid for mapping the probability of
occurrence of each risk and its impact on project objectives if that risk occurs. Whereas, the
chart provided by the question is an example of the resource breakdown structure (RBS)
and not a probability and impact matrix.
- **C We will use the chart as a source of information on identified risks, potential risk owners,**
and potential risk responses

---

Incorrect. The risk register includes a list of identified risks, potential risk owners, and
potential risk responses. The chart provided in this scenario does not include risk owners
or risk responses.
- **D It will help us consider the full range of sources from which individual risks may arise**
Correct. The chart from the question is an example of a risk breakdown structure (RBS),
which is a hierarchical representation of potential sources of risks. An RBS helps the
project team consider the full range of sources from which individual risks may arise,
making this choice the best answer to the question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 405-406

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 51 of 200
Question ID: 612815
- **A project manager is getting very frustrated that the pace of gathering answers from stakeholders**
is slowing the project. Every two weeks about fifty stakeholders get together on the phone, and a
series of questions are reviewed. The stakeholders do not seem to be focused on the issues. The
stakeholders unanimously reject the idea of more meetings.
What is the best course of action?
- **A Conduct brainstorming meetings**
- **B Set up meetings with focus groups**
- **C Use surveys and reduce the meetings**
- **D Switch the meetings to interviews**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

One option reduces the time and keeps people focused.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Questionnaires and surveys are written sets of questions designed to accumulate information
from a large number of respondents quickly. When you limit options within a survey or
questionnaire, it can help the stakeholders to focus. This method is also one of the quickest ways
to reach these many stakeholders in a short amount of time. Also, by using negotiation skills, the
project manager can gain commitment from the stakeholders to complete the survey in a timely
manner in exchange for reducing the number of meetings. Therefore, of the available options, the
best course of action for the project manager is to negotiate for the use of surveys and reduce the
meetings.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Conduct brainstorming meetings**
Incorrect. Brainstorming sessions would be beneficial in generating more options.
However, in this scenario, the project manager should focus the stakeholders and facilitate
decisions. Brainstorming would unlikely encourage convergence among the stakeholders.
- **B Set up meetings with focus groups**
Incorrect. Focus groups bring together prequalified stakeholders and subject matter
experts to learn about their expectations and attitudes about a proposed product, service,
or result. While focus groups may or may not be helpful in this situation, the question states
that the stakeholders have rejected the idea of setting up additional meetings.
- **C Use surveys and reduce the meetings**
Correct. By sending out surveys or questionnaires that are short and focused, and do not
require coordinating so many people’s schedule, answers may come more quickly, and the
stakeholders can reply when they can focus.
- **D Switch the meetings to interviews**
Incorrect. Interviews might be effective in enhancing focus, but this is not a practical
solution in this situation. Conducting interviews with fifty stakeholders would be very
difficult and excessively time-consuming. The project manager needs to find a more
efficient and effective method of soliciting feedback from the stakeholders.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 142-143, 527

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 52 of 200
Question ID: 613044
With your project nearly complete, you are performing the tasks associated with project closure.
This project was particularly challenging for you and your project team, and you want to ensure
that the key learnings are preserved for use in future projects.
What activity are you least likely to perform in this scenario?
- **A Create the lessons learned register**
- **B Update the organizational process assets**
- **C Lead a project retrospective**
- **D Facilitate a lessons learned meeting**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The question is asking for the activity that is 'least' likely to be performed as part of the Close
Project or Phase process, and one of the answer choices represents an activity conducted as part
of the Manage Project Knowledge process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Close Project or Phase process is being conducted. Activities
performed during project closure related to preserving key learnings may include gathering
lessons learned, finalizing the lessons learned register, and transferring the information in the
lessons learned register to the lessons learned repository. In this manner, the knowledge gained
from the project will be preserved and made available for use in future projects. Keep in mind
that the question is asking for the activity that is 'least' likely to be performed as part of the Close
Project or Phase process. The lessons learned register is created as an output of the Manage
Project Knowledge process early in the project. Therefore, of the available options, creating the
lessons learned register is the activity that is 'least' likely to be conducted in this scenario.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Create the lessons learned register**
Correct. While the lessons learned register is updated as part of the Close Project or Phase
process implied by the scenario, the lessons learned register is created as an output of the
Manage Project Knowledge process early in the project.
- **B Update the organizational process assets**
Incorrect. The lessons learned repository is an organizational process asset that serves as a
store of historical information about lessons learned from projects. Updating the
organizational process assets, which includes the lessons learned repository, will preserve
the knowledge gained from the project for use in future projects.
- **C Lead a project retrospective**
Incorrect. A project retrospective is a scheduled review held at the end of a project to
record lessons learned. The lessons learned can then be included in the organizational
process assets for use in future projects.
- **D Facilitate a lessons learned meeting**
Incorrect. A lessons learned meeting might be held during the Close Project or Phase
process to gather lessons learned from the project, finalize the lessons learned register, and
transfer the information to the lessons learned repository for use in future projects.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 104, 127-128

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 53 of 200
Question ID: 625217
Looking at your network diagram, resource calendars, and the risk register, you learn that one of
your resources on one non-critical path is scheduled to undergo minor surgery and will be out for
seven days. Another resource has a planned vacation for five days, and another one is presenting
at a conference for three days, and their assigned activities affect the critical path.
To proactively protect your milestones, what can you add to your project schedule using the
critical chain method?
- **A Both divergence and convergence**
- **B Both early start and late start**
- **C Both project buffers and feeding buffers**
- **D Both total float and free float**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The critical chain method builds on the critical path method to protect milestones from slippage
and uses elements with durations that have safety margins either before the target project finish
date or before the end of a non-critical chain.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The critical chain method builds on the critical path method to protect milestones from slippage
and uses elements with durations that have safety margins either before the target project finish
date (project buffers) or before the end of a non-critical chain (feeding buffers). While the topic
of this question is not included in the PMBOK® Guide, the Project Management Professional
(PMP)® Examination Content Outline, June 2015, covers knowledge and skills, such as
scheduling tools and techniques, with which PMP aspirants are expected to be familiar.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Both divergence and convergence**
Incorrect. When creating the network diagram, ‘divergence’ describes when one activity
has two or more successors and splits into different paths. ‘Convergence’ describes when
an activity requires two or more predecessor activities on different paths to be done before
commencing.
- **B Both early start and late start**
Incorrect. The critical path method is used to calculate the amount of scheduling flexibility
on the logical network paths of the schedule model. ‘Early start’ is determined during a
forward pass, and ‘late start’ is determined on a backward pass.
- **C Both project buffers and feeding buffers**
Correct. To protect milestones from slippage, the critical chain method builds on the
critical path method, and uses buffers, which are elements with durations that have safety
margins. Place a ‘project buffer’ before the target project finish date. Place ‘feeding
buffers’ before the end of a non-critical chain where it feeds into the critical chain. In this
example, you might add seven days feeding buffer after the activity assigned to the resource
undergoing surgery, and five days project buffer to account for the other planned absences.
- **D Both total float and free float**
Incorrect. To determine schedule flexibility amidst logical dependencies and schedule
constraints, you use the critical path method. ‘Total float’ is the amount of time an activity
can be delayed or extended from its early start date without delaying the project finish date
or violating a schedule constraint. ‘Free float’ is the amount of time that an activity can be
delayed without delaying the early start date of any successor or violating a schedule
constraint.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 210-212, The Practice Standard for Scheduling
– Second Edition, Project Management Institute Inc., 2011, Page(s) 12

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 54 of 200
Question ID: 651313
- **A team member is working on a project activity where the outcome did not go as planned, but**
this outcome was expected as a possibility.
Which of the following should the team member consult to know what to do next?
- **A Schedule diagram**
- **B Business case**
- **C Risk response plan**
- **D Project schedule**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How do you deal with the known unknowns?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Risk management deals with the uncertainties of the project. In this circumstance, there were
uncertain results expected for a project activity. The schedule reflects the expected outcomes and
results. The unexpected results are managed as a risk. The risk response plans are made to order
to best address and respond to the identified risk, if realized, which happened in this example.
The team member should refer to the risk response plan to know what to do next.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Schedule diagram**

---

Incorrect. In this scenario, the activity and outcome did not go as planned. The schedule
diagram is built based on planned outcomes. The schedule diagram does not communicate
what to do next.
- **B Business case**
Incorrect. The business case may be a good reference, but it is generally too high level to
be of assistance as to how the team member should respond to the unexpected result.
- **C Risk response plan**
Correct. The risk response plan is made for dealing with the known unknowns of the
project. There was a possibility of uncertain results in this project activity. The project team
prepared for such possibilities and how to respond. Those responses were captured in the
risk response plans. The team member should reference those plans to respond accordingly.
- **D Project schedule**
Incorrect. The activity and outcome did not go as planned. A project schedule is built based
on planned outcomes. The project schedule does not provide information on what to do next
when something goes wrong.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 449-450
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 55 of 200
Question ID: 614003
The following table contains information about activities and their durations (in days) and
predecessors on a project schedule. Following an approved change request, you have increased
the duration of activity C from 1 to 5 and decreased the duration of activity D from 5 to 2. You
have adjusted the baselines accordingly.
What would be the most likely result of your actions?
- **A The duration of the project will not change.**

---

- **B The project risk will increase.**
- **C The quality of the deliverables will degrade.**
- **D Customer satisfaction will improve.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Use the critical path method (CPM) to determine the length of each path before and after the
changes and analyze the resulting effect.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The first step to correctly answer this question is to determine the length of each path on the
project. This requires the creation of a project schedule network diagram where you map the
values from the data table included in the question. The project schedule network diagram for
this scenario is shown below.

---

For each path, you add up the original durations. The path with the longest duration is the critical
path. In this case, the critical path is Start-D-E-F-G-End with a duration of 17, as shown below.
You must now add 4 to the duration of activity C, subtract 3 from the duration of activity D, and
determine the resulting effect. Following are the updated paths and their adjusted durations.
By making these changes, the duration of the project decreased from 17 Days to 14 Days, but as
a result, the project now has two critical paths. Having more than one critical path means more
activities that have no slack. Any delay in any of the activities on a critical path puts the entire
project at risk of missing the target deadline. Additionally, more activities with no slack must be
watched closely, which creates more effort for the project manager to control bringing them all in
on time. Therefore, it can be reasonably assumed that the project risk will increase, making this

---

choice the best answer to the question asked. Nothing can be concluded regarding the quality of
the deliverables or customer satisfaction.
One may argue that the increased risk of having two critical paths instead of one can be
compensated by the schedule buffer created as a result of the decreased project duration, thus
keeping the overall project risk lower than it could have been if the project duration stayed
unchanged while an additional critical path was added. However, according to the scenario
provided, the baselines have been adjusted, implying the new finish date of the project is set in
accordance with the new critical path. Therefore, of the choices provided, with the new project
duration of 14 instead of 17 and two critical paths, the only conclusion that can be made in this
case is that the project risk would likely increase.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The duration of the project will not change.**
Incorrect. Activity D is part of the critical path. Decreasing the duration of any activity on
the critical path would shorten the duration of the project. An increase of the duration of
activity C would not result in the increase of the project duration since after the change, the
duration of the path to which activity C belongs is still shorter than the original duration of
the project.
- **B The project risk will increase.**
Correct. Once you determine the original duration of each project schedule network path
and calculate the adjusted path durations, you have two critical paths with no float or
slack. Delay on any activity along any critical path puts the entire project in jeopardy of
missing the target deadline, thus increasing the project risk in comparison to the level of
risk the project had with only one critical path.
- **C The quality of the deliverables will degrade.**
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine whether the quality
of the deliverables will degrade. Changing the duration of activities does not necessarily
affect the quality of the deliverables.
- **D Customer satisfaction will improve.**
Incorrect. One may argue that by shortening the overall project duration, the customer
satisfaction will improve. However, if the customer did not ask for the project to be
completed earlier or if the customer is not prepared to accept the project earlier, it is
unlikely to expect from the customer to be more satisfied. The nature of the change request

---

is unknown, and there is not enough information in the question to make any determination
regarding customer satisfaction.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 210-211
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 56 of 200
Question ID: 612266
- **A project is contracted to translate issues of a popular magazine into three languages. After the**
content of the first issue was translated into one language, the client asks that a survey is sent to
magazine subscribers in their respective language to gauge the quality and clarity of the
translation of each issue. The survey has resulted in multiple change requests. The changes have
been approved.
During which process will these changes be implemented?
- **A The Manage Stakeholder Engagement process**
- **B The Direct and Manage Project Work process**
- **C The Control Quality process**
- **D The Monitor Communications process**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In which process are approved change requests implemented?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario covers quite a few project activities that are part of the processes represented by all
answer choices. However, the question is specific to one process where the approved change
requests are implemented. Direct and Manage Project Work is the process of leading and
performing the work defined in the project management plan and implementing approved
changes to achieve the project's objectives.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A The Manage Stakeholder Engagement process**
Incorrect. Manage Stakeholder Engagement is the process of communicating and working
with stakeholders to meet their needs and expectations, address issues, and foster
appropriate stakeholder involvement. Manage Stakeholder Engagement does not involve
the implementation of the approved change requests.
- **B The Direct and Manage Project Work process**
Correct. The Direct and Manage Project Work process is part of the Project Integration
Management knowledge area and the Executing process group, where approved change
requests are implemented.
- **C The Control Quality process**
Incorrect. Control Quality is the process of monitoring and recording results of executing
the quality management activities to assess performance and ensure the project outputs are
complete, correct, and meet customer expectations. Approved change requests are inputs to
this process, but for the purpose of verifying that changes have been implemented properly.
Implementing the approved change requests is not part of this process.
- **D The Monitor Communications process**
Incorrect. Monitor Communications is the process of ensuring that the information needs of
the project and its stakeholders are met. The process may require methods, including
customer satisfaction surveys, team member observations, issue log analysis, or reviewing
the stakeholder engagement assessment matrix. Although the scenario involves such a
survey, the question is specific to implementing approved changes.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 93, 114

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 57 of 200
Question ID: 651303
Per organizational policy, any commodities purchased for a project must be either the least cost
option available or a sole source.
Which project process and tool and technique does this most impact?
- **A Source selection in Plan Procurement**
- **B Data representation in Identify Stakeholders**
- **C Pre-assignment in Acquire Resources**
- **D Accepted deliverables in Validate Scope**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Is what is being purchased from within or from outside the performing project organization?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

When planning the procurement needs of the project and how to manage those needs,
understanding the organization’s policies and procedures frames what one can and cannot do or
what one is encouraged to follow. In this circumstance, the organization has placed some
requirements on the commodities (which are common, standard items) purchased by projects.
Consequently, when planning the management of the project procurement, this information
shapes the source selection options and its analysis because certain items can only be sourced
from certain suppliers (sellers).
Note, the full name of the process is Plan Procurement Management. While the correct answer
provides only a partial name of the process, 'Plan Procurement', of the choices provided, 'Source
selection in Plan Procurement' is the best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Source selection in Plan Procurement**
Correct. When the project manager and team – say the procurement manager – are
analyzing the procurement needs of the project and determining source selection, the
inclusion of such factors as least cost and sole source are extremely important in preparing
the procurement plans.
- **B Data representation in Identify Stakeholders**
Incorrect. Stakeholders are not commodities. Those who supply commodities to the project
may be considered stakeholders to the project, but the criteria listed is focusing more on the
selection of those procurement needs rather than the analyzing of the stakeholders.
- **C Pre-assignment in Acquire Resources**
Incorrect. Resources may be acquired for the project from outside sellers, but
pre-assignment is not about those resources procured by the project. Pre-assignment is
where resources provided to the project with little or no influence from the project team.
- **D Accepted deliverables in Validate Scope**
Incorrect. In the process of Validate Scope, the stakeholders are verifying and accepting the
deliverables, not analyzing the sources of the materials and whether they should or should
not be purchased from various sources like the least cost supplier or the sole source of the
material.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 473 - 474

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 58 of 200
Question ID: 610052
- **A client completed a walkthrough of the deliverables and formally accepted the work. The next**
day, the project manager returns to the project site to pick up company equipment and make
arrangements for final payment.
What should the project manager do when meeting the client as part of project closure?
- **A Confirm the final acceptance of the deliverable**
- **B Settle procurement claims**
- **C Validate the scope objectives have been met**
- **D Ensure quality assurance was performed**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What process group are you in?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies the project is in the Close Project or Phase process. It is important to
distinguish the difference between formal acceptance of project deliverables in the Validate
Scope process versus 'confirming' formal acceptance in the Close Project or Phase process.
When closing a project, it is necessary to confirm the acceptance of all project deliverables in
order to adequately complete and close the project. By doing this, the project manager is
essentially 'confirming' the delivery and formal acceptance of deliverables by the client.
Sometimes, this can be viewed as ticking a checkbox in the checklist of the activities carried out
during project closure. It is like asking a question, "Have the deliverables been accepted earlier
in the project as part of the Validate Scope process?". If the answer is "Yes", check the box. This
would eventually confirm that the deliverables have already been accepted.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Confirm the final acceptance of the deliverable**
Correct. Based on the scenario described, the project manager is carrying out the Close
Project or Phase process. Although the customer or sponsor formally accepts the
completed project deliverables in the Validate Scope process, in the Close Project or Phase
process, you must 'confirm' final acceptance of the project deliverables.
- **B Settle procurement claims**
Incorrect. When a PMP exam question refers to procurements, it does this from the
perspective of a buyer. In this scenario, the buyer is the client, and you are the seller.
Therefore, settling procurement claims is not applicable in this scenario. Theoretically, if
the project manager, as a seller, subcontracted part of the work to a vendor, then the project
manager would have to settle procurement claims as specified in the contract with the
vendor. However, there is not enough information in the question to determine whether or
not contracts with vendors have been used on in the project. Even if the question referred to
the procurement claims between the seller and the client as a buyer, these claims would
have been settled using the claims administration technique as part of the Control
Procurements process, which should have been completed before project closure. Based on
all the above considerations, settling procurement claims is not the best answer to the
question asked.
- **C Validate the scope objectives have been met**
Incorrect. The Validate Scope process is the process of formalizing acceptance of the
completed project deliverables. This answer choice is incorrect for a couple of reasons.
First, the scenario states that the client has already formally accepted the work. Secondly,
the Validate Scope process is part of the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group and
not part of project closure as implied by the scenario.
- **D Ensure quality assurance was performed**
Incorrect. Quality assurance is done as part of the Manage Quality process to examine and
correct the process itself. Quality assurance would have been performed before the Close
Project or Phase process has begun, and therefore is an incorrect answer.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 123, 164
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 59 of 200
Question ID: 613192
During project execution, a change request is submitted to include a new set of high-priority
requirements to the product. The change requires an increase in the project scope and budget.
The change request is approved, and the project manager updates the document that will be used
in the Control Scope process to detect any deviation in the agreed-upon scope.
Which of the following documents did the project manager update?
- **A Requirements documentation**
- **B Requirements traceability matrix**
- **C Scope management plan**
- **D Configuration management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Look for the answer choice that describes a document used to 'detect' any deviation in the
agreed-upon scope as opposed to a document that is used to determine the 'impact' of any change
or deviation from the scope baseline.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question describes a situation where new high-priority requirements are being added to the
project's scope. The addition of these requirements necessitates updates to the requirements
documentation and the requirements traceability matrix. The requirements documentation is a
description of how individual requirements meet the business need for the project. The
requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links product requirements from their origin to the
deliverables that satisfy them. Although both the requirements documentation and the
requirements traceability matrix are inputs to the Control Scope process, the requirements
documentation is used to 'detect' any deviation to the agreed-upon scope; whereas, the
requirements traceability matrix helps to determine the 'impact' of any change or deviation from

---

the scope baseline. As it pertains to the Control Scope process, a deviation from the project scope
must first be identified before the impact of the deviation can be assessed. Therefore, of the
available options, updating the requirements documentation is what should be done first.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Requirements documentation**
Correct. The requirements documentation is a description of how individual requirements
meet the business need for the project. The requirements documentation is used as an input
to the Control Scope process to detect any deviation in the agreed-upon scope.
- **B Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. The requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links the product requirements
from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them. The requirements traceability matrix,
which is an input to the Control Scope process, should be updated to reflect the new
product features. However, as it pertains to the Control Scope process, a deviation from the
project scope must first be identified before the impact of the deviation can be assessed. The
requirements documentation is used first to 'detect' any deviation in the agreed-upon scope.
The requirements traceability matrix is later used to determine potential 'impact' of the
change or deviation from the scope baseline.
- **C Scope management plan**
Incorrect. The scope management plan details how the scope is defined, developed,
monitored, controlled, and validated. This plan does not describe what the scope is. It is
unlikely that the scope management plan would need to be updated as a result of the
situation described in the scenario. Additionally, the question is asking about a project
document, while this answer choice represents a component of the project management
plan.
- **D Configuration management plan**
Incorrect. The configuration management plan describes how to identify and account for
project artifacts under configuration control, and how to record and report changes to
them. No information presented in the question suggests that changes are required to
project artifacts under configuration control. Additionally, the question is asking about a
project document, while this answer choice represents a component of the project
management plan.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 169, 147-148
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5

Question 60 of 200
Question ID: 612534
In a matrix organization, a project manager requests that a department manager allow one of the
departmental staff members to contribute to the project. The project manager proposes a plan on
how to best schedule and share the resource for the duration of the project.
What technique is the project manager using?
- **A Resource calendar**
- **B Negotiation**
- **C Decision making**
- **D Pre-assignment**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is one of the interpersonal or team skills used in the Acquire Resources
process.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question describes a discussion or negotiation between a project manager and a department
manager for a shared resource. The project manager is hoping to acquire the resource as part of
his project team. If successful the project manager will reach an agreement with the department
manager that will allow the use of one of the departmental resources to contribute work to the
project.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Resource calendar**
Incorrect. Although the discussion between the project manager and the department
manager involves scheduling and sharing a resource, there is no mention in the question of
the specific information such as working days, shifts, business hours, resource availability,
or other information typically contained in a resource calendar.
- **B Negotiation**
Correct. This question shows the project manager contacting the department manager to
request a resource to use on the project. The project manager proposes a schedule that
would allow the resource to be shared between her department and the project. This is a
negotiation between the project manager and the department manager. Negotiation is
aimed at reaching an agreement and is an interpersonal and team skill used as a technique
of the Acquire Resources process.
- **C Decision making**
Incorrect. Decision making techniques such as multicriteria decision analysis involve using
a selection criteria for rating or scoring potential resources. In this scenario, the project
manager is seeking to acquire an identified resource from the department manager’s team
and there is no indication that their discussion involves rating or scoring of the resource.
- **D Pre-assignment**
Incorrect. Pre-assignment occurs when team members are selected in advance, typically
based on the expertise of a particular person. The information in the question does not
indicate that this resource has been pre-assigned or possesses a particular skill or type of
expertise.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 332

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 61 of 200
Question ID: 651320
You are considering using Unique Foods for a catering work package in your project. Unique
Foods has begun ordering food based on informal discussions with you. They are requesting
funds to order the rest of the supplies and begin work.
What is your next best response?
- **A Request Unique Foods to wait until procurement documents are prepared**
- **B Schedule a meeting and go over procurement deliverables and timing**
- **C Assess the Unique Food Inc. requirements and develop a project scope statement**
- **D Start payments so resources can be procured**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the agreement between you and the seller?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question states that you are considering a vendor to deliver some of the work packages for
your project, implying you are in the Conduct Procurements process. Agreements (or
procurement agreements) are an output from this process. Based on the scenario described, so far
only informal discussions between your organization and one of the prospective sellers, Unique
Foods, took place. Without any formalized procurement agreement between your project and the
seller, there is no requirement for supplying funds or resources to the potential seller. Project
managers are responsible for managing the costs of the project. Handing over funds to an outside
party based on the prospect of procuring materials or resources from them is the unwise
management of the project funds.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Request Unique Foods to wait until procurement documents are prepared**
Correct. Verbal notification or acknowledgment without proper procurement
documentation is not sufficient for a potential seller to proceed or produce materials.
- **B Schedule a meeting and go over procurement deliverables and timing**
Incorrect. Until there are formal agreements in place, it may be too premature to meet for
scheduling and logistics.
- **C Assess the Unique Food Inc. requirements and develop a project scope statement**
Incorrect. The project scope statement is the description of the project scope, major
deliverables, assumptions, and constraints. This document is developed by the performing
organization to satisfy the requirements of the customer. However, in the scenario
described, Unique Foods is your seller, not your customer. Therefore, if they are selected,
your organization has to provide them with the procurement documents and a procurement
statement of work, not with the project scope statement.
- **D Start payments so resources can be procured**
Incorrect. There are procurement agreements between you and the seller. There are
currently discussions to come to an agreement, but nothing is established at this point.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 460-462

Question 62 of 200
Question ID: 610017
- **A project manager has reviewed the lessons learned from past projects as well as the project**
charter to gain a high-level understanding of project goals and constraints.
Which data gathering technique is best for the project manager to use to develop the project
management plan?
- **A Mind mapping to consolidate ideas created through individual brainstorming sessions into**
a single map
- **B Feedback to support interactive communication between the project manager, team and all**
other project stakeholders
- **C Brainstorming to gather ideas and solutions about the project approach**
- **D Conflict management to bring diverse stakeholders into alignment on all aspects of the**
project management plan
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the available choices is a data gathering technique?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Brainstorming is a data gathering technique that is frequently used when developing the project
management plan to gather ideas and solutions on the project approach. The question is asking
for a data gathering technique, and of the available choices, only brainstorming is a data
gathering technique.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Mind mapping to consolidate ideas created through individual brainstorming sessions into**
a single map
Incorrect. Mind-mapping is a technique used to consolidate ideas created through
individual brainstorming sessions into a single map to reflect commonality and differences
in understanding and to generate new ideas. Mind mapping is a data representation
technique and not a data gathering technique as asked by the question.
- **B Feedback to support interactive communication between the project manager, team and all**
other project stakeholders
Incorrect. Feedback is information about reactions to communications, a deliverable, or a
situation. Feedback supports interactive communication between the project manager, team
and all other project stakeholders. However, feedback is a communication technique and
not a data gathering technique.
- **C Brainstorming to gather ideas and solutions about the project approach**
Correct. Brainstorming is a data gathering technique that is frequently used when
developing the project management plan to gather ideas and solutions on the project
approach.
- **D Conflict management to bring diverse stakeholders into alignment on all aspects of the**
project management plan
Incorrect. Conflict management is an interpersonal and team skill that may be necessary to
bring diverse stakeholders into alignment on all aspects of the project management plan.
Since conflict management is not a data gathering technique, this answer choice can be
eliminated.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 63 of 200
Question ID: 613757
The project is in planning, and the project team is identifying risks. The project team members
are utilizing a technique to increase the breadth of identified risks by including internally
generated risks. The team starts with the identification of the strengths and weaknesses of the
organization and then identifies any opportunities that arise from strengths, and any threats
resulting from weaknesses.
What data analysis technique is being used by the project team?
- **A Affinity diagrams**
- **B Alternatives analysis**
- **C SWOT analysis**
- **D Monte Carlo simulation**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What data analysis technique is an input to the Identify Risks process and analyzes the strengths,
weaknesses, opportunities, and threats of a project?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Based on the scenario provided, the project team is performing the Identify Risks process. One
of the tools and techniques used in this process is the data analysis technique referred to as
SWOT analysis. This technique examines the project from each of the strengths, weaknesses,
opportunities, and threats (SWOT) perspectives. The project team is using a SWOT analysis to
increase the breadth of identified risks by including internally generated risks.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Affinity diagrams**
Incorrect. An affinity diagram is a technique that allows large numbers of ideas to be
classified into groups for review and analysis. Based on the scenario provided, the project
team is performing the project management process of Identify Risks. An affinity diagram is
a data representation technique that is typically used in the Collect Requirements and
Manage Quality processes. However, it is not a data analysis technique used during the
Identify Risks process.
- **B Alternatives analysis**
Incorrect. An alternatives analysis is a technique used to evaluate identified options in
order to select the options or approaches to use to execute and perform the work of the
project. Based on the scenario provided, the project team is performing the project
management process of Identify Risks. An alternatives analysis is a data analysis technique
that is utilized for many of the project management processes. However, an alternatives
analysis is not typically used as a technique during the Identify Risks process.
- **C SWOT analysis**
Correct. A SWOT analysis is an analysis of strengths, weaknesses, opportunities, and
threats of an organization, project, or option. The project team is performing a SWOT
analysis to increase the breadth of identified risks.
- **D Monte Carlo simulation**
Incorrect. A Monte Carlo simulation is an analysis technique where a computer model is
iterated many times, with the input values chosen at random for each iteration driven by
the input data, including probability distributions and probabilistic branches. Based on the
scenario provided, the project team is performing the project management process of
Identify Risks. A Monte Carlo simulation is a data analysis technique that is used in several
project management processes. However, it is not used during the Identify Risks process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 415

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 64 of 200
Question ID: 613073
As a project manager, you are developing the project charter for your new project. In reviewing
the business case, you have noticed that an important element was not included in the economic
feasibility study.
What is the best course of action for you in this situation?
- **A Disregard the missing information as the project sponsor should be developing the project**
charter and not the project manager
- **B Update the business case with the missing information as necessary**
- **C Escalate the issue with the business case to the project sponsor along with**
recommendations
- **D The business case is not an input to the project charter, so the missing information is not**
relevant at this early stage of the project
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who has the authority to update the business documents?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The project charter incorporates the appropriate information for the project from the business
documents which include the business case and benefits management plan. The project manager
does not update or modify the business documents since they are not considered project
documents. The project manager does not have the authority to update the business case as it is
commonly used for decision making by managers or executives above the project level.
However, the project manager may make recommendations. Therefore, of the available choices,
escalating the issue with the business case to the project sponsor along with recommendations is
the best course of action in this situation.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Disregard the missing information as the project sponsor should be developing the project**
charter and not the project manager
Incorrect. The project charter may be developed by the project sponsor, project manager, or
a collaboration between the two. The project sponsor approves the project charter but does
not necessarily create it. Additionally, important and relevant information missing from the
business case is a significant issue that should not be disregarded.
- **B Update the business case with the missing information as necessary**
Incorrect. The business documents include the business case and the benefits management
plan. The project manager should not update or modify the business documents since they
are not considered project documents. The project manager lacks the authority to update
the business case as it is commonly used for decision making by managers or executives
above the project level.
- **C Escalate the issue with the business case to the project sponsor along with**
recommendations
Correct. The project charter incorporates the appropriate information for the project from
the business documents which include the business case and benefits management plan.
The project manager does not update or modify the business documents since they are not
considered project documents; however, the project manager may make recommendations.
- **D The business case is not an input to the project charter, so the missing information is not**
relevant at this early stage of the project
Incorrect. The approved business case is the business document most commonly used to
create the project charter. The business case describes the necessary information from a
business standpoint to determine whether the expected outcomes of the project justify the
required investment. Therefore, the business case is an input into the creation of the project
charter, and any missing information would be very relevant.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 77-78
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 65 of 200
Question ID: 612669
Midway into project execution, a vendor determines that the grade of concrete specified in the
agreement will not meet earthquake resistance standards that were just revised by a government
agency. The vendor submits a change request recommending the use of another grade of concrete
to ensure compliance with the new regulations. The project manager is unsure how to handle this
change request as it came from the vendor.
What is the best course of action for the project manager?
- **A Consult with the project sponsor**
- **B Record the disposition of the change request in the change log**
- **C Consult the change management plan**
- **D Document the risk of the new regulation in the risk register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where should the project manager find a description of the process for submitting, evaluating,
and implementing changes to the project?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The change management plan is a component of the project management plan that establishes the
change control board, documents the extent of its authority, and describes how the change
control system will be implemented. Changes can be requested by any project stakeholder.
Vendors are important external project stakeholders and, like any other internal stakeholder, can
submit change requests. As it pertains to project procurement management, the change
management plan contains information about how seller-created changes will be processed.
Therefore, to understand how to handle the change request issued by the vendor, the project
manager has to consult the change management plan.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Consult with the project sponsor**
Incorrect. There is no reason to bother the project sponsor with every change requested on
a project. Nothing in the scenario suggests that the project manager does not have the
authority to address the situation without consulting with the sponsor.
- **B Record the disposition of the change request in the change log**
Incorrect. In this scenario, the project manager is looking for the procedure on how to
handle a change request. A decision regarding the change request must be made before the
disposition can be recorded in the change log.
- **C Consult the change management plan**
Correct. As an input to the Control Procurements process, the change management plan
contains information about how seller-created changes will be processed. Therefore,
consulting this plan is the best course of action for the project manager.
- **D Document the risk of the new regulation in the risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a project document in which outputs of risk management
processes are recorded. While it is important to document the risk of the new regulation in
the risk register, the question asks what should the project manager do with the change
request rather than how to address the new regulation.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 495

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 66 of 200
Question ID: 612229
- **A project manager focuses on systems and structure to accomplish project goals. As a result, the**
project manager has a strained relationship with the project team. Although the current project is
trending to meet project objectives, excessive turnover of the project team threatens the project.
For self-improvement, what type of skills should the project manager spend time developing?
- **A Management skills**
- **B Operational and problem-solving skills**
- **C Leadership skills**
- **D Administrative skills**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager needs to focus on relationships with people.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The strained relationship with the project team suggests that the project manager lacks leadership
skills. Management focuses on systems and structure while leadership focuses on relationships
with people. All of the incorrect answer choices are representative of management rather than
leadership. Therefore, of the available options, the project manager should spend time
developing better leadership skills to foster a better relationship with the project team.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Management skills**
Incorrect. A focus on systems and structure is representative of management over
leadership. The fact that the project manager has a strained relationship with the project
team suggests that the project manager needs to develop better leadership skills.
- **B Operational and problem-solving skills**
Incorrect. Operational and problem-solving is related to management skills. The project
manager needs to develop better leadership skills to foster a better relationship with the
project team.
- **C Leadership skills**
Correct. The strained relationship with the project team suggests that the project manager
lacks in leadership skills to foster better relationships.
- **D Administrative skills**
Incorrect. The question implies that the project manager lacks in leadership skills as
exemplified by the strained relationship with the project team. Administrative skills are
more closely aligned with management skills, which are not likely to foster an improved
relationship with the project team.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 64

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 67 of 200
Question ID: 612284
- **A project manager has been asked to draft a charter for a project to develop GPS applications for**
use in aircraft. However, the company's past projects have been in the marine and automobile
industries.
What should the project manager do first to determine the high-level requirements, boundaries,
and key deliverables for the project?
- **A Find a consultant with extensive technical knowledge of the aviation industry**
- **B Develop rigorous quality metrics acceptable in the aviation industry**
- **C Start the process of acquiring team members with the necessary experience**
- **D Begin the development of the project management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice describes a tool or technique which may be beneficial in the development
of the project charter?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

One of the tools and techniques that may be beneficial in the Develop Project Charter process
described in the scenario is expert judgment. Since the performing organization lacks experience
in developing products for the aviation industry, before determining the high-level requirements
for the project and developing the high-level project description, boundaries, and key
deliverables, the project manager should seek insight from individuals or groups with specialized
knowledge or training in the aviation industry. Inputs provided by these experts may help the
project manager make better decisions while developing the elements of the project charter
requiring this expertise. Therefore, of the available choices, hiring a consultant with extensive
technical knowledge of the aviation industry is what the project manager should do first.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Find a consultant with extensive technical knowledge of the aviation industry**
Correct. This answer choice describes expert judgment in the form of technical knowledge
of the aviation industry. For the Develop Project Charter process, in this case, expertise
should be considered from individuals or groups with specialized knowledge or training in
the aviation industry.
- **B Develop rigorous quality metrics acceptable in the aviation industry**
Incorrect. While the quality metrics will have to be developed (regardless of the industry
the project operates in), this activity typically takes place during project planning, while the
scenario suggests the project is in initiation.
- **C Start the process of acquiring team members with the necessary experience**
Incorrect. Acquiring project team members is part of the Acquire Resources process which
is carried out during project execution. In the scenario described, the project is still early
in initiating.
- **D Begin the development of the project management plan**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the project is still in initiating, and the project charter
has not yet been created. Therefore, beginning the development of the project management
plan is premature at this point.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 79

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 68 of 200
Question ID: 613485
- **A project has greatly exceeded its projected business objectives providing nearly twice its**
estimated benefit.
What document should be created as part of project closure to capture this information?
- **A Final report**
- **B Benefits management plan**
- **C Lessons learned register**
- **D Project management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice represents a document that is created as an output of project closure?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The project’s final report contains the overall summary of project performance, including nearly
every aspect of the project from risk to the degree in which the product, service, or result of the
project fulfills the business case. Although all of the documents listed as answer choices should
be updated as part of the Close Project or Phase process, only the final report is 'created' as an
output of this process. Additionally, the incorrect answer choices are not likely to include an
overall summary of project performance. Therefore, of the options offered, the final report is the
best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Final report**
Correct. A summary of how well and to what degree the project achieved the business
needs should be documented in the project’s final report.
- **B Benefits management plan**
Incorrect. The benefits management plan documents the processes for creating,
maximizing, and sustaining the benefits provided by a project or program. It does not
contain an updated summary of how the project met business objectives.
- **C Lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register should be updated with the accuracy of the business
case, as well as any knowledge gained during the project. However, the lessons learned
register is not likely to contain an overall summary of the final project outcomes and how
well the project fulfilled the business objectives.
- **D Project management plan**
Incorrect. There may be parts of the project management plan (or other project documents)
that helped achieve the success, but they will not have a summary of how the project met
and exceeded business objectives.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 127

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 69 of 200
Question ID: 612673
It has come to the project manager's attention that critical information has been missed by
stakeholders, which has caused emerging issues to be overlooked and responses to be delayed.
Feedback from the stakeholders indicates that they are experiencing "information overload" as
critical project elements get lost in the weekly project status reports.
What is the best course of action?
- **A Transfer the responsibilities to other stakeholders**
- **B Introduce visual management tools including a project dashboard**
- **C Use push communications to ensure the project status reports are received by the**
stakeholders
- **D Generate the project status reports daily instead of weekly**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How can the project manager ensure that critical elements can be quickly gleaned from the
project status reports?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that critical elements cannot be quickly gleaned from the project status
reports. The use of visual management tools is one of the trends and emerging practices in
Project Integration Management. Some project teams use visual management tools, rather than
written plans and other documents, to capture and oversee critical project elements. Making key
project elements visible to the entire team provides a real-time overview of the project status,
facilitates knowledge transfer, and empowers the team members and other stakeholders to help
identify and solve issues. The incorrect answer choices do not address the underlying problem

---

posed by the question. Therefore, of the available choices, introducing visual management tools
including a project dashboard is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Transfer the responsibilities to other stakeholders**
Incorrect. The transfer of responsibilities to other stakeholders does not address the
underlying problem. It is likely the issues of "information overload" would transfer to the
other stakeholders unless action is taken to address the issue described by the question.
- **B Introduce visual management tools including a project dashboard**
Correct. Making key project elements visible to the entire team provides a real-time
overview of the project status, facilitates knowledge transfer, and empowers and aids the
team members and other stakeholders to identify and solve issues.
- **C Use push communications to ensure the project status reports are received by the**
stakeholders
Incorrect. It is not known from the question how the project status reports are being
disseminated. Regardless, the question does not indicate that the stakeholders are not
receiving the project status reports. Rather, critical project elements are getting lost in the
reports.
- **D Generate the project status reports daily instead of weekly**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents an action that does not address the underlying
problem described by the question. The question suggests that critical elements cannot be
quickly gleaned from the project status reports. Providing the reports more frequently is
more likely to exacerbate the problem rather than address it.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 73, 112; see also
https://www.pmi.org/learning/library/visual-project-management-visual-elements-9862

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 70 of 200
Question ID: 612706
You are scheduling a meeting of your project team to brainstorm ideas to solve a problem that
key stakeholders described in detail in a different meeting.
What would be helpful for the upcoming meeting?
- **A A detailed agenda for the upcoming meeting**
- **B A poll**
- **C Minutes from the stakeholder meeting**
- **D Inviting all of the stakeholders from the previous meeting**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The point of brainstorming is to freely generate ideas without judgment, after which you select
the best idea.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Brainstorming is a technique that can be used in many project management processes. The point
of brainstorming is to freely generate ideas without judgment, after which the best idea is
selected. To help your project team come to the meeting prepared, you should ask them to review
the minutes of the stakeholder meeting to orient them to the context of the issue in question,
highlighting the stakeholders' specific concerns.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A A detailed agenda for the upcoming meeting**
Incorrect. While having an agenda for a meeting is a good meeting management practice,
brainstorming solutions to one problem does not require a detailed agenda.
- **B A poll**
Incorrect. A poll can gather attendee's votes to prioritize issues or select the most popular
solutions, but does not help generate ideas for the upcoming brainstorming session.
- **C Minutes from the stakeholder meeting**
Correct. Meeting minutes are a formal communication artifact used to summarize what was
discussed during a meeting. Meeting minutes may include a list of attendees, the purpose
for the meeting, the original agenda, the events that actually occurred during the meeting,
materials presented such as slides or reports, outstanding questions or concerns, and
action items discussed along with relevant votes, milestones, assignments of responsibility,
and deadlines. If the project team can get some exposure to a formal report of what caused
the stakeholders to be concerned, and the context of the discussion, it may help with
brainstorming ideas for the solution.
- **D Inviting all of the stakeholders from the previous meeting**
Incorrect. Inviting all of the stakeholders from the previous meeting to a brainstorming
session with your project team may stifle ideas if team members are afraid of looking silly
in front of key stakeholders who may well be decision makers. Brainstorming should be
among people who feel comfortable speaking freely. Additionally, inviting all of the
stakeholders from the previous meeting to the brainstorming meeting may not be the best
use of the stakeholders' time.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 80, 361, 381, 386; see also
https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minutes
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 71 of 200
Question ID: 610062
- **A project manager submits a formal change request to the change control board (CCB). After a**
month with no response, the project has fallen significantly behind schedule. The project
manager follows up and is shocked to learn that the CCB approved the change request several
weeks ago.
What should have been done to avoid this mix-up?
- **A The CCB should have communicated their decision to the project manager.**
- **B The CCB should have made their decision faster.**
- **C Nothing; the project manager and the CCB acted as specified in the procedures.**
- **D The project manager should have been a member of the CCB.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who is responsible for recording and communicating the decisions made by change control
boards?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Change control boards are responsible for meeting and reviewing change requests and
approving, rejecting, or deferring change requests. All decisions should be recorded and
communicated to the request owner and stakeholders for information and follow-up actions. In
this scenario, that step appears to have been overlooked, resulting in unnecessary project
schedule delays. Of the answer choices, the best action that would have prevented such an issue
is for the change control board to communicate their decision to the project manager.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The CCB should have communicated their decision to the project manager.**
Correct. This issue is most likely due to poor communication. If the project manager was
not aware of the CCB’s decision until following up with them, it could be assumed that the
CCB never documented or communicated their decision. It is the responsibility of the CCB
to communicate the decision to the request owner.
- **B The CCB should have made their decision faster.**
Incorrect. In this scenario, the CCB’s mistake was not in taking too long to make a decision
but rather in failing to document and communicate their decision to the request owner so
that the project manager could implement follow-up actions.
- **C Nothing; the project manager and the CCB acted as specified in the procedures.**
Incorrect. Unless stated differently in the question, it is unlikely that the procedures would
specify that the decisions on the change requests should not be communicated to the
relevant stakeholders.
- **D The project manager should have been a member of the CCB.**
Incorrect. While project managers can and often do serve on change control boards, this is
not appropriate or feasible for every project. If the project manager was not made part of
the CCB during the project’s planning phase, we should assume there was a justifiable
reason. However, even if the project manager had been a member of the CCB, this does not
negate the need for documentation and communication from the CCB.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 120
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
