PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 98 of 200
Question ID: 651304
The project is developing an update to a software tool. There have been a series of changes made
to the product, and more changes are expected. Correspondingly, engineers on the team are
modifying documentation frequently to reflect the changes.
What is the best course of action to ensure engineers are working on the most current version of
documentation?
- **A Audit the documentation daily to ensure the correctness of the information**
- **B Require the requirements documentation to have the current date on the header**
- **C Assign an accountable engineer to validate all changes and update project plans**
- **D Maintain a configuration management system and communicate appropriately**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the root cause of the issue here? How can a project manager assure some document
control?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

In this scenario, the project team needs assurance that they are working with the most current
documentation. With many changes occurring – potentially because they are managing the
product scope in an agile manner – it is important that the engineers are working off the correct
documentation. A configuration management system assists the project team and other
stakeholders to track and monitor changes and versions to project artifacts. Having a single
source and a collection of procedures for the source, the team is well informed about the correct
documentation and can communicate to others when changes have been made. Hence the
configuration management system is more ideal for them in this situation.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Audit the documentation daily to ensure the correctness of the information**
Incorrect. An audit might help in assuring the correctness of the documents, but it is not a
long-term solution. There are many changes being made with more expected. The issue is
not so much about inaccuracies as it is about using the most current version of the product
documentation.
- **B Require the requirements documentation to have the current date on the header**
Incorrect. Using proper dates on the document headers might be a suitable short-term
resolution, if feasible and if changes only happen once a day and that dating is enough to
distinguish the multiple versions. Nevertheless, it does not address the root cause of not
having a more complete collection of procedures around managing the configuration items
of this project – which is the product documentation.
- **C Assign an accountable engineer to validate all changes and update project plans**
Incorrect. The problem in this situation is not necessarily that changes are being made to
the project plans and the changes require validation. The problem is more associated with
the document controls and communication. Assigning an engineer to validate the changes
and update plans does not address the issue.
- **D Maintain a configuration management system and communicate appropriately**
Correct. A configuration management system assists project stakeholders in monitoring
and tracking the changes to project artifacts, such as product documentation. The system
assures the engineers that they are working on the most current version of the
documentation.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 41, 701

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 99 of 200
Question ID: 612020
Your procurement manager has asked you to compare the current schedule and cost performance
of the installations against what was promised in the agreement with the vendor.
What comparative process does the procurement manager refer to?
- **A A performance review**
- **B A procurement statement of work (SOW)**
- **C A procurement improvement plan**
- **D An audit**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This is a type of data analysis used in the Control Procurements process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Based on the scenario described, you are going to perform the Control Procurements process.
Performance reviews are a type of data analysis tool used in that process. Performance reviews
for contracts measure, compare, and analyze quality, resource, schedule, and cost performance
against the agreement. This comparison includes identifying work packages that are ahead or
behind schedule, over or under budget, or have resource or quality issues.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A A performance review**

---

Correct. A performance review is a technique that is used to measure, compare, and
analyze actual performance of work in progress on the project against the baseline. In the
Control Procurements process, the baseline compared against is the contract with the
seller.
- **B A procurement statement of work (SOW)**
Incorrect. A procurement SOW is prepared by the buyer to give sellers a clear description
of the scope of the work the buyer is seeking to purchase. During the Conduct
Procurements process, the SOW is used by sellers to determine an estimate and submit it to
the buyer for consideration of a contract. In this scenario, the work is in progress, so the
agreement has already been signed making this an incorrect answer.
- **C A procurement improvement plan**
Incorrect. The 'procurement improvement' plan is a made-up term for this question.
- **D An audit**
Incorrect. An audit is a tool used in the Control Procurements process to review the
contracts and contracting processes for completeness, accuracy, and effectiveness. In the
scenario described, you are comparing actual results achieved to what was promised in the
contract. An audit is about evaluating and improving the procurement process while the
performance review is about assessing different aspects of the vendor's performance;
therefore, an audit is not the best answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 498

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 100 of 200
Question ID: 612678
- **A project manager is leading an infrastructure development project and is in the process of**
comparing actual overall project performance against the performance objectives described in
the project management plan.
Which of the following activities is the project manager least likely to conduct during this
process?
- **A Analyzing individuals or groups affected by the project**
- **B Checking the status of individual project risks**
- **C Providing forecasts to update the current cost and schedule information**
- **D Monitoring implementation of approved changes as they occur**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice is part of the Initiating Process Group and not the Monitoring and
Controlling Process Group?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Monitor and Control Project Work is being carried out. Monitor
and Control Project Work is the process of tracking, reviewing, and reporting the overall
progress to meet the performance objectives defined in the project management plan. All of the
incorrect answer choices are activities which are associated with the Monitor and Control Project
Work process. Individuals or groups affected by the project is a partial definition of stakeholders.
"Stakeholder analysis" is disguised by the correct answer choice. Stakeholder analysis is
performed during the Identify Stakeholders process in order to develop the stakeholder register.
Note, the question is asking to select the activity that is 'least' likely to be conducted during the
Monitor and Control Project Work process. Performing stakeholder analysis is the 'least' likely

---

activity to be conducted by the project manager in this scenario and is, therefore, the best answer
to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Analyzing individuals or groups affected by the project**
Correct. The question implies that the Monitor and Control Project Work is being carried
out. Individuals or groups affected by the project is a partial definition of stakeholders.
Stakeholder analysis is performed during the Identify Stakeholders process in order to
develop the stakeholder register. Therefore, performing stakeholder analysis is the 'least'
likely activity to be conducted in this scenario.
- **B Checking the status of individual project risks**
Incorrect. As part of the Monitor and Control Project Work process, the project manager
may check the status of individual project risks.
- **C Providing forecasts to update the current cost and schedule information**
Incorrect. Providing forecasts to update the current cost and schedule information is a
function of the Monitor and Control Project Work process.
- **D Monitoring implementation of approved changes as they occur**
Incorrect. Although approved changes are implemented through the Direct and Manage
Project Work process, 'monitoring' of the implementation of approved changes is an aspect
of the Monitor and Control Project Work process.

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 101 of 200
Question ID: 612918
All the technical work on a project has been completed, and the product has been transitioned to
a support team.
What should the project manager do before the project can be closed?
- **A Issue a quality report**
- **B Validate the scope**
- **C Close the contracts**
- **D Measure stakeholder satisfaction**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What other activity is part of the Close Project or Phase process?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Since all the technical work has been completed, and the product has been transitioned to the
support group, one may assume the project is in the Close Project or Phase process. When
closing a project, the project manager reviews the project management plan to ensure all project
work is completed, and that the project has met its objectives. Measuring stakeholder satisfaction
is one of the activities which is necessary to be performed before the administrative closure of
the project can take place.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Issue a quality report**
Incorrect. The quality report typically includes all of the quality assurance issues that were
managed by the team, recommendations for improvement, and the summary of findings
from the Control Quality process. Quality reports are an output of the Manage Quality
process and an input to the Close Project or Phase process. According to the scenario, all
the technical work has been completed, and the product has been transitioned to a support
team suggesting the project is in the Close Project or Phase process, not the Manage
Quality process.
- **B Validate the scope**
Incorrect. During the Validate Scope process, the completed project deliverables are
inspected and formally accepted by the customer or relevant stakeholders. In the scenario
described, the product has already been transitioned to the support team. The transitioning
of the product to the support team is part of the project closure. This action suggests the
scope has already been validated.
- **C Close the contracts**
Incorrect. While closing contracts should be done before the project can be closed, there is
not enough information in the question to determine if there were any contracts on the
project.
- **D Measure stakeholder satisfaction**
Correct. Measuring stakeholder satisfaction is one of the activities performed during
project closure.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 123, 127

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 102 of 200
Question ID: 625114
At this point in the project, the system analysis, design, and development should have been
completed. However, according to the table shown below, system development is only 50%
complete, and the actual cost of system analysis is higher than planned. You believe that
remaining project work will be influenced by these low cost and schedule performance values.
Which of the formulas should be used to determine estimate at completion (EAC)?
- **A EAC = AC + [(BAC - EV) / (CPI x SPI)]**
- **B EAC = BAC / CPI**
- **C EAC = AC + BAC - EV**
- **D EAC = BAC**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

When both CPI and SPI influence the remainder of the project work, you should select the
formula that contains both of these indices.
Correct Answer: A

---


**Explanation:**

The table shows that cost performance is poor as the actual costs are greater than planned values
for completed and partially completed work. In addition, since the 3rd task system development
is only 50% complete instead of being finished according to the plan, the schedule performance
is poor. The scenario indicates that these current cost and schedule performance will influence
the remainder of the project work. In other words, both CPI and SPI affect the estimate at
completion (EAC). Therefore, one should use the formula that considers both of these indices,
i.e., EAC = AC + [(BAC - EV) / (CPI x SPI)].

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A EAC = AC + [(BAC - EV) / (CPI x SPI)]**
Correct. The correct formula to use in this scenario is EAC = AC + [(BAC - EV) / (CPI x
SPI)] because the question states the CPI and the SPI will be factors in determining EAC.
This equation factors both in the estimate.
- **B EAC = BAC / CPI**
Incorrect. This formula is used when only the CPI is considered to be a factor in
determining EAC. However, the question is asking to include the performance of both cost
and schedule to derive the EAC, making this choice an incorrect answer.
- **C EAC = AC + BAC - EV**
Incorrect. This formula is to be used when the remainder of the work is expected to be
completed at the initial budgeted rate. This would require the CPI to improve, and the
remaining work will be done at this rate. However, the question states that for the
remainder of the project, the work is expected to be influenced by the current cost
performance and not improved to the budgeted rate.
- **D EAC = BAC**
Incorrect. Given that both the cost performance and the schedule performance are both not
performing at the budgeted rate and that these performances are not expected to change, it
is not plausible to assume that the estimated cost at completion would be the same as what
was originally planned.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 265; see
also https://www.project-management-prepcast.com/pmp-formulas

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 103 of 200
Question ID: 612272
As the project manager, you are in the process of developing a draft of a document which
authorizes a new software development project. You have reviewed the agreements and both
business documents.
What is also important to do during this process?
- **A Identify stakeholders and prepare the stakeholder register**
- **B Study the governance functions and processes to provide guidance and decision making**
- **C Update the business documents to correct any errors**
- **D Review the benefits management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

You, as the project manager, are developing the project charter.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes a project manager who is developing a draft of the project charter. One of
the typical activities performed while developing the charter is to review organizational process
assets (OPAs), which may influence this process. One of the OPAs is the project governance
framework which often provides information about the governance functions, processes, that are
important when making decisions that are relevant to the project charter.
One may argue that a stakeholder register can be created at the same time the project charter is
developed and approved. While it's true, the question is asking to select the answer choice that
represents an action performed 'during this process'. Since the scenario describes the Develop
Project Charter process, any action that is associated with 'this process' would be a better option
than an action associated with 'another process', even if that process can be done in parallel with
the one described in the scenario. Therefore, as we always recommend selecting the best answer

---

of those provided, studying the governance functions and processes to provide guidance and
decision making is a better answer choice than identifying stakeholders and preparing the
stakeholder register since the former is associated with the inputs to the Develop Project Charter
process while the latter is not even part of this process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Identify stakeholders and prepare the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The question implies that you, as the project manager, are conducting the
Develop Project Charter process. The stakeholder register is developed during the Identify
Stakeholders process and not the Develop Project Charter process.
- **B Study the governance functions and processes to provide guidance and decision making**
Correct. The project governance framework is part of the organizational process assets
(OPA), which serve as an input into the Develop Project Charter process.
- **C Update the business documents to correct any errors**
Incorrect. The project manager may make recommendations but does not update or modify
the business documents since they are not project documents.
- **D Review the benefits management plan**
Incorrect. The benefits management plan and business case comprise the business
documents, and the question states that these documents have already been reviewed.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

Question 104 of 200
Question ID: 612242
- **A project manager has been asked to create a document that formally authorizes a project to use**
ground-penetrating radar to map geological conditions along a proposed crude oil pipeline route.
The performing organization has agreed to share the data with a local university. The project
manager has reviewed the business documents and considered any relevant external
environmental factors to create the requested document.
What might the project manager do next?
- **A Research the stakeholder engagement plan for any information to be included in the**
document
- **B Ensure any relevant information from the memorandum of understanding (MOU) is**
included in the document
- **C Review the business case for any pertinent information**
- **D Look to see if a benefits management plan was previously created**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project charter is a document issued by the project initiator or sponsor that formally
authorizes the existence of a project.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project manager is developing the project charter. The project
charter is a document issued by the project initiator or sponsor that formally authorizes the
existence of a project. The question indicates that the project manager has already included the
business documents as inputs into the process of developing the project charter as well as
considered any external environmental factors. The business documents include the business
case and benefits management plan. Agreements are also inputs into the Develop Project Charter
process, and a memorandum of understanding (MOU) is an example of an agreement.

---

Additionally, the agreement to share data with the university in this scenario may be documented
as an MOU. Note that organizational process assets (OPA) are also considered inputs into this
process but were not mentioned in the scenario or offered as an answer choice. Therefore, of the
available options, ensuring that any relevant information from the memorandum of
understanding (MOU) is included in the document is the best answer.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Research the stakeholder engagement plan for any information to be included in the**
document
Incorrect. The question suggests that the project manager is developing the project charter.
The stakeholder engagement plan is a subsidiary of the project management plan and is not
produced until later in the project during project planning.
- **B Ensure any relevant information from the memorandum of understanding (MOU) is**
included in the document
Correct. An MOU is an agreement that may be used as an input into the development of the
project charter, as implied by the question. For instance, the agreement to share data with
the university in this scenario might be documented as an MOU.
- **C Review the business case for any pertinent information**
Incorrect. The business case is one of the business documents, and the question states that
the business documents have already been reviewed. Therefore, reviewing the business case
would be redundant.
- **D Look to see if a benefits management plan was previously created**
Incorrect. The benefits management plan is a business document used in the Develop
Project Charter process. The question states that the business documents have already been
reviewed. So, if the plan exists, it would have already been reviewed.

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 105 of 200
Question ID: 612616
When estimating resources for your project, you have determined that the company does not
have enough developers to complete the required work. You can either hire additional developers
as permanent employees or bring temporary contractors. The make-or-buy analysis resulted in a
return on investment (ROI) of 25% if the project work is completed by adding permanent
employees and an ROI of 20% if you bring in contractors. You decide to bring in the contractors.
Which of the following was the most likely reason for this decision?
- **A To avoid expanding permanent employment obligations**
- **B To reduce the project costs by using less expensive contractors**
- **C To protect confidential information and intellectual property**
- **D To complete the project faster by shortening its duration by 5%**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In addition to profitability, what else should be considered when making a make-or-buy
decision?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

In this scenario, the ROI for using internal resources was estimated to be 25% versus outsourcing
with an ROI of 20%. Based on these estimates, it is more profitable to hire the additional
developers compared with using contractors to complete the project work. Based on profitability
alone, the logical decision is to hire the additional developers and conduct the project internally.
However, other considerations beyond profitability should be taken into account. One important
consideration includes the financial obligation for providing employment to the newly hired
developers after the project is concluded. If the performing organization feels that they will not
need additional developers after the current project is complete, then it may make sense to use
contractors instead of hiring developers even though the project will be less profitable as a result.

---

Therefore, of the available options, the most likely reason to use contractors in this scenario is to
avoid expanding permanent employment obligations.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A To avoid expanding permanent employment obligations**
Correct. If the performing organization feels that they will not need additional developers
after the current project is complete, then it may make sense to use contractors instead of
hiring developers even though the project will be less profitable as a result.
- **B To reduce the project costs by using less expensive contractors**
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine that the contractors
were estimated to be less expensive than internal resources. In fact, the estimated ROI
indicates that it would be more profitable to use internal resources than contractors.
- **C To protect confidential information and intellectual property**
Incorrect. If the company wanted to protect its confidential information and intellectual
property, the company would unlikely involve external contractors in the project work.
- **D To complete the project faster by shortening its duration by 5%**
Incorrect. It cannot be determined based on the information provided in the question if
supplementing the existing team with contractors would have resulted in completing the
project faster and by what percentage. The 5% is the difference between the ROI values and
has nothing to do with the project duration.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 473

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 106 of 200
Question ID: 612514
As a project progresses, existing knowledge is used, and new knowledge is created to achieve the
project's objectives and contribute to organizational learning.
Which of the following enterprise environmental factors would contribute to this process?
- **A Lessons learned register**
- **B Knowledge management plan**
- **C Trusting working relationships**
- **D Interpersonal and team skills**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The answer has to do with how people work with each other.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Using existing knowledge and creating new knowledge to achieve the project's objectives and
contribute to organizational learning is the definition of the Manage Project Knowledge process.
The question is asking to find an enterprise environmental factor (EEF) which contributes (in
other words, serves as an input) to this process. Organizational, stakeholder, and customer
culture is an example of the EEFs that are among the inputs to the Manage Project Knowledge
process. The culture of trusting working relationships and a no-blame culture is particularly
important in managing knowledge on a project as it allows people to feel comfortable sharing
information. The incorrect answer choices, while being inputs to the process, can be eliminated
simply because none of them is considered an EEF.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register provides information on effective practices in
knowledge management and serves as an input to the Manage Project Knowledge process
implied by the scenario. However, the lessons learned register is a project document rather
than an enterprise environmental factor. At the same time, due to the iterative nature of
project management, the lessons learned register is an output from the process, while the
question is looking for a contributing factor, e.g., an input.
- **B Knowledge management plan**
Incorrect. The knowledge management plan is a made-up term. Even if this plan did exist, it
would have been considered a component of the project management plan rather than an
EEF.
- **C Trusting working relationships**
Correct. Having trusting working relationships and a no-blame culture allows the team, the
stakeholders, and the customer feel comfortable sharing information, thus contributing to
the creation of new knowledge and achieving the project's objectives.
- **D Interpersonal and team skills**
Incorrect. While having strong interpersonal and team skills would likely contribute to the
Manage Project Knowledge process inferred by the scenario, these skills are not considered
enterprise environmental factors.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 101

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 107 of 200
Question ID: 612210
You are managing a project to develop recreational facilities for a community. You have internal
and external groups of stakeholders. You would like to send project performance-related
information to internal stakeholders only, but deliverable status information to both internal and
external stakeholders.
Which of the following processes would you use to actively send this information?
- **A Monitor Stakeholder Engagement**
- **B Plan Stakeholder Engagement**
- **C Manage Stakeholder Engagement**
- **D Plan Communications Management**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which process is most involved in actively communicating with the project stakeholders?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

One may argue that the correct answer should be Manage Communications. However, this option
is not listed among the answer choices. Certainly, Project Communications Management and
Project Stakeholder Management are two very closely correlated Knowledge Areas. Manage
Communications is the process of "ensuring timely and appropriate collection, creation,
distribution, storage, retrieval, management, monitoring, and the ultimate disposition of project
information." One of the outputs from this process is the actual project communications, which
include the performance reports, the status of deliverables, schedule progress, the cost incurred,
presentations, and other information required by stakeholders which is what described in the
scenario. Manage Stakeholder Engagement is the process of "communicating and working with
stakeholders to meet their needs and expectations, address issues, and foster appropriate
stakeholder involvement." However, the output artifacts for this process only include change

---

requests and updates to the project management plan and project documents. Eventually, we can
say that Manage Communications process is the means by which Manage Stakeholder
Engagement process is carried out.
Now let us for a moment forget what we have just written. Let’s pretend we are taking the actual
PMP exam. What choice would you pick? There is no Manage Communications as one of the
answer choices. There is only Manage Stakeholder Engagement and three other choices which
are likely incorrect (we assume you do not argue over them). The point we are trying to make
here is that on the real PMP exam the questions and the answers could be ambiguous. They may
have no any specific clarifications or clear definitions. There may be situations where more than
one (or even all) choices will seem to be correct or, on the other hand, incorrect answers.
Therefore while taking the exam, it is recommended to make reasonable assumptions based on
all 'available' information in the question and select the 'best' answer among the choices given. It
would not always be the ideal answer or the perfect answer you would prefer to hear, but it
should be better than the others. This is the whole idea of this simulator – to simulate the real
PMP exam so you would be better prepared for it. In this particular scenario, of the choices
provided, Manage Stakeholder Engagement is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Monitor Stakeholder Engagement**
Incorrect. Monitor Stakeholder Engagement is the process of 'monitoring' overall
stakeholder relationships and adjusting strategies and plans for engaging stakeholders,
which is not what is described in the scenario.
- **B Plan Stakeholder Engagement**
Incorrect. Plan Stakeholder Engagement is a planning process that involves developing
effective approaches required to involve stakeholders based on their needs, expectations,
interests, and potential impact. The question is asking to select a process in which you will
actively send information, implying the process is part of the Executing Process Group.
- **C Manage Stakeholder Engagement**
Correct. Of the choices available, Manage Stakeholder Engagement is the only process
where you are actively 'managing' the information for each type of stakeholder, making this
choice the best answer to the question asked.
- **D Plan Communications Management**

---

Incorrect. Plan Communications Management is a planning process that involves
'determining and documenting' the information required to manage project communications
effectively. The question is asking to select a process in which you will actively send
information, suggesting you are looking for an executing process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 503, 359
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 108 of 200
Question ID: 651302
- **A project requires consultant services. How much and for how long these services are needed is**
not known. The project needs to procure these services quickly.
Which contract type should be used?
- **A Cost plus fixed fee**
- **B Time and material**
- **C Cost plus award fee**
- **D Fixed fee with economic price adjustments**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the best type of contract for consultant services?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The details of the services needed are not fully determined. Since little is known about how
much time is needed for the consultant services, then a more logical choice of contract would be
to use one that only pays for the time and work needed. Additionally, the materials and
equipment needed are less known in this situation. Defining a contract that pays a fixed fee for
open-ended services is too risky. Similarly, a cost reimbursable for a service with unknown
boundaries could present its own risks – depending on how the contract was written and its terms
and conditions. Ergo, in this situation, the best contract type would be the time and material
contract.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Cost plus fixed fee**
Incorrect. At this time, not enough is known to determine the costs and fees of the services
requested properly. Additionally, the project needs procured services in the near term, so
the project team may not have the time and resources available to define these materials
and associated costs fully.
- **B Time and material**
Correct. Since little is known on how much time and material is needed for the consultant
services the time and material contract should be used. This contract type provides the
most flexibility for each party to acquire the resources and services needed without
pre-determining too many of the costs and other fees.
- **C Cost plus award fee**
Incorrect. Paying for the procured services via a cost-reimbursable type of contract may be
warranted in some situations. Although in this situation, there are too many unknown costs
and length of services required. Paying for the costs incurred would work if more were
known about the expected costs. The inclusion of an award fee would not be useful in this
situation unless more were known of the expected outcomes and satisfaction criteria.
- **D Fixed fee with economic price adjustments**
Incorrect. Paying a set cost for open-ended services is not a logical choice. That places too
much risk on both parties – seller and buyer. The inclusion of economic price adjustments
is more suitable for a long-term contract where fluctuations in costs, resources,
commodities, market value, currency rates, for example, are likely. There is no indication in
this scenario that a long-term agreement is needed.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 471-472

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 109 of 200
Question ID: 614004
The following table contains information about the duration, in days, of project activities and
their predecessor activity for a project.
What is the total float of activity G?
- **A 10 days**
- **B 17 days**
- **C 6 days**
- **D 0 days**
Question answered incorrectly

---


**Hint:**

The total float of any activity on the critical path is zero.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Total float refers to the maximum amount of time an activity can be delayed without pushing out
the project end date. If an activity is on the critical path, the total float of the activity is zero.
The first step to correctly answer this question is to determine the activity paths and their
durations for the project. This requires the creation of a project network diagram using the
precedence diagramming method (PDM) where you map the values from the data table included
in the question. Following is the network diagram for this question's scenario.
Once you have created the network diagram, the next step is to determine the specific paths that
exist for the activities on the project. This requires following each path that is mapped and
determining the duration of each path by adding up the number of days for each activity on that
specific path. The longest path through the project identifies the shortest possible length of the
project and is, therefore, the critical path. Following is each path through the project and its
duration:
Start-A-B-C-G-Finish = 10 days
Start-D-E-F-G-Finish = 17 days - the critical path because it has the longest length
Start-H-I-Finish = 6 days

---

Activity G is on two paths, Start-A-B-C-G-Finish and Start-D-E-F-G-Finish. As a rule, if an
activity is present on more than one path, and one of the paths is the critical path, the total float
for the activity will always be zero because delaying any activity on the critical path will delay
the project. Since activity G is on the critical path, its total float has to be zero.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A 10 days**
Incorrect. Activity G is on the critical path; therefore, its total float is zero. 10 days is the
duration of the path Start-A-B-C-G-Finish.
- **B 17 days**
Incorrect. Activity G is on the critical path; therefore, its total float is zero. 17 days is the
duration of the path Start-D-E-F-G-Finish.
- **C 6 days**
Incorrect. Activity G is on the critical path; therefore, its total float is zero. 6 days is the
duration of the path Start-H-I-Finish.
- **D 0 days**
Correct. Total float is defined as the amount of time a schedule activity can be delayed
without delaying the project finish date. Using the information given in the question and
drawing a network schedule using PDM, the critical path and its duration can be
determined. Activity G is on the critical path, and because delaying activity G would delay
the entire project, the total float of activity G has to be 0 days.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 210
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 110 of 200
Question ID: 612666
You are leading a project to bring a new automotive battery to market. You have just completed
an initial run of the production line to test the manufacturing process in preparation for mass
production. The knowledge gained from the test run will be used to improve performance during
mass production. During the test run, the conveyer belt transporting a subassembly jammed
several times for unknown reasons.
What should you do next?
- **A Update the issue log with the resolution**
- **B Develop a why-why diagram**
- **C Record the information in the lessons learned register**
- **D Begin mass production as soon as possible due to the aggressive timeline**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The problem must first be analyzed before any knowledge of value can be gained.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that you, as a project manager, are conducting a test run of the
manufacturing process to gain lessons learned to be used later in the project during mass
production. However, the problem encountered during the test run does not provide any useful
information that can be applied later in the project. The problem must first be analyzed to
understand the cause of the issue and then determine what corrective actions must be taken to
prevent the problem from recurring. A description of the problem, as well as steps necessary to
prevent the problem from recurring, can then be recorded in the lessons learned register.
- **A why-why diagram is also known as a cause-and-effect diagram, a fishbone diagram, or**
Ishikawa diagram. This type of diagram breaks down the causes of the problem statement

---

identified into discrete branches, helping to identify the main or root cause of the problem. This
identification of the root cause of the problem described by the question is a necessary first step
in resolving the issue and preventing the recurrence during mass production. Therefore, of the
available choices, you should first develop a why-why diagram to analyze the problem before the
knowledge gained can be documented in the lessons learned register.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Update the issue log with the resolution**
Incorrect. The problem encountered during the test run should be captured in the issue log.
However, the resolution is not known at this point in the scenario. The cause of the problem
must be understood and then resolved before the issue log can be updated with the
resolution.
- **B Develop a why-why diagram**
Correct. A why-why diagram is also known as a cause-and-effect diagram, a fishbone
diagram, or Ishikawa diagram. This type of diagram breaks down the causes of the
problem statement identified into discrete branches, helping to identify the main or root
cause of the problem. This identification of the root cause of the problem described by the
question is a necessary first step in resolving the issue and preventing the recurrence
during mass production.
- **C Record the information in the lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The knowledge gained from the test run should be captured in the lessons
learned register for use later in the project during mass production. However, the problem
encountered during the test run does not provide any useful information that can be applied
later in the project. The problem must first be analyzed to understand the cause of the issue
and then determine what corrective actions must be taken to prevent the problem from
recurring. A description of the problem, as well as steps necessary to prevent the problem
from recurring, can then be recorded in the lessons learned register.
- **D Begin mass production as soon as possible due to the aggressive timeline**
Incorrect. Without first resolving the problem encountered during the test run, mass
production would be severely hampered by the recurring issue. In order to bring the
product to market as soon as possible, any problems identified during the test run should be
addressed first.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 293, 297

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 111 of 200
Question ID: 625080
For a project, strict quality specifications must be followed, and all project team members were
required to read and sign off on the quality management plan, acknowledging complete
understanding of the specifications. The project manager suspects that one or more of the
project's primary material vendors is not supplying parts that meet project quality specifications.
What should the project manager do first?
- **A Tell the vendor to replace the parts**
- **B Conduct a procurement performance review**
- **C Discuss the issue with the sponsor**
- **D Terminate the contract with the vendor**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager is not sure but only suspects. Before taking any action, the project manager
should confirm these concerns.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

An aspirational standard of professional conduct in project management is that project managers
must earnestly seek to understand the truth. In this scenario, the project manager only suspects
that parts supplied by the vendor or vendors are not meeting the project's quality specifications,
but she does not know this for sure. The best way to determine this is to perform a procurement
performance review for the vendors. Performance reviews measure, compare, and analyze
quality, resource, schedule, and cost performance against the agreement. The results of this
procurement performance review will indicate whether or not the vendors are supplying parts
that meet project quality specifications specified in the agreement, and if any further action is
necessary on the project manager's part.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Tell the vendor to replace the parts**
Incorrect. At this point, the project manager only suspects that there are parts that do not
meet the project quality specifications and has not identified a specific vendor. The project
manager must first validate that her suspicions are correct and identify the specific
vendor(s) before asking for replacement parts.
- **B Conduct a procurement performance review**
Correct. A performance review is an example of a data analysis technique that can be used
as part of the Control Procurements process described in the scenario. Conducting a
procurement performance review to compare the quality of the materials received to the
quality specifications would provide the project manager the work performance
information needed to determine if quality issues truly exist with the materials received.
- **C Discuss the issue with the sponsor**
Incorrect. Though it may be necessary to confer with the project sponsor if it is determined
that quality issues exist and may impact the project schedule or budget, the discussion
should not take place until a determination has been reached by employing the appropriate
control processes.
- **D Terminate the contract with the vendor**
Incorrect. Terminating the contract with the vendor is a premature action. Such action
should not be taken until a true determination has been reached by employing the
appropriate control processes.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 498

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 112 of 200
Question ID: 625087
- **A junior project manager wants to understand the inputs, the outputs, the tools and techniques**
(ITTOs) which will be helpful in developing the change management plan. However, when she
reviews the PMBOK® Guide, she cannot find the ITTOs associated with this process.
What advice might an experienced project manager provide to the junior project manager?
- **A The ITTOs are listed in the PMBOK® Guide under the Plan Change Management process**
- **B Review the ITTOs associated with the Develop Project Management Plan process**
- **C The appropriate ITTOs will be listed with the Perform Integrated Change Control process**
- **D The project management office (PMO) provides the change management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

During which project management process is the change management plan developed?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The change management plan is a component of the project management plan that establishes the
change control board, documents the extent of its authority, and describes how the change
control system will be implemented. Although there is no specific project management process
for the creation of the change management plan, it is created as part of the Develop Project
Management Plan process. Therefore, the best advice the experienced project manager may
provide to the junior project manager who wants to develop the change management plan is to
review the ITTOs associated with the Develop Project Management Plan process.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A The ITTOs are listed in the PMBOK® Guide under the Plan Change Management process**
Incorrect. 'Plan Change Management' is not a process specified in the PMBOK® Guide.
- **B Review the ITTOs associated with the Develop Project Management Plan process**
Correct. Although there is no specific project management process for the creation of the
change management plan, it is created as part of the Develop Project Management Plan
process. Therefore, it would be best to review the ITTOs associated with the Develop
Project Management Plan process.
- **C The appropriate ITTOs will be listed with the Perform Integrated Change Control process**
Incorrect. Perform Integrated Change Control is the process of reviewing all change
requests; approving and managing changes to deliverables, project documents, and the
project management plan and communicating the decision. This process belongs to the
Monitoring and Controlling Process Group. The change management plan is created
during the Develop Project Management Plan process which is part of the Planning
Process Group. While some of the ITTO's may be similar for both processes, most are not
and serve different purposes.
- **D The project management office (PMO) provides the change management plan**
Incorrect. The PMO may supply an approved template for a change management plan, but
a PMO is not likely to provide the change management plan for a specific project. It is the
project manager's responsibility to develop the change management plan as part of project
planning.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 83-86, 88

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 113 of 200
Question ID: 612204
- **A change request on a project you are leading has just been approved. You communicate the**
tasks required to implement the change to the project team. A team member suggests an
alternative solution that departs from the approved change request but which reduces the time
and cost of implementing the change and still meets the scope and quality requirements.
What should you do?
- **A Reject the suggestion as gold plating and implement the exact steps as specified in the**
approved change request.
- **B Implement the alternative suggestion and update the relevant components of the project**
management plan.
- **C Refer to the change management plan for criteria whether the suggestion requires the**
approval of the change control board.
- **D Refer to the configuration management plan for guidance on whether the content of the**
change request remains consistent and operable.
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

When implementing a change request, how can the project manager know what to do next?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Approved change requests are outputs of the Perform Integrated Change Control process, and
inputs to the Direct and Manage Project Work process. The change management plan provides
for a responsible individual or party to review, evaluate, approve, defer, or reject change
requests. Either this plan or organizational procedures may authorize the project manager or
sponsor as the responsible party, or may formally charter a group to serve as the change control
board. The plan may also grant authority for the project manager to approve change requests

---

with a certain level of impact on the scope, schedule, budget, or quality or other constraints
before involving the sponsor or the change control board (if it exists).
Given an approved change request, the project manager has responsibility for implementing it as
specified. In this scenario, however, a suggestion that meets the project scope and quality
requirements but saves time and money in implementation should not be ignored. The change
management plan should guide the project manager to evaluate whether the effects of the
suggestion are significant enough (or unknown enough) to merit a new change request to be
evaluated. Perhaps the project manager has the authority to adjust the tactical approach during
implementation and may document the updates as needed in the change log. Of the choices
available, referring first to the change management plan before implementing the suggestion or
before submitting a revised change request is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reject the suggestion as gold plating and implement the exact steps as specified in the**
approved change request.
Incorrect. Gold plating refers to the practice of intentionally adding features or
functionalities that the customer did not request. According to the scenario, the team
member suggests an alternative to the solution specified in the change request, rather than
adding features or functionalities that the customer did not request. Rejecting the
potentially beneficial suggestion without evaluating it first may foster an environment that
devalues the expertise and creativity of the project team in favor of bureaucracy.
- **B Implement the alternative suggestion and update the relevant components of the project**
management plan.
Incorrect. Immediately implementing the alternative suggestion without consideration for
the change management policies and procedures can lead the team to sneak in
undocumented changes that fail to consider overall project objectives or plans.
- **C Refer to the change management plan for criteria whether the suggestion requires the**
approval of the change control board.
Correct. Given an approved change request, its preventive or corrective measures and
defect repairs should be implemented as the project work is being executed. However, it is
the responsibility of the project manager to make sure that the project resources are spent
efficiently. In this scenario, an alternative solution is suggested that may merit
consideration to save time and money in implementation. The change management plan
may grant the project manager the authority to approve change requests that meet certain

---

criteria, beyond which the suggestion requires re-evaluation of the change request by the
change control board.
- **D Refer to the configuration management plan for guidance on whether the content of the**
change request remains consistent and operable.
Incorrect. The configuration management plan defines which project artifacts need to be
formally controlled under change management procedures so that the project's resulting
product remains consistent and operable. It might be helpful to consult this plan to ensure
that the alternative solution does not negatively impact the product. However, the
configuration management plan would not provide guidance on the content of any specific
change request.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 93. 96, 115-120; see
also https://support.office.com/en-us/article/how-to-evaluate-project-change-requests-fc36f2bb-5
858-48fa-8fe9-fad4721fff6c

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 114 of 200
Question ID: 613689
- **A fellow project manager comes to you complaining about the amount of scope creep that she is**
experiencing in her project.
Which of the following is the most probable reason for her difficulties?
- **A Lack of historical records from past projects**
- **B Weak interpersonal and team skills**
- **C Lack of project exclusions in the scope statement**
- **D Insufficient test and evaluation documents**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Defining the scope is concerned with what is and is not included in the project.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The degree and level of detail of the scope statement determine how well the scope can be
controlled. The scope statement describes the project's deliverables in detail. Explicitly stating
what is out of scope, particularly where stakeholders requested scope and it was not approved,
helps manage stakeholders, and can reduce scope creep. Therefore, the scope creep mentioned in
this scenario is probably due to lack of project exclusions in the scope definition and is the best
answer.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Lack of historical records from past projects**
Incorrect. Historical records are most often used to develop cost estimates for a project.
This scenario is about scope creep, which is uncontrolled growth in a project's scope;
therefore, historical records would not be of assistance.
- **B Weak interpersonal and team skills**
Incorrect. One may argue that weak interpersonal and team skills are what causing the
project manager to be a "yes-man" who has troubles to say 'no' to uncontrolled changes
resulting in scope creep. While having strong interpersonal and team skills is helpful to any
individual, with proper scope planning and change management, even those with weak
skills will likely be able to address the situation described in the scenario.
- **C Lack of project exclusions in the scope statement**
Correct. An ideal scope statement would include what is in scope, as well as what is not.
Explicitly stating what is out of scope for a project, particularly the areas where people
have requested scope but where they were not approved, helps manage stakeholder
expectations and reduce scope creep.
- **D Insufficient test and evaluation documents**
Incorrect. The question is essentially asking about how to control the scope of the project.
Test and evaluation documents are an output of the Manage Quality process and are used
to evaluate the achievement of quality objectives rather than control the scope of the
project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 154, 168

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 115 of 200
Question ID: 612225
- **A project manager is leading a retrospective for a project that is running behind schedule and**
over budget. Feedback from the meeting suggests that the project manager was too focused on
problem-solving and operational issues and did not effectively inspire and motivate the project
team.
What could the project manager have done differently to have been more successful?
- **A Focused more on the bottom line**
- **B Spent more time developing the project team and providing a vision for project success**
- **C Directed the team using positional power**
- **D Emphasized the administrative aspects of the project**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager has been relying too heavily on managing the project rather than leading the
project team.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project manager has been relying too heavily on managing the
project rather than leading the project team. Project managers need to employ both leadership
and management and strike the right balance between them to be successful. Developing the
project team and providing a vision for success represents an emphasis on leadership. All of the
incorrect answer choices are examples of greater management rather than leadership. Therefore,
of the available options, the project manager could have spent more time developing the project
team and providing a vision for project success.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Focused more on the bottom line**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents a greater focus on management versus leadership.
The question suggests that the project manager needs to focus more on leadership and rely
less on management.
- **B Spent more time developing the project team and providing a vision for project success**
Correct. The question indicates that the project manager has been relying too heavily on
managing the project rather than leading the project team. Developing the project team
and providing a vision for success represents more of an emphasis on leadership.
- **C Directed the team using positional power**
Incorrect. Leadership emphasizes relational power over positional power. Directing using
positional power represents management over leadership, and the question implies that the
project manager needs to rely less on management and more on leadership.
- **D Emphasized the administrative aspects of the project**
Incorrect. The question suggests that the project manager needs to spend less time and
effort on managing the project and focus more on leading the project team. Emphasizing
the administrative aspects of the project is related to management and not leadership.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 64

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 116 of 200
Question ID: 612437
Due to an increase in actual costs that have not been accounted for in the original budget, the
project manager submits a change request to update the cost baseline. To support the request, the
project manager compiles all of the costs that have been authorized, incurred, invoiced, and paid.
What has the project manager compiled?
- **A Planned value**
- **B Earned value**
- **C Work performance information**
- **D Work performance data**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What are the raw observations and measurements identified during project activities?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Work performance data are the raw observations and measurements identified during activities
performed to carry out the project work. In the scenario, the project manager compiles all of the
costs, which have been authorized, incurred, invoiced, and paid. Those are best described as the
work performance data. Only after these raw data have been analyzed, will it become work
performance information. Therefore, what the project manager has compiled was the work
performance data.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Planned value**
Incorrect. Planned value is the authorized budget assigned to scheduled work. The question
describes costs that are incurred rather than the budget.
- **B Earned value**
Incorrect. Earned value is the measure of work performed expressed in terms of the budget
authorized for that work. The question is asking about costs and not earned value.
- **C Work performance information**
Incorrect. Work performance data, once analyzed, becomes work performance information.
The question indicates that the cost analysis has yet to be performed. Therefore, this choice
can be eliminated as a correct response.
- **D Work performance data**
Correct. Work performance data contains data on project status such as which costs have
been authorized, incurred, invoiced, and paid.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 26, 260

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 117 of 200
Question ID: 651319
Undertaking a project requires a business case to justify whether the project is worth the
investment.
Which is the best example of a business case?
- **A The operational budget is greater than previous years, and we must allocate those funds**
- **B Technology is constantly changing, and we must learn the latest tools**
- **C Carbon emissions can be reduced with the installation of filters on all current machines,**
and we can gain governmental environment certification
- **D Projects like this have been done in the past with great success, and we must have more**
successful projects this quarter
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Remember that business cases are from the perspective of the business and their strategies and
objectives.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

- **A business case is a reason and justification for a business to undertake and fund a project. The**
case to take on any project should fulfill the needs and objectives of the business. The goals of
the business vary from one business to the next; even within businesses, there are various cases
to take on projects. Whatever the case, there must be a legitimate, explicit outcome that can
feasibly achieve benefits for the business and its objectives. Of the available choices, only one
has all the characteristics of the valid business case, “Carbon emissions can be reduced with the
installation of filters on all current machines, and we can gain government environment
certification.”

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The operational budget is greater than previous years, and we must allocate those funds**
Incorrect. Costs are a part of a business case but not the only reason. Simply having money
does not warrant a business reason to spend the money.
- **B Technology is constantly changing, and we must learn the latest tools**
Incorrect. While knowing and recognizing that technology is changing might be of value, it
does not alone present a reason for the business to spend time, money, and resources on
learning the latest tools and other forms of technology.
- **C Carbon emissions can be reduced with the installation of filters on all current machines,**
and we can gain governmental environment certification
Correct. Addressing the carbon emissions via the project efforts presents a reason for the
business to undergo the project.
- **D Projects like this have been done in the past with great success, and we must have more**
successful projects this quarter
Incorrect. Having performed similar work in the past gives credence to the potential
success of a project, but it is not the reason from a business perspective for repeating a
similar project again.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 30-31
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 5
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 118 of 200
Question ID: 612306
In the absence of the project sponsor, you are leading a meeting with key stakeholders to aid in
the development of the project charter. At the beginning of the meeting, a stakeholder stalls the
meeting insisting on discussing an omission in the business case.
With the meeting at an impasse, what is your best course of action?
- **A Update the business case as necessary and proceed with the meeting**
- **B Postpone further discussion on the omission and move on to other items on the agenda**
- **C Submit a change request to document the omission in the project charter**
- **D Dismiss the participants, and reschedule the meeting once the sponsor is available**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which conflict management technique might allow the meeting to move forward?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that the Develop Project Charter process is underway. Interpersonal and
team skills including conflict management are among the tools and techniques associated with
this process. Withdraw/avoid is a conflict resolution technique which may include postponing the
issue to be better prepared or to be resolved by others. In this scenario, the project sponsor is not
in attendance at the meeting, but only the project sponsor has the responsibility for the creation
and maintenance of the business case. With the meeting at an impasse, the best course of action
is to postpone further discussion on the omission raised by the stakeholder and move on to other
items on the agenda until the project sponsor can be engaged to render a decision for the
modification of the business case.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Update the business case as necessary and proceed with the meeting**
Incorrect. A project manager may make recommendations but does not have the authority
to update the business case as it is not a project document.
- **B Postpone further discussion on the omission and move on to other items on the agenda**
Correct. In this situation, the omission in the business case will need to be addressed by the
project sponsor. Withdraw/avoid is a conflict resolution technique which may include
postponing the issue to be better prepared or to be resolved by others.
- **C Submit a change request to document the omission in the project charter**
Incorrect. This answer choice is incorrect for several reasons. First, the project is in
initiation; change requests are not necessary until the project has been baselined at the end
of project planning. Second, while the business case is an input to the project charter, it is
the business case and not the project charter that should be fixed (assuming the stakeholder
is correct). Third, even if the project was in execution and the project charter required an
update, such an update could have been done without a change request as the project
charter is not a controlled document. And lastly, project charters are rarely updated after
project planning begins. If needed, a project charter can be amended, but not updated.
- **D Dismiss the participants, and reschedule the meeting once the sponsor is available**
Incorrect. While this action represents a plausible option, it might be too extreme.
According to the scenario, the meeting has just started. Dismissing the participants at the
beginning of the meeting would be a waste of the project resources. Even if the issue raised
by the stakeholder would affect other elements of the project charter, continuing the
meeting may help discover additional issues, which in turn, would more effectively utilize
the time of the meeting participants and contribute to the project initiation efforts.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 29, 80 348-349

Question 119 of 200
Question ID: 612337
You have been commissioned by your company to propose a cost-efficient strategy for a new
leading-edge server farm. While researching options, you identify the power source to be a large
expense of maintaining servers.
You narrow the power source choices down to four options with the following attributes:
● Chemical energy has an investment of $1,000,000 and NPV of $200,000
● Solar energy has an investment of $1,500,000, a payback period of 3 years, and NPV of $350,000
● Wind energy has an investment of $2,000,000, a payback period of 3 years, and NPV of $100,000
● Thermal energy has an investment of $1,800,000 and NPV of $175,000
Which of these power options should you propose based on the net present value (NPV)?
Top of Form
- **A Chemical energy**
- **B Solar energy**
- **C Wind energy**
- **D Thermal energy**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

You should select the project with the highest value of the difference between the present value
of cash inflows and the present value of cash outflows.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**


---

The four options include extraneous information, namely the investment amount (which is
already factored into the NPV calculation), and the payback period (which is another type of
project selection technique that can be used by itself or along with NPV calculations). However,
the question clearly asks to base the answer on the NPV. You should, therefore, have keyed in
only on the term NPV when selecting the correct answer. The correct answer is 'solar energy,'
since its NPV is $350,000, which is the largest of all the answer choices.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Chemical energy**
Incorrect. Chemical energy has a lower NPV than solar energy, making this an incorrect
answer.
- **B Solar energy**
Correct. Solar energy has the highest NPV and is, therefore, the correct answer.
- **C Wind energy**
Incorrect. Wind energy has a lower NPV than solar energy, making this an incorrect
answer.
- **D Thermal energy**
Incorrect. Thermal energy has a lower NPV than solar energy, making this an incorrect
answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 33-34

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 120 of 200
Question ID: 612295
As a project manager, you contracted with another company to develop a smartphone app. The
company has demonstrated the completed app, and you have verified that it meets all technical
and quality requirements. Overall, you are pleased with the performance of the seller and plan to
use them again in the future.
Now that the project deliverables are complete, who is responsible for declaring the formal
closure of the procurement contract?
Top of Form
- **A The buyer is responsible for closing out the procurement contract.**
- **B The seller is responsible for closing out the procurement contract.**
- **C Both buyer and seller are mutually responsible for closing out the contract.**
- **D A procurement contract is considered closed when the deliverables are accepted.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who provides formal written notice that the contract has been completed?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The party that awards the contract is responsible for declaring its closure. The buyer, usually
through its authorized administrator, provides the seller with the formal written notice that the
contract has been completed. Procurement closure only occurs after the deliverables have been
accepted and transferred, all claims are settled, and final payments have been made.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The buyer is responsible for closing out the procurement contract.**
Correct. The buyer provides the seller with the formal written notice that the contract has
been completed.
- **B The seller is responsible for closing out the procurement contract.**
Incorrect. The seller does not close out the contract. The buyer closes out the contract and
sends formal written notice to the seller that the contract has been completed.
- **C Both buyer and seller are mutually responsible for closing out the contract.**
Incorrect. Both the buyer and seller are mutually bound by the terms of the contract, but it
is the buyer's responsibility to provide formal written notice of contract completion.
- **D A procurement contract is considered closed when the deliverables are accepted.**
Incorrect. The contract is not closed out when the deliverables are accepted. Any
outstanding claims should be settled, and final payment should be made before formal
procurement closure.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 499
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam 5

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 121 of 200
Question ID: 612622
You are in the execution stage of a corporate restructuring project in which the company's sales
managers will assume responsibility for certain operational aspects of the business in addition to
their role as sales leaders. The sales managers have repeatedly expressed concerns about the
impact of the project on their roles, and you need their support for the project to be successful.
What is the best course of action in this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Utilize conflict management skills to diffuse the conflict between the sales managers**
- **B Send the sales managers a copy of the team charter**
- **C Introduce the concept of co-creation**
- **D Replace the sales managers as necessary to ensure the success of the project**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Including the sales managers in the project team may address their concerns and build support
for the project.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

One of the trends and emerging practices for Project Stakeholder Management involves the
concept of co-creation. Co-creation places greater emphasis on including the affected
stakeholders on the team as a partner. Working in close collaboration with the stakeholders that
are most affected by the work or outcomes of the project can build support for the project and
improve the probability of a successful outcome. Of the available choices, the strategy that is

---

most likely to be effective in addressing the concerns of the sales managers and building support
for the project is to introduce the concept of co-creation with the sales managers.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Utilize conflict management skills to diffuse the conflict between the sales managers**
Incorrect. The question describes a situation where the sales managers are concerned
about the impact of the reorganization on their roles. There is no indication of conflict
between the sales managers.
- **B Send the sales managers a copy of the team charter**
Incorrect. The team charter is a document that records the team values, agreements, and
operating guidelines, as well as establishing clear expectations regarding acceptable
behavior by project team members. There is no indication from the question that the
behavior of the sales managers has not been acceptable. Expressing concerns about the
impact of the project should not be considered unacceptable behavior. Additionally, the
sales managers are stakeholders in this scenario and not members of the project team.
- **C Introduce the concept of co-creation**
Correct. Working in close collaboration with the stakeholders that are most affected by the
work or outcomes of the project can build support for the project and improve the
probability of a successful outcome for the project.
- **D Replace the sales managers as necessary to ensure the success of the project**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents an extreme action, and there is no information
presented by the question which suggests that replacing the sales managers is necessary at
this point. Additionally, it is highly unlikely that the project manager would have the
authority to replace the sales managers.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 505
