PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 122 of 200
Question ID: 625044
Both supportive and resistant stakeholders are influencing the project team and asking for
unapproved changes. You are more concerned about the resistant stakeholders and want to
determine if any unapproved features have been added to the project deliverables.
What is your best approach?
Top of Form
- **A Perform the Integrated Change Control process**
- **B Perform the Direct and Manage Project Work process**
- **C Perform the Control Scope process**
- **D Perform the Control Schedule process**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might you, as the project manager, address scope creep?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question implies that you, as the project manager, suspect that scope creep may be an issue
for the project. Scope creep represents the uncontrolled expansion to product or project scope
without adjustments to time, cost, and resources. The detection and prevention of scope creep
may be addressed in the Control Scope process. Hence, The Control Scope process should be
performed to detect any unapproved changes to the scope baseline. Once unauthorized changes
are found, the Perform Integrated Change Control process can be implemented. Therefore, in this
scenario, performing the Control Scope process is the best approach.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Perform the Integrated Change Control process**
Incorrect. Getting stakeholders to follow the integrated change control process helps
control scope, but the concern is uncontrolled scope issues, which means the stakeholders
are not following the Perform the Integrated Change Control process.
- **B Perform the Direct and Manage Project Work process**
Incorrect. The Direct and Manage Project Work process is for directing work and known
changes. Unfortunately, this process does not easily identify uncontrolled changes.
- **C Perform the Control Scope process**
Correct. The Control Scope process is the process of monitoring the status of the project
and product scope and managing changes to the scope baseline. The Control Scope process
has the tools and techniques to identify scope creep (uncontrolled changes).
- **D Perform the Control Schedule process**
Incorrect. The question suggests that the current concern is with scope creep, which are
controlled changes. Although scope creep may lead to schedule issues, the description in
the scenario indicates that the focus needs to be on potential scope issues.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 167-169

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 123 of 200
Question ID: 612454
You are identifying the specific actions that will be required to complete the project deliverables.
As part of this process, you have created a project document which describes portions of work to
be performed during the project. Each portion of work specified in the document has various
details such as leads and lags, imposed dates, constraints, assumptions, as well as logical
relationships.
Which project document have you created?
Top of Form
- **A Activity list**
- **B Activity attributes**
- **C Activity register**
- **D Milestone list**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which option extends the description of the activity by identifying multiple components
associated with each activity?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that you are carrying out the Define Activities process. The project
documents created during this process include the activity list, activity attributes, and milestone
list. Activity attributes include activity codes, predecessor activities, successor activities, logical
relationships, leads and lags, resource requirements, imposed dates, constraints, and assumptions.
The description provided by the question indicates that the activity attributes have been created.

---

Note, the question disguises the word ‘activities’ by providing its definition from the glossary of
the PMBOK® Guide which reads, “Activity. A distinct, scheduled portion of work performed
during the course of a project.”

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Activity list**
Incorrect. An activity list is a documented tabulation of schedule activities that shows the
activity description, activity identifier, and a sufficiently detailed scope of work description,
so project team members understand what work is to be performed. However, the activity
list does not describe the necessary sequence of events.
- **B Activity attributes**
Correct. Activity attributes include activity codes, predecessor activities, successor
activities, logical relationships, leads and lags, resource requirements, imposed dates,
constraints, and assumptions.
- **C Activity register**
Incorrect. ‘Activity register’ is a made-up term.
- **D Milestone list**
Incorrect. A milestone list is a significant point or event in a project. Although a milestone
list may contain a sequence of important events, it does not describe the logical
relationships between activities.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 186

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 124 of 200
Question ID: 613231
As the project manager acquires the aluminum for a project to construct a new airliner, a tariff is
enacted which raises the cost by 30%. Although the overall project budget will not be affected,
the existing contingency reserves are inadequate to cover the increased cost, and the project
manager needs to access the management reserves.
What should the project manager do next?
Top of Form
- **A Submit a change request to transfer the management reserves into the contingency reserves**
- **B Submit a change request to transfer the management reserves into the cost baseline**
- **C Access the management reserves since the project budget is not affected**
- **D Request the project sponsor to provide additional funds for the project**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Management reserves are not included in the cost baseline.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that during the Acquire Resources process, a significant increase in
material costs have exceeded the contingency reserves for the project and the project manager
needs to access the management reserves. The management reserves are part of the project
budget but are not included in the cost baseline. An approved change request is required to
transfer the management reserves into the cost baseline. Even though the project budget will not
be affected, any change to a baseline first requires an approved change request. Therefore, a

---

change request first needs to be submitted and approved before the management reserves can be
transferred to the cost baseline, and that is what the project manager should do next.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Submit a change request to transfer the management reserves into the contingency**
reserves
Incorrect. The cost baseline is comprised of two components, the work package cost
estimates, and the contingency reserves. When the management reserves are required to
fund unforeseen work, they are transferred into the cost baseline as a whole and not
particularly to one of its components. It is reasonable to assume that if the existing
contingency reserves are inadequate to cover the increased cost, then the part of the
management reserves transferred to the cost baseline would serve, together with the
existing contingency reserves and the work package cost estimates, as the overall funds
necessary to cover the project costs needed to proceed with the project.
- **B Submit a change request to transfer the management reserves into the cost baseline**
Correct. An approved change request is required to transfer the management reserves into
the cost baseline. Even though the project budget will not be affected, any change to a
baseline first requires an approved change request.
- **C Access the management reserves since the project budget is not affected**
Incorrect. The management reserves are part of the project budget but are not included in
the cost baseline. Therefore, a change request needs to be submitted and approved before
the management reserves can be transferred to the cost baseline.
- **D Request the project sponsor to provide additional funds for the project**
Incorrect. Additional funds are already available in the form of management reserves.
However, management reserves are not included in the cost baseline. The project manager
just needs an approved change request to access the management reserves; therefore, there
is no reason to ask the project sponsor for the additional funds.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 254-255, 334

Question 125 of 200
Question ID: 612308
To reduce potential conflict and increase productivity, the project manager creates a team charter
with clear expectations of acceptable behavior and diligently enforces the terms of the charter.
Despite these efforts, team conflict has become a significant issue and threatens the successful
completion of the project.
What could the project manager have done differently to avoid this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Have the human resources department provide a preapproved team charter**
- **B Allow the project team to develop the team charter**
- **C Conduct more frequent performance appraisals**
- **D Create a team member of the month award**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who should develop the team charter?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question describes a situation where the project manager developed, implemented, and
enforced the team charter. The team charter works best when the team develops it or at least has
an opportunity to contribute to it. Additionally, all project team members share responsibility for
ensuring the rules documented in the team charter are followed. Of the available options,
allowing the project team to develop the team charter provides the best way to avoid team
conflict.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Have the human resources department provide a preapproved team charter**
Incorrect. Using a preapproved team charter suggests that it was not developed to address
the unique needs of a specific project team, and it is likely to be less effective as a result.
- **B Allow the project team to develop the team charter**
Correct. The team charter works best when the team develops it or at least has an
opportunity to contribute to it. Additionally, all project team members share responsibility
for ensuring the rules documented in the team charter are followed.
- **C Conduct more frequent performance appraisals**
Incorrect. It is not known from the question how often performance appraisals are being
conducted. Therefore, it is not possible to determine if a gap exists in the frequency of
performance appraisals. Additionally, performance appraisals are a reactive measure and
unlikely to have prevented the conflict described by the question.
- **D Create a team member of the month award**
Incorrect. Incentives can influence team productivity but are unlikely to prevent team
conflict.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 319, 320, 348

Question 126 of 200
Question ID: 651310
In a meeting with a project stakeholder, the stakeholder explains why she has not been engaged
with the project as expected. You meet with her in her office. You take notes, ask some clarifying
questions, and demonstrate attentiveness through body language, and capturing her input.
What interpersonal skill are you leveraging in this exchange?
Top of Form
- **A Passive listening**
- **B Cultural awareness**
- **C Political awareness**
- **D Active listening**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Are you engaging with the stakeholder?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Active listening is a powerful interpersonal skill of project managers. It is an important tool and
technique when monitoring stakeholder engagement. The ability to take an active role in
listening to others and ensuring you have heard them properly and their message reduces
miscommunication and misunderstandings. By listening intently and following up with
clarification and discussion, you are taking an active role in listening and capturing the
communication between you and the stakeholder.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Passive listening**
Incorrect. If you were passively listening to the stakeholder, you would not take any action
to communicate to your stakeholder that you are capturing and understanding what you are
hearing. In this situation, you are actively demonstrating to your stakeholder that you are
not simply listening but taking an active role in consuming the information and making sure
the message was received and understood.
- **B Cultural awareness**
Incorrect. Although there may be cultural aspects to this encounter, none were discussed or
provided as behavior in this exchange.
- **C Political awareness**
Incorrect. Although there may be political aspects to this encounter, none of those were
discussed or provided as behavior in this exchange.
- **D Active listening**
Correct. The behaviors and actions demonstrated in this scenario are examples of active
listening.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 534

Question 127 of 200
Question ID: 612084
Where would you look to find what activities should be performed to close out contracts on your
project?
Top of Form
- **A Enterprise environmental factors**
- **B Resource management plan**
- **C Project management plan**
- **D Procurement documentation**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where would you find the procurement management plan?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question surrounds the Control Procurements process which is the process of managing
procurement relationships; monitoring contract performance, and making changes and
corrections as appropriate; and closing out contracts. The activities to be performed during this
process are described in the procurement management plan. This plan is a component of the
project management plan. Therefore, to understand what activities should be performed to close
out contracts on your project, you should review the project management plan.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Enterprise environmental factors**
Incorrect. Enterprise environmental factors (EEFs) are conditions, not under the immediate
control of the team, that influence, constrain, or direct the project, program, or portfolio.
While the EEFs are inputs to the Control Procurements process described in the question,
they do not specify activities that should be performed to close out contracts on your
project.
- **B Resource management plan**
Incorrect. The resource management plan is the component of the project management plan
that describes how project resources are acquired, allocated, monitored, and controlled.
The resource management plan does not have information on closing procurements.
- **C Project management plan**
Correct. The procurement management plan contains the activities to be performed during
the Control Procurement process. Closing out contracts is one of these activities. Since the
procurement management plan is a component of the project management plan, looking at
the latter is what you should do to find what activities should be performed to close out
contracts on your project.
- **D Procurement documentation**
Incorrect. Procurement documentation is an input to the Control Procurements process
described in the scenario. Procurement documentation contains complete supporting
records for the administration of the procurement processes. However, this documentation
does not specify activities that should be performed to close out contracts on your project.

Question 128 of 200
Question ID: 612356
You are drafting a project charter. In order to solicit the required feedback from each department,
you are planning to invite all of the functional leaders to attend a meeting except for the director
of human resources, since that position is currently vacant.
What is your best course of action in preparation for the meeting?
Top of Form
- **A Schedule the meeting without human resources representation**
- **B Invite a designated human resources representative to attend**
- **C Delay the meeting until a new director of human resources is named**
- **D Terminate the project**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might effective meeting management provide a solution to the problem?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that the project charter is being developed, and feedback is required from
each department, but the director of human resources position is currently vacant. The solution to
this problem can be provided by effective meeting management, which is one of the
interpersonal and team skills associated with the Develop Project Charter process. Meeting
management includes preparing the agenda, ensuring that a representative for each key
stakeholder group is invited, and preparing and sending the follow-up minutes and actions.

---

Therefore, among the available options, the best course of action is to identify and invite a
qualified individual to represent the human resources department at the meeting.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Schedule the meeting without human resources representation**
Incorrect. Excluding the human resources department from the project at this point may
have unintended consequences later in the project. In this case, the question states that
feedback is required from each department, so continuing without representation from the
human resources department is not a viable option.
- **B Invite a designated human resources representative to attend**
Correct. If representation is required from each department, as indicated in the question,
you, as the project manager, will need to identify a qualified individual to represent the
human resources department.
- **C Delay the meeting until a new director of human resources is named**
Incorrect. While delaying the meeting is a plausible option, there is not enough information
in the question to determine when the new director of human resources is named. Therefore,
delaying the meeting until further notice may unnecessarily delay the project. Seeking to
find another representative of the human resources department to attend the meeting would
be a better solution.
- **D Terminate the project**
Incorrect. Terminating the project is an overreaction to the problem described by the
question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 80

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 129 of 200
Question ID: 612631
The performing organization requires the use of a change control board (CCB) for all projects.
An influential stakeholder has complained about his requested changes not getting implemented
even when using the established change control procedures.
What should the project manager do first?
Top of Form
- **A Record the information in the change log**
- **B Capture the concern in the stakeholder register**
- **C Investigate the issue on behalf of the stakeholder**
- **D Add the stakeholder's complaint to the issue log**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where is information about problems encountered on the project recorded and monitored?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

In this scenario, a stakeholder has raised a concern which needs to be addressed. Any project or
stakeholder concerns are documented in the issue log, as well as any assigned action items
associated with managing the issue. The issue log will help the project manager effectively track
and manage issues, ensuring that they are investigated and resolved. In this case, it is not known
why the stakeholder's requests have not been implemented. Perhaps the change requests were
denied, or they might be scheduled to be implemented later in the project. The issue will need to
be investigated, resolved, and then communicated back to the stakeholder. Of the available
choices, the stakeholder's issue should first be captured in the issue log to ensure it is tracked and

---

monitored until it can be resolved. Note, an issue log is an input to the Manage Stakeholder
Engagement process described in the scenario. Updates to the issue log are among the outputs
from that process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Record the information in the change log**
Incorrect. A change log is a comprehensive list of changes submitted during the project and
their current status. The project manager will want to refer to the change log in this
scenario to see the status of the change requests that were submitted by the stakeholder.
However, the project manager should first record the issue in the issue log to ensure it is
effectively tracked and monitored.
- **B Capture the concern in the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is a project document including the identification,
assessment, and classification of project stakeholders. Any concerns raised by stakeholders
should be captured in the issue log, not the stakeholder register, where they can be tracked
and monitored.
- **C Investigate the issue on behalf of the stakeholder**
Incorrect. The issue raised by the stakeholder will need to be investigated. However, the
question is asking what should be done first, and the issue should be documented in the
issue before it is investigated. The issue log will help the project manager effectively track
and manage issues, ensuring that they are investigated and resolved.
- **D Add the stakeholder's complaint to the issue log**
Correct. Any project or stakeholder concerns are documented in the issue log, as well as
any assigned action items associated with managing the issue.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 96, 525, 529

PMP Exam 5

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 130 of 200
Question ID: 612429
Due to the complexity of a project, representatives from various departments of your company
are invited to participate in seller proposal evaluation including Finance, Real Estate,
Engineering, and Sales and Marketing.
Based on this situation, what tool or technique are you using?
Top of Form
- **A Make-or-buy analysis**
- **B Bidder conferences**
- **C Source selection criteria**
- **D Expert judgment**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The seller proposals are being evaluated by a multi-disciplinary committee with expertise in
different areas.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question describes the evaluation of seller proposals by a multi-disciplinary committee with
expertise in different areas. Expert judgment is judgment provided based upon expertise in an
application area, knowledge area, discipline, industry, etc., as appropriate for the activity being
performed. Such expertise may be provided by any group or person with specialized education,
knowledge, skill, experience, or training. The inclusion of representatives from various
departments to evaluate seller proposals is an example of using expert judgment.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Make-or-buy analysis**
Incorrect. Make-or-buy analysis is the process of gathering and organizing data about
product requirements and analyzing them against available alternatives including the
purchase or internal manufacture of the product. The question only refers to proposal
evaluation and not whether or not the deliverables should be produced internally.
- **B Bidder conferences**
Incorrect. Bidder conferences are meetings between the buyer and prospective sellers
before proposal submittal, and the evaluation of the seller proposals can only occur after
submittal.
- **C Source selection criteria**
Incorrect. Source selection criteria describe how bidder proposals will be evaluated,
including evaluation criteria and weights. Whereas, the question is describing the inclusion
of individuals with specialized expertise. Additionally, source selection criteria are part of
the procurement documentation and not a tool or technique.
- **D Expert judgment**
Correct. Expert judgment is judgment provided based upon expertise in an application
area, knowledge area, discipline, industry, etc., as appropriate for the activity being
performed. Such expertise may be provided by any group or person with specialized
education, knowledge, skill, experience, or training. The inclusion of representatives from
various departments to evaluate seller proposals is an example of using expert judgment.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 487

Question 131 of 200
Question ID: 612193
Working for a company with an organizational structure type that is best described as organic or
simple, you have been assigned a project to replace the computers at a retail store. All you need
to complete the project on time is for the company's information technology (IT) specialist to
load the required software, but this individual states that they are busy with another project.
With the deadline now in jeopardy, what is your best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Approve overtime for the IT specialist to complete the software update**
- **B Direct the IT specialist to prioritize your project over the other project**
- **C Escalate the issue to the owner**
- **D Discuss the situation with the project management office (PMO)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

- **A project manager has little or no authority within an organic or simple organizational structure**
type.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question describes a company with an organizational structure type of organic or simple. In
this environment, the project manager is better described as a project coordinator and has little or
authority over the project. In this situation, the owner or operator controls the budget and project
resources. Therefore, the only viable option for you, as the project manager, is to escalate the
issue to the owner.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Approve overtime for the IT specialist to complete the software update**
Incorrect. Within an organic or simple organizational structure, the project manager does
not have control over the project budget. Therefore, you, as the project manager, would not
be able to approve the overtime for the IT specialist.
- **B Direct the IT specialist to prioritize your project over the other project**
Incorrect. The question states that the company has an organic or simple organizational
structure type. The project manager within this organizational structure has little or no
control over resources. It is not likely that you, as the project manager, have the authority
to direct the IT specialist to prioritize your project over the other project.
- **C Escalate the issue to the owner**
Correct. With an organic or simple organizational structure, the project manager has little
or no authority. In this situation, the owner or operator controls the budget and project
resources.
- **D Discuss the situation with the project management office (PMO)**
Incorrect. The question indicates that the company has an organic or simple organizational
structure rather than PMO organizational structure type. Therefore, there is no PMO in this
scenario.

Question 132 of 200
Question ID: 610009
The project team reports that they have finished creating the requirements management plan, the
requirements documentation, and the requirements traceability matrix. The team informs that
they are going to start working on the project work breakdown structure (WBS) next.
What has the project team forgotten to do?
Top of Form
- **A Create the project scope statement**
- **B Complete the project management plan**
- **C Update the lessons learned register**
- **D Perform the Validate Scope process**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What output of the Define Scope process is missing?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

In the scenario described, the project team has completed the requirements management plan,
which is an output of the Plan Scope Management process. Additionally, the team has completed
the requirements documentation and requirements traceability matrix, which are outputs of the
Collect Requirements process. The next step in the Planning Process Group is the Define Scope
process and the creation of the project scope statement. Before creating the WBS, the project
scope must be well defined and documented in the project scope statement. The completed
project scope statement sets the boundaries for the project by defining the work that is included
in the project as well as the work excluded from the project. The project scope statement serves

---

as a guide when creating the WBS and should be completed before work begins on the WBS.
The project team wants to move on to creating the WBS, but they have forgotten that they need
to create the project scope statement before the WBS can be created.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Create the project scope statement**
Correct. According to the scenario, the project team is in the Planning Process Group of
the Project Scope Management Knowledge Area. The requirements documentation and the
requirements traceability matrix are both outputs of the Collect Requirements process;
therefore, the team has completed the Collect Requirements process. The next step in the
Planning Process Group would be the Define Scope process. The project scope statement is
an output of the Define Scope process and should be completed before proceeding to the
Create WBS process.
- **B Complete the project management plan**
Incorrect. In the scenario described, the team has completed the requirements management
plan which is an output of the Plan Scope Management process. The requirements
management plan is one of the components of the project management plan. Therefore, it is
not possible to complete the project management plan before creating the requirements
management plan.
- **C Update the lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register is a project document that captures knowledge
gained in the project. The project team is supposed to benefit from this knowledge to
improve further project performance. There is not enough information in the question to
determine what beneficial knowledge has been gained during the development of the
project artifacts described in the scenario.
- **D Perform the Validate Scope process**
Incorrect. The scenario states the project is still in the planning stage; therefore, in the
Planning Process Group. The Validate Scope process is part of the Monitoring and
Controlling Process Group. The project planning must be completed, and execution
underway before the project would be in the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group.
Therefore, performing the Validate Scope process is not what the team forgot.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 154, 157

PMP Exam 5

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 133 of 200
Question ID: 613717
- **A company needs to purchase a 3D printer for a project in the planning stage. The project**
manager assigns a project team member to be responsible for acquiring the 3D printer while two
other team members will be trained on operation and maintenance and can then be consulted
when needed.
What tool or technique is most useful in documenting these responsibilities for future reference?
Top of Form
- **A Requirements traceability matrix**
- **B Project team directory**
- **C RACI chart**
- **D Probability and impact matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is a common type of responsibility assignment matrix (RAM)?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Plan Resource Management process is being carried out, and a
responsibility assignment matrix (RAM) is one of the tools associated with this process. A RACI
chart is a common type of RAM that uses responsible, accountable, consult, and inform statuses
to define the involvement of stakeholders in project activities. In the scenario described,
activities such as acquiring the 3D printer, training to operate and maintain the printer, etc., are
shown in the left column, while the roles and responsibilities of the team members assigned to

---

these activities are shown in rows. Therefore, a RACI chart is the best tool for documenting the
responsibilities for future reference.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. The requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links product requirements
from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them. The requirements traceability matrix
does not have responsibility assignments for project activities.
- **B Project team directory**
Incorrect. The project team directory is a documented list of project team members, their
project roles, and communication information. However, the project team directory does
not have activity level assignments.
- **C RACI chart**
Correct. A RACI chart is a common type of responsibility assignment matrix that uses
responsible, accountable, consult, and inform statuses to define the involvement of
stakeholders in project activities.
- **D Probability and impact matrix**
Incorrect. The probability and impact matrix is a grid for mapping the probability of
occurrence of each risk and its impact on project objectives if that risk occurs. The question
is asking about activity level responsibilities rather than project risks.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 317

Question 134 of 200
Question ID: 613754
The project manager has scheduled individual discussions with experienced project participants,
stakeholders, and subject matter experts. The purpose of these discussions is to obtain a
comprehensive list of individual project risks and sources of overall project risk.
Which tool or technique is the project manager utilizing in this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Risk register**
- **B Risk abatement**
- **C Brainstorming**
- **D Interviews**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What data gathering technique utilizes individual discussions during the Identify Risks process to
produce a comprehensive list of individual project risks and sources of overall project risk?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question states that the project is in the planning stage and implies that the project team is
performing the project management process of Identify Risks. The interview is one of the tools
and techniques used during the Identify Risks process. The purpose of interviews during the
Identify Risks process is to obtain a comprehensive list of individual project risks and sources of
overall project risk. The interview is the data gathering technique that is being utilized by the
project manager.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a repository that contains details of identified project risks.
The question implies that the project manager is performing the project management
process of Identify Risks and is asking for a tool or technique associated with this process.
The risk register is an output of the Identify Risks process and not a tool or technique.
- **B Risk abatement**
Incorrect. 'Risk abatement' is a fake term made up for this question.
- **C Brainstorming**
Incorrect. While brainstorming is one of the tools and techniques of the Identify Risks
process, brainstorming is typically conducted as a meeting with multiple participants. In
the scenario described, the project manager is conducting individual discussions, making
this choice an incorrect answer.
- **D Interviews**
Correct. Interviews is a technique used in the project management process of Identify Risks.
The purpose of the interviews during the Identify Risks process is to obtain a
comprehensive list of individual project risks and sources of overall project risk.

Question 135 of 200
Question ID: 613688
Some stakeholders are disappointed that not all of their needs were included in the final
requirements documentation. A senior project manager suggests using a document that relates
the planned capabilities with the business objective that each capability satisfies. This document
would demonstrate how each requirement adds business value.
To what type of document is the senior project manager referring?
Top of Form
- **A Requirements traceability matrix (RTM)**
- **B Requirements register**
- **C Requirements management plan**
- **D Context diagram**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

- **A grid that links product requirements to the business objectives that satisfy them.**
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The RTM is a grid that links the product requirements to the business objectives. It provides a
means to track requirements throughout the project lifecycle helping to ensure that requirements
approved in the requirements documentation are delivered at the end of the project. Using an
RTM will assist in ensuring and showing that each requirement adds business value by linking it
to the business and project objectives. Each requirement has attributes associated with it that help
to define the requirement further. One of the attributes that can be used is the owner of the

---

requirement, who will manage it throughout the project. Based on the scenario described, the
RTM is the document to which the senior project manager was referring.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Requirements traceability matrix (RTM)**
Correct. The RTM is a grid that links the product requirements to the business objectives.
Each requirement has attributes associated with it that help to define the requirement
further. One of the attributes that can be used is the owner of the requirement, who will
manage it throughout the project, making this the correct answer.
- **B Requirements register**
Incorrect. 'Requirements register' is a made-up term for this question.
- **C Requirements management plan**
Incorrect. The requirements management plan is an output from the Plan Scope
Management process that describes how requirements will be collected, analyzed,
documented, and managed. In this scenario, you have already obtained the requirements.
The senior project manager has suggested a way to track the requirements throughout the
project rather than plan them.
- **D Context diagram**
Incorrect. Context diagrams visually depict the product scope and the data flow when
people, other systems, and processes interact with it. It is an example of a scope model and
is a technique used in the Collect Requirements process rather than a document used to
track requirements.

Question 136 of 200
Question ID: 613113
You took over a project in execution to build a new marine radar system. The project has
proceeded smoothly until the quality inspection team reports that most of the high voltage test
equipment is badly corroded and will need to be replaced. You remember your predecessor
mentioning a surprisingly inexpensive solution for a similar problem earlier in the project.
Where should you look for the details of this solution?
Top of Form
- **A Organizational process assets**
- **B Resource breakdown structure**
- **C Risk management plan**
- **D Issue log**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where is the repository for the current project's problems?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

According to the scenario, you are looking for a solution that helped resolve a similar issue
earlier in the project. This implies you are carrying out the Manage Quality process. The issue
log helps the project manager effectively track and manage issues, and it will typically include
the details about issues encountered throughout the project. This may include the issue type, who
raised it, date/time, description, priority, who the issue was assigned to, status, and the final
solution. Therefore, assuming the previous project manager carried out the project using sound

---

project management practices, the issue log is supposed to include the details of the solution you
are looking for.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Organizational process assets**
Incorrect. Organizational process assets may include artifacts such as the lessons learned
repository, which, in turn, may contain detailed information on issues and solutions.
However, the information captured in the lessons learned repository belongs to previous
projects and company activities, not the current project.
- **B Resource breakdown structure**
Incorrect. The resource breakdown structure provides a hierarchical structure of resources
by category and type. It does not include information about issues and solutions.
- **C Risk management plan**
Incorrect. The risk management plan describes how risk activities will be planned on the
project but does not include details about individual risks, issues, and solutions that come
up during the project.
- **D Issue log**
Correct. The issue log is a project document that may help effectively track and manage
issues. It typically includes the issue description and final solution, making this choice the
best answer to the question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 297, 96

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 137 of 200
Question ID: 612728
You hold a video conference with the stakeholders and the development team to demonstrate the
product increment completed during the last iteration. A stakeholder brings up a concern
regarding the functionality of the application. To ensure you understand the concern, you are
using active listening techniques.
Which of the following quotes from the video conference illustrates the active listening skill of
confirming understanding?
Top of Form
- **A "Thank you for bringing up that concern. Good catch."**
- **B "When you said you couldn't tell if the application was doing anything, did you mean that the**
page took too long to respond to your click?"
- **C "It sounds like what you're looking for with the page transition is a loading animation to show that**
the system is working on it. Am I correct?"
- **D "We are having trouble hearing. There is background noise. Andy, is that you taking notes? Could**
you please mute your microphone?"
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Techniques of active listening involve acknowledging, clarifying and confirming, understanding,
and removing barriers that adversely affect comprehension.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Techniques of active listening involve acknowledging, clarifying and confirming, understanding,
and removing barriers that adversely affect comprehension. Of the choices, the only one that

---

demonstrates confirming understanding is one that reflects the meaning of what was heard, "It
sounds like what you're looking for with the page transition is a loading animation to show that
the system is working on it" and invites correction or verification, "Am I correct?"

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A "Thank you for bringing up that concern. Good catch."**
Incorrect. This is an example of active listening that models acknowledgment. A verbal or
textual acknowledgment that what was said was heard can defuse emotions when the
sender is upset. An acknowledgment is especially important in a text message, email, or
audio exchange where eye contact cannot establish a signal that the recipient is engaged in
the exchange. However, the scenario describes a video conference where eye contact can be
established, making this choice an incorrect answer.
- **B "When you said you couldn't tell if the application was doing anything, did you mean that**
the page took too long to respond to your click?"
Incorrect. This is an example of active listening that models clarifying. The recipient of a
message may need additional detail to respond appropriately. Questions are used to clarify
and create a more accurate picture. These questions may ask for more specific examples or
ask for related details involving the 5 Ws and the H: who, what, when, where, why, and
how.
- **C "It sounds like what you're looking for with the page transition is a loading animation to**
show that the system is working on it. Am I correct?"
Correct. This is an example of active listening that models confirming understanding. It
reflects or mirrors the general meaning and significance of what was heard, frequently by
paraphrasing. These thoughtful responses are usually prefaced by phrases such as "it
sounds like", "if I understand you correctly", or "correct me if I'm wrong", and invites
confirmation or corrective feedback, such as "am I correct?"
- **D "We are having trouble hearing. There is background noise. Andy, is that you taking**
notes? Could you please mute your microphone?"
Incorrect. This answer choice describes active listening that models removing barriers that
adversely affect comprehension. This example is specific to audible distractions, which may
also include closing a door or window to minimize outside noise, hanging up and calling
again to minimize noise on the phone conference line, or asking other attendees to save
side conversations for after the meeting. Other examples may be to remove visual
distractions, such as showing a slideshow in full screen rather than with a computer's
toolbars showing. Other examples may remove psychological barriers to comprehension,

---

such as setting a norm that everyone in the group will take an open-minded approach to the
exchange without prejudice. Other examples may remove language barriers to
comprehension, including having translators available when needed.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 386; See
also https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Active_listening; see
also https://www.pmi.org/learning/library/good-communication-engaged-mindset-project-tips-21
91

Question 138 of 200
Question ID: 612078
To create the project schedule, a project manager needs to break down the project scope and
develop a comprehensive list of activities, which are needed to complete the deliverable.
What tool or technique should project manager use in this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Work breakdown structure**
- **B Decomposition**
- **C Progressive elaboration**
- **D Gold plating**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What tool or technique is used for dividing and subdividing the project scope during the Define
Activities process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Define Activities process is being carried out, and decomposition is
one of the tools and techniques used during this process. Decomposition is a technique used for
dividing and subdividing the project scope and project deliverables into smaller, more
manageable parts. Decomposition is the technique that is being used to create the activity list as
indicated by the question.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work breakdown structure**
Incorrect. The work breakdown structure (WBS) is a hierarchical decomposition of the total
scope of work to be carried out by the project team to create the required deliverables. The
WBS is part of the scope baseline and is not a tool or technique.
- **B Decomposition**
Correct. Decomposition is a technique used for dividing and subdividing the project scope
and project deliverables into smaller, more manageable parts. Decomposition is used to
build the WBS and the activity list when defining the project’s scope.
- **C Progressive elaboration**
Incorrect. Progressive elaboration is the iterative process of increasing the level of detail in
a project management plan as greater amounts of information, and more accurate
estimates become available. The question describes the process of creating an activity list
rather than the project management plan.
- **D Gold plating**
Incorrect. Gold plating refers to the practice of adding features or functionalities that the
customer did not request. Gold plating is considered a bad practice for project
management. There is not enough information in the question to determine that gold
plating is taking place.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 185

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 139 of 200
Question ID: 651301
- **A new project was chartered. As the project manager, you meet with some of the pre-assigned**
team members to look over the problems the project seeks to address. The project team feels the
requirements provided are vague and unclear.
What is the project manager's next best action?
Top of Form
- **A Assign accountability of the various requirements to each project team member**
- **B Facilitate a benchmarking session to collect more detailed requirements**
- **C Facilitate a discussion meeting between the project team and the customer**
- **D Take responsibility as project manager to rewrite the requirements with more clarity**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What does the team need?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Understanding the needs, wants, expectations, and requirements is extremely important for the
project team to plan and manage the project to address those needs appropriately. The one best
qualified to express those needs is the customer, or a suitable customer representative or business
analyst. In the options provided to you in the question, the customer is an option. That is the
project manager's best source. Clarifying the requirements and gaining more definition from the
customer allows the project team to better fulfill those requirements. Including suitable members
of the team eliminates misinterpretation and unanswered questions. Educating more of the team

---

on the needs and the problems to solve enables the project team to better comprehend the
requirements and customer need.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Assign accountability of the various requirements to each project team member**
Incorrect. What is gained from assigning accountability to requirements that are not
well-understood or fleshed out? Assigning responsibility for requirements is better suited
after acquiring stakeholders’ better grasp and understand the project requirements. Then
the data in a requirements traceability matrix better aligns the team member, role, or group
to own the requirement with the skill set and ability to deliver.
- **B Facilitate a benchmarking session to collect more detailed requirements**
Incorrect. More information and clarity is being sought by the project team. Nonetheless,
the data gathering technique of benchmarking is not optimal at this point. More
information about the business need and the customer need and expectations should be
sought before comparing those needs to others. The project manager and the team could be
comparing the wrong targets, assumptions, and/or objectives.
- **C Facilitate a discussion meeting between the project team and the customer**
Correct. One must understand project requirements before knowing how to best approach,
manage, and satisfy them. Holding discussions or information seeking sessions with those
most knowledgeable about the requirements is the best place to start. These could be
subject matter experts, the project sponsor, the customer, or a customer representative with
enough ability and (ideally) authority to speak to the requirements.
- **D Take responsibility as project manager to rewrite the requirements with more clarity**
Incorrect. Rewriting unclear requirements without gaining and gathering more clarity does
not resolve the issue. There can be no assumptions that the project manager understands
the requirements better than the customer. To satisfy customer needs via project delivery,
the project manager and team must understand the project needs. Acting on assumptions
and personal impressions is unlikely to yield optimal results.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 138-142

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 140 of 200
Question ID: 613759
During risk planning, a project manager collects historical information from past projects and
populates the risk register with all the risks she can identify. She then records which team
member will be the risk owner for which risk. In reviewing the risk register, the project sponsor
says that the project manager made a critical mistake and should rethink her entire risk
identification process.
What is the best corrective action for the project manager to take at this point?
Top of Form
- **A Create a risk response plan before going to the project sponsor again**
- **B Include the project team and other key stakeholders in the risk identification process**
- **C Create a risk report to share with the project sponsor**
- **D Ask project team members to volunteer as risk owners, rather than to assign them, as a way to get**
buy-in
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which approach increases the likelihood that all potential project risks will be identified?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Project stakeholders should be encouraged to participate in risk identification activities. This
activity makes it more likely that all project risks will be identified and helps project teams
develop and maintain a sense of ownership and responsibility for identified project risks and
their associated risk response actions. If a project manager creates the risk register without input

---

from subject matter experts, project team members, or other stakeholders, it creates additional
risks for the project that could jeopardize its success.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Create a risk response plan before going to the project sponsor again**
Incorrect. Though potential risk responses can be identified and recorded in the risk
register during the Identify Risks process, risk responses are typically identified or
confirmed during the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process. As such, it is not
necessary to have a risk response plan already developed before approaching the project
sponsor.
- **B Include the project team and other key stakeholders in the risk identification process**
Correct. Project stakeholders should be encouraged to participate in risk identification
activities. This makes it more likely that all project risks will be identified and helps project
teams develop and maintain a sense of ownership and responsibility for identified project
risks and their associated risk response actions. In this scenario, the project manager
developed the risk register on her own, without input from her project team or other
stakeholders – a mistake that could seriously jeopardize the success of her project.
Therefore, her best course of action is to invite her project team and other stakeholders to
participate in the development of the risk register.
- **C Create a risk report to share with the project sponsor**
Incorrect. The risk report is an output of the Identify Risks process that presents
information on sources of overall project risk, together with summary information on
identified project risks. However, the risk report is developed progressively throughout the
project risk management process and, therefore, would not be something the project
manager in this scenario should have completed at this stage. Besides, creating a risk
report for the project sponsor does not address the real problem, which is that project
stakeholders were not included in the risk identification process.
- **D Ask project team members to volunteer as risk owners, rather than to assign them, as a**
way to get buy-in
Incorrect. Although there is nothing wrong with letting project team members self-select as
risk owners, this is not always feasible or appropriate. A project manager has the authority
to identify risk owners. When a potential risk owner has been identified during the Identify
Risks process, it should be recorded in the risk register, as the project manager has done in
this scenario.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 411, 414-418
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 141 of 200
Question ID: 650107
To manage workflow on a software development project, you are using a Kanban board with
strict work in progress (WIP) limits to expose bottlenecks. During project execution, one of the
developers leaves the project, and you need to backfill the position.
In searching for a replacement developer, which of the following characteristics would be of
greatest value to the team in this project environment?
Top of Form
- **A Experience with traditional project management**
- **B Expertise in manual and automatic testing**
- **C Diverse skill set with demonstrated versatility**
- **D Proficiency in contract negotiations with vendors**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Strict work in progress (WIP) limits will likely expose bottlenecks and potentially lead to idle
time, especially if the team members specialize in their own discipline.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question describes a team of developers that uses a Kanban board to manage their workflow
and track tasks as they progress through the development process. A Kanban board is made up of
columns representing the stages of work. For example, a Kanban board may have columns for
the backlog, planning, coding, testing, and deployment. Work in progress (WIP) limits will place
a limit on the work that can be in any particular column. Strict WIP limits will expose
bottlenecks as a column will reach the limit, and no additional work can be added to that column.

---

With a team of narrowly specializing developers, this can lead to idle time as the team
member(s) wait for the bottleneck to clear before they can continue working. However, if the
team is comprised of generalizing specialists, the workload can be balanced. The generalizing
specialist may have a specialty but can perform any of the necessary project tasks. For example,
if the testing stage has reached its WIP limit, a generalizing specialist can switch tasks from
coding to testing to help clear the bottleneck. This flexibility will improve velocity as work is not
held up by the bottleneck. Therefore, among the available options, it is best to select a candidate
with a diverse skillset and demonstrated versatility to join the project team.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Experience with traditional project management**
Incorrect. The question indicates that an agile framework is being used for the project. A
candidate experienced with traditional project management best practices might bring a
fresh perspective, but an experienced agile practitioner would be of greater value for this
project.
- **B Expertise in manual and automatic testing**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents a specialist. The project team will likely need
someone to perform manual and automatic testing of the code as it is developed. However,
a team of all specialists lacks flexibility. With strict WIP limits, bottlenecks are likely to
develop, which will lead to idle time. It is better to have a generalizing specialist on the
team that can float as needed to clear any bottlenecks.
- **C Diverse skill set with demonstrated versatility**
Correct. With strict WIP limits, bottlenecks will likely be exposed leading to idle time. This
answer choice represents a generalizing specialist. Versatility will allow the project team
member to float if needed to clear bottlenecks as they occur, which will reduce or eliminate
idle time. Versatility is highly valued when using a Kanban system with strict WIP limits.
- **D Proficiency in contract negotiations with vendors**
Incorrect. Negotiation with vendors is typically performed by someone other than a
developer on the team. Either the project manager or a dedicated procurement, purchasing
or contracting department within the performing organization negotiates and signs
contracts with vendors.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 311, 177
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 142 of 200
Question ID: 612658
You are a project manager who wants to mitigate the impact of any realized risks for the project.
To achieve this goal, you conduct an initial trial at one location before launching to other
locations. During the trial, you learn best practices to apply during the national launch and
identify pitfalls that should be avoided.
Once the trial is over, what should you do with this information?
Top of Form
- **A Capture the information in the lessons learned register**
- **B Record the implementation of the risk responses in the risk register**
- **C Document issues and their resolutions in the lessons learned repository**
- **D Share the information with the project sponsor and stakeholders**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What project document is used to record knowledge gained during a project?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question suggests you, as the project manager, are attempting to mitigate the impact of any
identified and unknown risks by conducting a trial at one location prior to launching at all
locations. The purpose of the trial is to learn best practices as well as identify any pitfalls. The
knowledge gained from the trial will be vital to the success of the overall effort. The lessons
learned register is a project document used to record knowledge gained during a project so that it

---

can be used later in the project. You should capture the knowledge gained from the trial in the
lessons learned register so that it can be used later in the project.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Capture the information in the lessons learned register**
Correct. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge
gained during a project so that it can be used later in the project.
- **B Record the implementation of the risk responses in the risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register should be updated with information on individual project risks
including adding new risks, updating outdated risks or risks that were realized, updating
risk responses, and so forth. Therefore, the risk register will likely be updated during the
trial. However, the risk register reflects information about risks only, while the question is
also asking about best practices which are not documented in the risk register.
- **C Document issues and their resolutions in the lessons learned repository**
Incorrect. Lessons learned during the project are transferred from the lessons learned
register to the lessons learned repository at the end of the project, where the information
can be used in future projects. The question is concerned with the current project only. The
knowledge gained during the trial should be captured in the lessons learned register (not
the repository) so it will be available for use later in the project when the kiosks are
launched nationwide.
- **D Share the information with the project sponsor and stakeholders**
Incorrect. The knowledge gained from the trial may or may not need to be shared with the
project sponsor and stakeholders depending on what is documented in the communication
management plan, which is not known in this case. While the project sponsor and
stakeholders 'might' be provided with the information, the lessons learned register 'should'
be updated with the knowledge gained from the trial.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 104, 452
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 143 of 200
Question ID: 613643
Due to insufficient historical data, you are applying an approach that factors in uncertainty and
risk calculations to determine time estimate of some of your project activities. The resulting time
estimates will be based on a range.
What tool or technique are you using?
Top of Form
- **A Parametric estimating**
- **B Three-point estimating**
- **C Data analysis**
- **D Analogous estimating**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which technique uses factors such as optimistic and pessimistic to determine an approximate
range for an activity’s duration?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Three-point estimating factors in uncertainty and risk by using most-likely, optimistic, and
pessimistic estimates to calculate the expected duration of an activity. One of the most
commonly used formulas, tE=(tO+tM+tP)/3, factors the optimistic or best-case scenario for the
activity duration, tO; the most likely duration of the activity, tM; and the pessimistic or
worst-case scenario for the activity duration, tP; to arrive at the expected duration, tE. This
approach is useful when there is insufficient historical data (as is the case in the scenario
described) or when judgmental data is used. Duration estimates based on three points with an

---

assumed distribution provide an expected duration and clarify the range of uncertainty around
the expected duration.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Parametric estimating**
Incorrect. Parametric estimating calculates duration (or cost) based on specific historical
data and applicable project parameters rather than using risk and uncertainty factors.
- **B Three-point estimating**
Correct. Three-point estimating is a technique that improves single-point estimates by
considering uncertainty and risk to help define approximate ranges for task durations. This
technique applies an average or weighted average to determine the estimated activity
duration range. By calculating the most-likely, optimistic, and pessimistic estimates, an
overall expected duration is determined.
- **C Data analysis**
Incorrect. There are a number of data analysis techniques that can be used when planning
the project schedule. For example, alternative analysis can be used to compare resource
capabilities or scheduling compression techniques. However, those techniques are not
specifically used to determine an approximate range of time for the duration of an activity.
- **D Analogous estimating**
Incorrect. Analogous estimating uses historical data from previous projects or similar
activities to estimate activity duration. Analogous estimating does not factor in the
uncertainty and risk stated in the question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 200-202

Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 144 of 200
Question ID: 612276
You are developing a charter for a high-risk project. You are aware that the project sponsor has a
low-risk tolerance, which requires special consideration.
What should you do next?
Top of Form
- **A Double the size of the management and contingency reserves**
- **B Ensure the risk identification process is extremely rigorous**
- **C Tell the sponsor that you have managed similar projects**
- **D Consult with a PMI Risk Management Professional (PMI-RMP)®**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project is still in the initiation stage with the development of the project charter. What tool or
technique can be used as part of this process?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question describes a high-risk project in the initiation stage where project risk is a significant
concern. Although the identification of individual project risks is not formally performed until
project planning, the project charter should contain a summary of the overall project risk. The
project manager should consider consulting individuals or groups who have a specialized
knowledge or training in risk identification. Seeking assistance from a PMI Risk Management
Professional (PMI-RMP)® is an example of expert judgment. Under the circumstances described
in the scenario, it is the best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Double the size of the management and contingency reserves**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the project is in initiation. Management and
contingency reserves are determined during project planning and should be adequate to
address the identified risks (contingency reserves) and unknown-unknowns (management
reserves). Not only is it premature to allocate reserves during project initiation, but also
doubling the size of the reserves (which are still unknown at this point) without proper
planning is not an acceptable project management practice.
- **B Ensure the risk identification process is extremely rigorous**
Incorrect. In general, the Identify Risks should be performed properly. The level of rigor
applied in risk identification is tailored to the requirements of the project. However, this
process is part of project planning, while the scenario suggests the project is still in
initiation.
- **C Tell the sponsor that you have managed similar projects**
Incorrect. While it may be comforting for the sponsor to know that you have managed
similar projects, merely stating your experience does not address the essence of the
question. A choice other than this one is more effective in taking into account the low-risk
tolerance of the project sponsor when the project charter is being developed.
- **D Consult with a PMI Risk Management Professional (PMI-RMP)®**
Correct. This answer choice describes expert judgment. The project manager should
consider consulting with individuals or groups who have specialized knowledge or training
in risk identification.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 79

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 145 of 200
Question ID: 612644
- **A project is in the execution stage, and the project manager is currently in the process of**
implementing the stakeholder engagement plan.
Which of the following activities is most likely to be conducted during this process?
Top of Form
- **A Facilitating a meeting to discuss and address any issue or concern regarding stakeholder**
engagement
- **B Producing work performance information about the status of stakeholder engagement**
- **C Capturing stakeholders' current and desired engagement levels in the stakeholder engagement**
assessment matrix
- **D Creating a document that contains identification, assessment, and classification information about**
stakeholders
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The stakeholder engagement plan is implemented during the Manage Stakeholder Engagement
process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The stakeholder engagement plan is a component of the project management plan that identifies
the strategies and actions required to promote the productive involvement of stakeholders in
project or program decision making and execution. The stakeholder engagement plan is created
as an output of the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process and implemented during the Manage
Stakeholder Engagement process. As part of the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process,

---

meetings may be held to discuss and address any issue or concern regarding stakeholder
engagement. The incorrect answer choices describe tasks that are typically associated with
processes other than the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process. Therefore, facilitating a
meeting to discuss and address any issue or concern regarding stakeholder engagement is the
best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Facilitating a meeting to discuss and address any issue or concern regarding stakeholder**
engagement
Correct. During the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process, meetings may be used to
discuss and address any issue or concerns related to stakeholder engagement.
- **B Producing work performance information about the status of stakeholder engagement**
Incorrect. During the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process work performance
information may be produced which includes information about the status of stakeholder
engagement, such as the level of current project support compared to the desired levels of
engagement as defined in the stakeholder engagement assessment matrix or other
documents. Work performance information is not generally created as part of the Manage
Stakeholder Engagement process.
- **C Capturing stakeholders' current and desired engagement levels in the stakeholder**
engagement assessment matrix
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement assessment matrix is initially produced during the
Plan Stakeholder Engagement process to capture stakeholders' current and desired
engagement levels. The stakeholder engagement assessment matrix may then be used
during the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process to monitor stakeholder engagement
through tracking changes in the level of engagement for each stakeholder. Capturing the
stakeholders' current and desired engagement level is not an activity typically performed
during the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process.
- **D Creating a document that contains identification, assessment, and classification**
information about stakeholders
Incorrect. This answer choice describes a stakeholder register. The stakeholder register is
created as an output of the Identify Stakeholder process during project initiation. The
stakeholder register may be updated as the result of performing the Manage Stakeholder
Engagement process but would not be created during this process.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 528

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 146 of 200
Question ID: 612696
As the project manager, once your internal project team members are assigned, you ensure they
can log in and have read and write permissions for the project repository, where all project
related documents are electronically stored. Selected external stakeholders may be provided
logins with limited access and read-only permissions.
What type of communication do you encourage in this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Interpersonal communication**
- **B Interactive communication**
- **C Push communication**
- **D Pull communication**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

When you send a message prompting users to login, does it involve face-to-face interaction with
the users in real time? Does it push the information to the users or prompt the users to pull the
information?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies you, as the project manager, are carrying out the Manage Communications
process. The choice of media, such as a decision about when to use push/pull options, is among
the techniques and considerations for effective communication management. Pull
communication is a method that is used for large complex information sets, or for large
audiences and requires the recipients to access content at their own discretion subject to security

---

procedures. These methods include web portals, intranet sites, e-learning, lessons learned
databases, or knowledge repositories. Of the choices provided, the repository described in the
question meets the definition of pull communication closely, making pull communication the
best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Interpersonal communication**
Incorrect. Interpersonal communications, where information is exchanged between
individuals and usually face to face, is not a communications method, but an approach.
- **B Interactive communication**
Incorrect. Interactive communication is a multidirectional exchange of information in real
time between two or more parties. It employs communications artifacts such as meetings,
phone calls, instant messaging, some forms of social media, and videoconferencing. The
repository described in the question does not enable any of those, making this choice an
incorrect answer.
- **C Push communication**
Incorrect. Push communication is a communication method where the information is sent
or distributed directly to specific recipients who need to receive it. This ensures that the
information is distributed but does not ensure that it actually reached or was understood by
the intended audience. Push communications artifacts include letters, memos, reports,
emails, faxes, voice mails, blogs, and press releases. Since the scenario describes a method
requiring recipients to log in to access the information and take action, it does not meet the
description of push communication.
- **D Pull communication**
Correct. Pull communication is a method that is used for large complex information sets, or
for large audiences and requires the recipients to access content at their own discretion
subject to security procedures.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 374

PMP Exam 5
