PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 171 of 200
Question ID: 613537
- **A seller has completed the work that was formally accepted by the buyer. The key deliverables**
specified in the statement of work (SOW) are the robot, operational and support documents,
specialized tools, and software. The seller has also offered the buyer to purchase a support
service, but the buyer has declined the offer. Two weeks after the robot was deployed, the buyer
contacts the seller to ask how to adjust the robot's programming.
What is the best course of action for the seller?
Top of Form
- **A Tell the buyer that they should have purchased the support service**
- **B Record the problem in the issue log for the seller's project**
- **C Return to the job site and make the requested adjustments**
- **D Advise the buyer to check their organizational process assets**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The operational and support documents should contain information on how to adjust the robot.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question states that operational and support documents were among the key project
deliverables. These documents should have the necessary information on how to make
adjustments to the robot. Note, there are two sides to the scenario, the buyer, and the seller. Both
are carrying out the project. The buyer in this scenario is the performing organization, while the
seller is the one who delivers the work based on the procurement statement of work (SOW)
provided by the buyer. The buyer, as the performing organization, is supposed to carry out all

---

processes necessary to complete the project, including the Close Project or Phase process.
Updates to the organizational process assets (OPAs) is among the outputs of this process.
Documents required for an organization to maintain, operate, and support the product or service
delivered by the project (whether the product/service has been produced internally or by an
external vendor) are part of the buyer's OPAs updated during the Close Project or Phase process.
Even though it was the seller who has produced the documents, it is the responsibility of the
buyer to ensure the documents are available. Therefore, of the choices offered, the best course of
action for the seller is to advise the buyer to check their organizational process assets to review
the operational and support documents which were delivered by the seller to the buyer.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Tell the buyer that they should have purchased the support service**
Incorrect. Telling the buyer that they should have purchased the service agreement when
they had the chance is needlessly confrontational and not particularly helpful. If the buyer's
trial is successful, they may want to acquire more products from and establish a
longer-term business relationship with the seller. It would be better to provide appropriate
guidance for the buyer.
- **B Record the problem in the issue log for the seller's project**
Incorrect. From the standpoint of the seller company, the contract has been completed, and
the project closed out. The issue log would only be useful during the lifecycle of the project.
- **C Return to the job site and make the requested adjustments**
Incorrect. Returning to the job site to provide assistance as a goodwill gesture might seem
like a good idea. However, the buyer did not purchase a service agreement, and performing
service work may create an expectation of continued support without compensation.
Realistically, the seller cannot keep returning to the job site every time the robot needs to
be adjusted in the absence of a service agreement.
- **D Advise the buyer to check their organizational process assets**
Correct. The operational and support documents should have the necessary information on
how to make the requested adjustments to the robot and are considered an organizational
process asset of the buyer who is the performing organization in the scenario described.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 128, 477

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 172 of 200
Question ID: 613667
- **A project manager is in the process of estimating the costs of a project to construct a 300,000**
square foot shopping mall. Based on historical data, the project manager uses a value of $400 per
square foot and estimates the cost at $120,000,000.
What estimating technique is the project manager using?
Top of Form
- **A Bottom-up estimating**
- **B Parametric estimating**
- **C Analogous estimating**
- **D Three-point estimating**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What estimating technique uses an algorithm to estimate costs?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Estimate Costs process is underway. Parametric estimating is an
estimating technique in which an algorithm is used to calculate the cost based on historical data
and project parameters. The example provided in the question uses an average cost per square
foot to estimate the cost, which is a very simplistic example of parametric estimating. While both
parametric estimating and analogous estimating use historical data to calculate the cost (or
duration), there is a difference between the two. Analogous estimating is used when there is a
limited amount of information available for the current project, but the project/activity looks
similar to a past project/activity. Thus, the overall cost estimate of the current project/activity is

---

considered similar (analogous) to the past one and, therefore, the cost can be ‘roughly’ estimated.
This is the reason analogous estimating is sometimes called top-down estimating. This method is
less accurate than parametric estimating.
Parametric estimating, on the other hand, uses information from past similar projects/activities
AND parameters of the current project/activities because these parameters are already known
during project planning. There is a statistical relationship between the parameters, such as cost
per unit and the number of units. When cost per unit from the past project/activity as well as the
number of units required for the current project are known, an algorithm can be used to estimate
cost, thus producing a more accurate estimate. In the scenario described, the number of units and
the cost per unit are known - 300,000 square foot, $400 per square foot. The project manager
multiplied one parameter by the other and obtained the cost estimate of $120,000,000. Therefore,
of the choices provided, parametric estimating is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Bottom-up estimating**
Incorrect. Bottom-up estimating is a method of estimating project duration or cost by
aggregating the estimates of the lower-level components of the work breakdown structure
(WBS). The description provided in the question indicates that an algorithm is being used
to estimate the costs rather than a bottom-up approach.
- **B Parametric estimating**
Correct. Parametric estimating is an estimating technique in which an algorithm is used to
calculate the cost based on historical data and project parameters. The example provided
in the question uses an average cost per square foot to estimate the cost.
- **C Analogous estimating**
Incorrect. Analogous estimating is a technique for estimating the cost of an activity or a
project using historical data from a similar activity or project. While the question indicates
that information from a past project was used in creating the cost estimate, the scenario
also provides more details as to what parameters were used to reach the estimate. Another
answer choice more accurately describes the technique used.
- **D Three-point estimating**
Incorrect. Three-point estimating is a technique used to estimate cost by applying an
average or weighted average of optimistic, pessimistic, and most likely estimates. The
question does not provide any information on optimistic, pessimistic, or most likely
estimates.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 244
Bottom of Form

Question 173 of 200
Question ID: 612249
You are in the initiation stage of a project that aims to deploy and then maintain the robotics for
an automated production line for an important client. In the project charter, you need to include
the agreed mean time to recover (MTTR) in the event of a breakdown.
What should you do to find this information?
Top of Form
- **A Do nothing since agreements are not yet available during project initiation**
- **B Refer to the procurement management plan**
- **C Review any emails or other correspondence with the client**
- **D Check the service level agreement with the client**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This information is typically included in the terms and conditions of a contract.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

- **A service level agreement (SLA) can serve as an input into the Develop Project Charter process.**
An SLA may define agreed-upon service levels such as mean time to recover (MTTR). The SLA
is likely to be included in the terms and conditions of a contract along with penalties or other
recourse for failing to achieve the agreed-upon service levels. Therefore, of the available answer
choices, you, as the project manager, should check the SLA for information on the agreed-upon
mean time to recover.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Do nothing since agreements are not yet available during project initiation**
Incorrect. Agreements serve as an input into the Develop Project Charter process, and the
project charter is created during project initiation.
- **B Refer to the procurement management plan**
Incorrect. The procurement management plan is a component of the project management
plan. The project management plan is not created until project planning which occurs after
project initiation has been completed.
- **C Review any emails or other correspondence with the client**
Incorrect. Although emails and other correspondence may serve as informal agreements
and may contain information on service levels, another choice has a more formal and
suitable input to the Develop Charter process.
- **D Check the service level agreement with the client**
Correct. The service level agreement (SLA) may define agreed-upon service levels, such as
mean time to recover (MTTR).

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 78

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 174 of 200
Question ID: 612057
You are the project manager for the initial design phase of a new ergonomic pen. You have
conducted multiple interviews with pen users and have tested various design concepts. Your
most recent design has been verified and accepted by key stakeholders. The pen design is ready
to transition to the team managing the next phase.
Which of the following should you consult to find out who will take ownership of the pen
design?
Top of Form
- **A The project management plan**
- **B The final report**
- **C The scope statement**
- **D The communications management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What project artifact describes how a project will be closed?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Since the pen design is ready to transition to the next phase, you can infer the scenario is in the
Close Project or Phase process. A key action when closing a phase is transferring the ownership
of your phase's intermediary deliverables to the proper group or organization tasked with using
the output from your phase to meet the project objectives in their phase. You would consult the
project management plan, specifically the subsidiary project life cycle description because it
describes the series of phases that a project passes through from its initiation to its closure. While

---

the PMBOK® Guide does not explicitly state that the project management plan specifies ‘who’ in
the next phase takes ownership of the deliverables from the previous phase, it is reasonable to
assume that, of the choices given, only the project management plan is likely to have this
information and is, therefore, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The project management plan**
Correct. The project management plan defines the basis of all project work and how the
work will be performed. Transferring the ownership of deliverables to the assigned
stakeholders is done in accordance with the project management plan to facilitate project
closures. The project management plan would indicate who will manage the next phase
(and subsequent phases) in the development of the new ergonomic pen and would also
identify the recipient of the final product.
- **B The final report**
Incorrect. The final report provides a summary of the project performance, such as a
summary level description of the project or phase, and objectives for scope, quality, cost,
and schedule as well as validation information for the output, a summary of risks/issues,
and how the deliverable achieved business objectives. The final report does not include
information on who will take ownership of the project or phase output.
- **C The scope statement**
Incorrect. The project scope statement is created during planning and includes the
description of the project scope, major deliverables, assumptions, and constraints. The
project scope does not indicate what group or organization the final pen design will
transfer to at the completion of a project phase.
- **D The communications management plan**
Incorrect. The communications management plan describes how, when, and by whom
information about the project will be administered and distributed. The communications
management plan may include communication protocols with the group(s) or
organization(s) who will take ownership of the project deliverables, but it does not
explicitly states the transfer of ownership from phase-to-phase or who the recipient of the
final output would be at the end of the project.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 88, 123, 135, 568

Question 175 of 200
Question ID: 625138
The following chart was taken from the project's current performance report. The project has
encountered some unforeseen obstacles, but those challenges have now been overcome. You are
confident that you can hold costs to the budgeted rate for the remainder of the project. The
method used to determine the earned value is based on percent complete.
Based on the budgeted rate, what is the EAC for the project?
Top of Form
- **A $666,667**
- **B $550,000**
- **C -$50,000**

---

- **D $500,000**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The question states that the work is expected to progress at the budgeted rate for the remainder of
the project, so the correct EAC formula is EAC = AC + (BAC - EV).
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question states that the future performance will be at the budgeted rate. Even though the
project to date has not performed at the budgeted rate, it is expected that the project will perform
at the budgeted rate for the remainder of the project. Therefore, the formula that should be used
in this scenario is EAC = AC + (BAC – EV). Note, since the scenario mentions that the method
used to determine the earned value is based on percent complete, the earned value of a partially
completed work package is calculated by multiplying the planned value of the work package by
its the percent complete.
The calculations are shown below:
EV = EV of activity 1 + EV of activity 2 + EV of activity 3 = (1 x $15,000) + (1 x $10,000) +
(0.50 x $250,000) = $150,000
AC = AC of activity 1 + AC of activity 2 + AC of activity 3 = $14,000 + $11,000 + $175,000 =
$200,000
EAC = AC + (BAC - EV) = $200,000 + ($500,000 - $150,000) = $550,000
Therefore, the estimate at completion (EAC) is $550,000.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A $666,667**
Incorrect. When the cost performance is expected to be unchanged for the remainder of the
project, the EAC can be calculated as EAC = BAC / CPI = $500,000 / .75 = $666,667.
However, the question states that the project is expected to continue at the budgeted rate
and not based on the CPI. Therefore, the correct formula for EAC is EAC = AC + (BAC -
EV).
- **B $550,000**

---

Correct. If the future work will be accomplished at the planned rate, the EAC formula is
EAC = AC + (BAC - EV) = $200,000 + ($500,000 - $150,000) = $550,000.
- **C -$50,000**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents the variance at completion (VAC) which can be
calculated as the budget at completion (BAC) minus the estimate at completion (EAC)
which equals -$50,000. However, the question is asking for the EAC and not the VAC.
- **D $500,000**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents the budget at completion (BAC) which is the total
planned value of the project and is provided in the table. However, the question is asking
for the EAC and not the BAC.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 264-265
Practice Standard for Earned Value Management - Second Edition, Project Management
Institute Inc., 2011, Page(s) 38-39
https://www.project-management-prepcast.com/pmp-formulas

Question 176 of 200
Question ID: 625115
The following table represents the current project status. According to the project schedule,
system analysis, system design, and system development should now be complete. The project
manager is confident that the project objectives will be met. The method used to determine the
earned value is based on percent complete.
What is the project's current schedule performance index, and what does this mean for the
project?
Top of Form
- **A The SPI is -$12,500, and the project is running behind schedule**
- **B An SPI of 1.0 since the project manager is confident that the project objectives will be met**
- **C The SPI is 1.24, and the project is running ahead of schedule**
- **D The SPI is 0.81, and the project is running behind schedule**
Question answered incorrectly

---


**Hint:**

The first step is to calculate the earned value (EV). The earned values for each phase can be
calculated by multiplying the planned value of the phase by its percentage of completion.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The schedule performance index (SPI) can be calculated as the earned value (EV) divided by the
planned value (PV). The current total earned value can be obtained by multiplying each activity's
planned value by its percentage complete and adding them together. Therefore, the current total
earned value is $52,500. The current total planned value is the sum of the planned values of the
activities that should have been completed by now according to the approved plan, which is this
scenario is $65,000. Note, since the scenario mentions that the method used to determine the
earned value is based on percent complete, the earned value of a partially completed work
package is calculated by multiplying the planned value of the work package by its the percent
complete.
The calculations are shown below:
SPI = EV / PV
EV = ($5,000 x 100%) + ($10,000 x 100%) + ($50,000 x 75%) = $52,500
PV = $5,000 + $10,000 + $50,000 = $65,000
SPI = $52,500 / $65,000 = 0.81
Therefore, the schedule performance index is 0.81. Additionally, since the SPI is less than one,
the project is running behind schedule.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The SPI is -$12,500, and the project is running behind schedule**
Incorrect. While it is correct that the project is running behind schedule, the first part of
this answer choice, -$12,500, represents the schedule variance (SV). However, the question
is asking for the schedule performance index and not the schedule variance.
- **B An SPI of 1.0 since the project manager is confident that the project objectives will be met**
Incorrect. An SPI of 1.0 would indicate that the project is progressing on schedule.
However, according to the calculation, the SPI is 0.81, meaning the project is currently
running behind schedule. The project manager may believe that the gap will be closed by
the end of the project, but that has yet to be seen. The fact that the project manager is
confident that the project will be completed on time is not relevant to the actual SPI.

---

- **C The SPI is 1.24, and the project is running ahead of schedule**
Incorrect. If the SPI were 1.24, the project would have been ahead of schedule. However,
this answer choice represents the result of the incorrect usage of the SPI formula where the
numerator and denominator are transposed.
- **D The SPI is 0.81, and the project is running behind schedule**
Correct. The schedule performance index (SPI) can be calculated as the earned value (EV)
divided by the planned value (PV) or SV = EV / PV. EV = ($5,000 x 100%) + ($10,000 x
100%) + ($50,000 x 75%) = $52,500. PV = $5,000 + $10,000 + $50,000 = $65,000. SV =
$52,500 / $65,000 = 0.81. Since the SPI is a less than 1, in this case, the project is running
behind schedule.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 263, 267
Practice Standard for Earned Value Management - Second Edition, Project Management
Institute Inc., 2011, Page(s) 38-39
https://www.project-management-prepcast.com/pmp-formulas

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 177 of 200
Question ID: 612191
- **A project is broken down into four phases: design, build, test, deploy. At the end of the design**
phase, the project manager would like to determine if the project should be terminated or proceed
to the build phase.
What should the project manager do next?
Top of Form
- **A Hold a phase gate**
- **B Schedule a retrospective**
- **C Facilitate a meeting with the project team**
- **D Convene the change control board (CCB)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who has the authority to terminate a project or authorize a project to proceed with the next
phase?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

- **A phase gate is held at the end of a phase. The purpose of a phase gate is to compare the project's**
performance and progress to the project and business documents. At the phase gate, a
determination is made to proceed with the next phase, repeat the current phase (or elements of
it), remain in the phase, or terminate the project. Therefore, of the available options, holding a
phase gate is what the project manager should do next.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Hold a phase gate**
Correct. A phase gate may be held to review project performance and determine if the
project should be terminated or proceed to the next phase.
- **B Schedule a retrospective**
Incorrect. A retrospective is a scheduled review to record lessons learned. Although project
performance may be reviewed during a retrospective, a determination of whether a project
should proceed or be terminated is not likely to be made during a retrospective.
- **C Facilitate a meeting with the project team**
Incorrect. The project team may or may not be involved in determining if the project should
be terminated or proceed to the build phase. However, the project team does not have the
authority to terminate a project. A decision regarding the next steps for the project is made
by the customer, project sponsor, and/or senior executives.
- **D Convene the change control board (CCB)**
Incorrect. The CCB is a formally chartered group responsible for reviewing, evaluating,
approving, delaying, or rejecting change requests. The CCB is not authorized to make
decisions regarding the termination of a project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 21

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 178 of 200
Question ID: 651307
To create a burndown chart at the end of iteration planning, where is the to-be-charted work
pulled from?
Top of Form
- **A Iteration backlog**
- **B Work package**
- **C Product backlog**
- **D Requirements document**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Is the project manager trying to figure out where the project is now or what it must do from this
point on?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Burndown charts are typically used on agile projects. A burndown chart is intended to relay the
progress of the project team in any iteration. That progress is based on the work pulled from the
iteration backlog. That iteration backlog represents the commitment of the project team for the
work to be completed in the upcoming iteration. As the iteration progresses, the expectation is
that the committed work is being completed or ‘burned off’. Hence the chart starts with what was
committed and if things go as planned, that work is burned down until there is no other work
remaining in that iteration.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Iteration backlog**
Correct. When an iteration is scheduled, the project team prunes and cultivates the
iteration backlog until they finalize on the commitment for the upcoming iteration. That list
is the iteration backlog. The iteration backlog represents the work that must be ‘burned
down’ in the upcoming iteration.
- **B Work package**
Incorrect. Iterations may consist of a work package or many work packages. Iterations may
not even fulfill all the needs of a work package. Work packages are much too large to
measure and track in a burndown chart.
- **C Product backlog**
Incorrect. The product backlog consists of all the expected work of a project, not only the
iteration. And since agile projects are constantly changing and revising those expectations,
the product backlog is also revised. The burndown chart is to relay the progress of the
project team in any iteration. That progress is based on the work pulled from the iteration
backlog.
- **D Requirements document**
Incorrect. The requirements documentation is often too detailed and technical to serve as a
reliable source of data to demonstrate the team’s progress during an iteration.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 226

PMP Exam 5

Question 179 of 200
Question ID: 612227
You are planning a large, complex, and lengthy project. To identify as many risks as possible,
you want input from the sponsor, subject matter experts, vendors, customer representatives, and
other project stakeholders.
Which of the following will help you the most?
Top of Form
- **A Risk audit**
- **B Risk report**
- **C Risk workshop**
- **D Risk register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which meeting is conducted as part of the Identify Risks process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

According to the scenario, you are about to begin the Identify Risks process. A risk workshop is
an example of a meeting that can be used as part of this process. A risk workshop a specialized
meeting undertaken for the sole purpose of risk identification and is typically used for large,
complex projects, and may involve the sponsor, subject matter experts, vendors, customer
representatives, and other project stakeholders. Risk workshops often include some sort of
brainstorming, but other risk identification techniques may be used depending on the level of the

---

risk process defined in the risk management plan. To increase the effectiveness of the meeting, it
is recommended that a skilled facilitator attends the risk workshop.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk audit**
Incorrect. A risk audit is a structured review of the risk management process to evaluate its
effectiveness. In the scenario, you are looking to identify as many risks as possible rather
than evaluate the effectiveness of the risk management process.
- **B Risk report**
Incorrect. A risk report is a project document developed progressively throughout the
Project Risk Management processes, which summarizes information on individual project
risks and the level of overall project risk. According to the scenario, the project is still in
planning, and it is likely that only high-level risks listed in the project charter are those that
have been identified at this point. Your goal in the scenario described is to identify as many
risks as possible.
- **C Risk workshop**
Correct. A risk workshop is a specialized meeting undertaken for the sole purpose of risk
identification. The risk workshop is associated with the Identify Risks process suggested by
the scenario.
- **D Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a repository in which the outputs of risk management
processes are recorded. The risk register will be used to document all of the risks identified
in a risk workshop or other technique used to identify as many risks as possible. The risk
register itself will not help you identify risks.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 416

PMP Exam 5

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 180 of 200
Question ID: 610081
You have compiled a list of potential stakeholders for your project, and now you are classifying
the stakeholders with regard to their influence. As you work through your way down the list of
stakeholders, you have come to the project sponsor.
How should you classify the direction of influence of this stakeholder?
Top of Form
- **A Downward**
- **B Sideward**
- **C Outward**
- **D Upward**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think of the seniority level of the project sponsor.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

According to the scenario, you are carrying out the Identify Stakeholders process. Directions of
influence is an example of a data representation technique that can be used as part of this
process. This technique classifies stakeholders according to their influence on the work of the
project or the project team itself. Stakeholders can be classified as upward, downward, outward,
or sideward. The upward classification includes senior management of the performing
organization or customer organization, sponsor, and steering committee. Therefore, the project
sponsor should be classified as upward.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Downward**
Incorrect. The downward classification is typically assigned to the team or specialists
contributing knowledge or skills in a temporary capacity. The project sponsor is neither a
part of the project team nor a specialist contributing knowledge or skills in a temporary
capacity.
- **B Sideward**
Incorrect. The sideward classification includes peers of the project manager, such as other
project managers or middle managers who are in competition for scarce project resources
or who collaborate with the project manager in sharing resources or information. This
description does not include the project sponsor.
- **C Outward**
Incorrect. Stakeholder groups and their representatives outside the project team, such as
suppliers, government departments, the public, end-users, and regulators are typically
classified outward when the directions of influence technique is used.
- **D Upward**
Correct. The upward classification includes senior management of the performing
organization or customer organization, sponsor, and steering committee. Therefore, the
project sponsor should be classified as upward.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 513

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 181 of 200
Question ID: 625056
In preparation for an upcoming project status meeting, you have determined the value of the
work completed thus far is $100,000 with a budget at completion (BAC) of $1,000,000. At this
point in the project, you have spent 12% of the project budget. The value of work planned to be
completed at this point is $115,000.
What will you report at the project status meeting?
Top of Form
- **A The project is performing well in terms of cost but not in terms of schedule**
- **B The project is not performing well both in terms of cost and schedule**
- **C The project is currently behind schedule**
- **D The project is currently over budget**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

You have to calculate either CV and SV or CPI and SPI using the available values of EV =
$100,000, PV = $115,000, AC = $120,000. Remember to select the answer choice that more
accurately and fully addresses the question asked.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

To determine the status of the project, the schedule variance and cost variance (or, alternatively,
the cost performance index (CPI) and schedule performance index (SPI)) must be calculated. The
earned value (EV), which is the actual work completed in the scenario described, is stated as
$100,000. The planned value (PV), which is the value of work planned to be completed at this
point in the scenario, is stated as $115,000. The actual cost (AC), which is the portion of the

---

project budget you have spent so far in the scenario described, is 12% of the budget of
$1,000,000 which is $120,000. The calculations of the cost variance (CV) and the schedule
variance (SV) are shown below:
CV = EV - AC = $100,000 - $120,000 = -$20,000
SV = EV - PV = $100,000 - $115,000 = -$15,000
Both the schedule variance and the cost variance are negative at this point in the project.
Therefore, at the project status meeting, you should report that the project is not performing well
both in terms of cost and schedule.
Alternatively, you can calculate the CPI and the SPI:
CPI = EV / AC = $100,000 / $120,000 = 0.83
SPI = EV / PV = $100,000 / $115,000 = 0.87
Both the schedule variance and the cost variance are less than 1 at this point in the project.
Therefore, the same conclusion can be made: the project is not performing well both in terms of
cost and schedule.
Note, three answer choices represent correct statements regarding the status of the project
described in the scenario. However, the goal of the PMP aspirant is, of the choices provided, to
select the best answer to the question asked. Reporting to the meeting participants that the project
is over budget would not be wrong. Reporting to the meeting participants that the project is
behind schedule would not be wrong either. However, none of these statements fully represents
the current project status. Of the available choices, reporting to the meeting participants that the
project is over budget 'and' behind schedule, i.e., the project is not performing well both in terms
of cost and schedule, is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The project is performing well in terms of cost but not in terms of schedule**
Incorrect. The cost variance (CV) = EV - AC or $100,000 - $120,000 which is -$20,000.
The schedule variance (SV) = EV - PV or $100,000 - $115,000 which is -$15,000. The cost
and schedule variances are both negative in this case which indicates that the project is
behind schedule and over budget. Since at least one part of this answer choice represents
an incorrect statement, this choice is an incorrect answer.
- **B The project is not performing well both in terms of cost and schedule**
Correct. The cost variance (CV) = EV - AC or $100,000 - $120,000 which is -$20,000. The
schedule variance (SV) = EV - PV or $100,000 - $115,000 which is -$15,000. The cost and
schedule variances are both negative in this case which indicates that the project is behind

---

schedule and over budget, meaning the project is not performing well both in terms of cost
and schedule.
- **C The project is currently behind schedule**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents a true statement: SV = EV - PV = $100,000 -
$115,000 = -$15,000. Since the schedule variance is negative, the project is behind
schedule. However, this statement does not fully reflect the overall project status. There is
another answer choice that more accurately addresses the question asked.
- **D The project is currently over budget**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents a true statement: CV = EV - AC = $100,000 -
$120,000 = -$20,000. Since the cost variance is negative, the project is over budget.
However, this statement does not fully reflect the overall project status. There is another
answer choice that more accurately addresses the question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 267; see
also https://www.project-management-prepcast.com/pmp-formulas
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 182 of 200
Question ID: 612279
- **A newly identified stakeholder just informed the project team of changes to regulations that**
would impact the project.
Which of the following is the least likely to be updated in this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Change log**
- **B Scope baseline**
- **C Stakeholder register**
- **D Change management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

- **A new stakeholder with new requirements has joined the project. Which of the answer choices**
represent a project artifact that needs to be updated and which one is not?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The key to answering this question correctly is to understand the nature and purpose of each of
the answer choices. While it may be tempting to think that the change management plan needs to
be updated to reflect the change in the regulations, the change management plan describes 'how'
the change requests throughout the project will be formally authorized and incorporated. The
changes themselves are captured in the change log, not in the change management plan.
Therefore, the way the changes are handled on the project would likely remain the same
regardless of the changes to regulations. However, changes to regulations will likely require an
additional scope, which must be accounted for in the scope baseline. Additionally, anytime new

---

stakeholders are added to the project, as is in the scenario describes, the stakeholder register must
be updated. Therefore, since the question is asking to select the option that represents the 'least'
likely project artifact to be updated, the change management plan is the best answer to the
question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change log**
Incorrect. A change log is a project document that contains a comprehensive list of changes
submitted during the project and their current status. A change to the regulations will
require a change request (or multiple change requests) to various project artifacts.
Therefore, saying that the change log is the 'least' likely to be updated in the scenario
described would not be correct.
- **B Scope baseline**
Incorrect. The new regulations may trigger new requirements implying possible additions
to the project scope. Therefore, the scope baseline likely will require changes.
- **C Stakeholder register**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, a new stakeholder has been identified. Therefore, the
stakeholder register should be updated.
- **D Change management plan**
Correct. The change management plan describes how the change requests throughout the
project will be formally authorized and incorporated. The new regulations will likely
require a change request to update the relevant project artifacts. However, the way the
changes are handled on the project is unlikely to be modified. Therefore, the change
management plan is the least likely to be updated given the choices provided.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 116, 120, 161-162, 169-170

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 183 of 200
Question ID: 610051
You are mentoring project stakeholders on processes to be carried out during the project. You are
now displaying the slide about the Close Project or Phase process.
What should you tell the stakeholders about this process?
Top of Form
- **A The Close Project or Phase process is not used if the project is terminated before completion.**
- **B The Close Project or Phase process is always the last process to be performed.**
- **C The Close Project or Phase process is performed before the administrative closure.**
- **D Procurements are closed out as part of the Close Project or Phase process.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Close Project or Phase is the process of finalizing all activities across all of the project
management process groups to formally complete the project or phase.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Close Project or Phase is the process of finalizing all activities for the project or phase.
During this process the project or phase information is archived, the planned work is completed,
and the organizational team resources are released to pursue new endeavors. The Close Project or
Phase process is always the last project management process carried out. Of the available
options, the only answer choice that is correct in all cases is that the Close Project or Phase
process will be the final project management process performed.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The Close Project or Phase process is not used if the project is terminated before**
completion.
Incorrect. The Close Project or Phase process should still be carried out to establish
procedures to investigate and document the reasons for actions taken when a project is
terminated before completion.
- **B The Close Project or Phase process is always the last process to be performed.**
Correct. Close Project or Phase is the process of finalizing all activities for the project or
phase. During this process the project or phase information is archived, the planned work
is completed, and the organizational team resources are released to pursue new endeavors.
Under any circumstances, the Close Project or Phase process should always be carried out
at the end of the project or phase and is therefore always the last process to be performed.
- **C The Close Project or Phase process is performed before the administrative closure.**
Incorrect. Administrative closure is an essential component of the Close Project or Phase
process, and it is performed as part of the Close Project or Phase process and not
afterward.
- **D Procurements are closed out as part of the Close Project or Phase process.**
Incorrect. Closed procurements are an output of the Control Procurements process rather
than the Close Project or Phase process. Therefore, this answer choice can be eliminated.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 121-123

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 184 of 200
Question ID: 612205
The current project phase is scheduled to conclude on July 29. Today is July 14, and the project
team should complete the remaining work well before the July 29 deadline. The project manager
proposes a change to move ahead a few tasks from the next phase into the current phase to
prevent the team from procrastinating and coasting.
Which of the following theories describes the project manager's concern behind this change
request?
Top of Form
- **A McClelland's expectancy value theory**
- **B Parkinson's law**
- **C Moore's law**
- **D Law of diminishing returns**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

According to this law, work expands to fill the time available for its completion.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question describes a situation where the project manager, based on an analysis of the
velocity of the team's prior work, feels that the remaining work should be able to be completed
well before the current deadline. The project manager believes that unless more work is assigned
in this phase, the project team will waste time, since the deadline gives them more than the time
they need to finish the remaining work of the first phase. According to Parkinson's law, work
expands to fill the time available for its completion. In other words, if resources are left idle, time

---

and money are wasted. The project manager, in this case, is concerned with optimizing resource
utilization. Therefore, of the choices provided, Parkinson’s law is the best answer to the question
asked.
Although the PMBOK® Guide comprises the majority of the content that you will encounter on
the Project Management Professional (PMP)® exam, the PMP® Examination Content Outline
assumes that the prospective PMP aspirants are familiar with other sources that are used by the
Project Management Institute (PMI)® as content material. Some of the answer choices presented
in this question are based on the sources outside the PMBOK® Guide.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A McClelland's expectancy value theory**
Incorrect. David McClelland's expectancy value theory of motivation states, "every person
has one of three main driving motivators: the needs for achievement, affiliation, or power.
These motivators are not inherent; we develop them through our culture and life
experiences." These factors are not relevant to reprioritizing the tasks to optimize resource
utilization.
- **B Parkinson's law**
Correct. Cyril Northcote Parkinson wrote in a book about the inefficiency of bureaucracy,
"Work expands so as to fill the time available for its completion." In the scenario described,
the project manager is concerned about optimizing resource utilization and minimizing idle
time.
- **C Moore's law**
Incorrect. Gordon Moore projected in 1975 that computer processor speeds and processing
power would double every two years for at least a decade. This observation is not relevant
in the case of re-prioritizing project tasks.
- **D Law of diminishing returns**
Incorrect. The law of diminishing returns states that for each additional amount of input,
effort, or cost, the return on that investment or effort becomes less and less as more input or
cost are applied. In other words, a point is reached where the level of profits or benefits
gained is less than the amount of money or energy invested. This law would be more
relevant to a project manager crashing the project than re-prioritizing tasks from a future
phase. Therefore, this choice is not the best answer.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 197
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 185 of 200
Question ID: 625117
- **A project manager is leading a software development project for an important client. The**
following table represents the current project status. According to the project schedule, system
analysis, system design, and system development should now be complete. The method used to
determine the earned value is based on percent complete.
What is the project's current schedule variance, and what does this mean for the project?
Top of Form
- **A The schedule variance is -$12,500, and the project performance is unknown**
- **B The schedule variance is -$12,500, and the project is running behind schedule**
- **C The schedule variance is -$12,500, and the project is running ahead of schedule**
- **D The schedule variance is $12,500, and the project is running behind schedule**
Question answered incorrectly

---


**Hint:**

The first step is to calculate the earned value (EV). The earned values for each phase can be
calculated by multiplying the planned value of the phase by its percentage of completion.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The schedule variance (SV) can be calculated as the earned value (EV) minus the planned value
(PV). The current total earned value can be obtained by multiplying each activity's planned value
by its percentage complete and adding them together. Therefore, the current total earned value is
$52,500. The current total planned value is the sum of the planned values of the activities that
should have been completed according to the approved plan, which is this scenario is $65,000.
Note, since the scenario mentions that the method used to determine the earned value is based on
percent complete, the earned value of a partially completed work package is calculated by
multiplying the planned value of the work package by its percent complete.
The following are the correct calculations for the schedule variance:
SV = EV - PV
EV = ($5,000 x 100%) + ($10,000 x 100%) + ($50,000 x 75%) = $52,500
PV = $5,000 + $10,000 + $50,000 = $65,000
SV = $52,500 - $65,000 = -$12,500
Therefore, the schedule variance (SV) is -$12,500. Since the SV is a negative value, in this case,
the project is running behind schedule.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The schedule variance is -$12,500, and the project performance is unknown**
Incorrect. While the schedule variance is indeed -$12,500, the project performance 'can' be
determined using various earned value measurement techniques. For example, when the
schedule variance is negative, such as in this scenario, the project is behind schedule.
- **B The schedule variance is -$12,500, and the project is running behind schedule**
Correct. The schedule variance (SV) can be calculated as the earned value (EV) minus the
planned value (PV) or SV = EV - PV. The EV is calculated as EV = ($5,000 x 100%) +
($10,000 x 100%) + ($50,000 x 75%) = $52,500. The PV is calculated as PV = $5,000 +
$10,000 + $50,000 = $65,000. Therefore, SV = $52,500 - $65,000 = -$12,500. Since the
SV is a negative value, the project is running behind schedule.

---

- **C The schedule variance is -$12,500, and the project is running ahead of schedule**
Incorrect. The schedule variance is -$12,500. Negative schedule variance means the project
is behind, not ahead of, schedule.
- **D The schedule variance is $12,500, and the project is running behind schedule**
Incorrect. While the project is indeed running behind schedule, the first part of this answer
choice represents incorrect usage of the formula for the schedule variance where EV and
PV are transposed.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 262, 267
Practice Standard for Earned Value Management - Second Edition, Project Management
Institute Inc., 2011, Page(s) 38-39
https://www.project-management-prepcast.com/pmp-formulas

PMP Exam 5

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 186 of 200
Question ID: 613283
- **A project manager at a shipbuilding firm is managing a marine construction project. The ship is**
partially complete when a previously undiscovered systematic flaw in the deck welds is detected.
As a result, an additional plate will need to be designed and fabricated for every piece of deck
equipment.
Which of the following must be updated?
Top of Form
- **A Risk register**
- **B Resource management plan**
- **C Project charter**
- **D Scope baseline**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Focus on what has changed.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

In the scenario, the project team is performing quality management activities. The main focus of
the question is to determine what plan or document must be updated as a result of adding a plate
for every piece of deck equipment. Since the fabrication and the installation of those plates
represent an additional scope, the scope baseline must be updated (assuming approval of the
corresponding change request has been obtained). Therefore, of the choices available, the scope

---

baseline is the document that must be updated and is, therefore, the best answer to the question
asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk register**
Incorrect. A risk register is a repository in which the outputs of risk management processes
are recorded. The risk register would need to be updated if the welding flaw was a
previously identified risk, or if the additional plates introduce a new risk to the project.
However, the scenario gives no indication that either of these conditions is true. On the
other hand, the additional plates clearly represent additional scope. Therefore, while the
risk register 'may' need to be updated, the scope baseline 'must' be updated.
- **B Resource management plan**
Incorrect. Although the additional deck plates are resources, the project manager will not
necessarily need to change the resource management plan, which describes how project
resources are acquired, allocated, monitored, and controlled.
- **C Project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter is a document that authorizes the project, the project
manager, and contains high-level information about the project. This document is rarely
updated throughout the course of the project. It is highly unlikely that the project charter
would be updated as a result of scope changes.
- **D Scope baseline**
Correct. The new deck equipment plates will require additional project work to fabricate
and install, and this represents additional project scope. The scope baseline must be
updated to reflect the change before the new work can begin.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 297, 131, 161

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 187 of 200
Question ID: 650110
After reviewing proposals for a large-scale product development project, vendors X and Y are
equally qualified to deliver both the hardware and software. The project manager believes the
hardware should be developed with a traditional project management approach, but the software
might be better suited to an agile framework.
What is the best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Contract with vendor X for hardware, with vendor Y for software and use the appropriate**
methodology for each
- **B Contract with vendor X for both hardware and software and require an agile framework for the**
entire project
- **C Contract with vendor Y for both hardware and software and require a waterfall approach for the**
entire project
- **D Contract with either vendor X or vendor Y for both hardware and software and utilize a master**
services agreement
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might changes be allowed to be made to the adaptive scope without impacting the overall
contract?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Larger projects may use an adaptive approach for some deliverables and a traditional project
management approach for other parts. In these cases, a governing agreement such as a master

---

services agreement (MSA) may be used for the overall engagement, with the adaptive work
being placed in an appendix or supplement. This hybrid strategy allows changes to occur on the
adaptive scope without impacting the overall contract. The incorrect answer choices represent
actions that will not permit the selected vendor from using the best project management approach
for each aspect of the project. Since both vendors are capable of delivering both the hardware
and the software, and since there is not enough information in the question to determine which
one of them is better in delivering projects using waterfall or agile project management
approach, among the available choices, utilizing a master services agreement (MSA) with either
of the vendors provides the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Contract with vendor X for hardware, with vendor Y for software and use the appropriate**
methodology for each
Incorrect. This approach represents a course of action which resolves the issue of which
project management methodology to use. However, since both vendors are equally capable
of producing both the hardware and the software, then it is better to make appropriate
arrangements to allow one vendor to deliver both as it may save project resources in
managing one vendor instead of two.
- **B Contract with vendor X for both hardware and software and require an agile framework**
for the entire project
Incorrect. As stated by the scenario, it has been concluded that an agile framework is best
for developing the software component of the project, but not the hardware. Limiting the
vendor to use one approach over another would diminish from the benefits of using the best
project management approach for each aspect of the project.
- **C Contract with vendor Y for both hardware and software and require a waterfall approach**
for the entire project
Incorrect. According to the question text, a traditional waterfall project management
approach is best to develop the hardware for the project in this case, but not the software
component. Limiting the vendor to use one approach over another would diminish from the
benefits of using the best project management approach for each aspect of the project.
- **D Contract with either vendor X or vendor Y for both hardware and software and utilize a**
master services agreement

---

Correct. In this case, a governing agreement such as a master services agreement (MSA)
may be used with any of the vendors for the overall engagement, with the adaptive work
being placed in an appendix or supplement.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 465

PMP Exam 5

Question 188 of 200
Question ID: 612492
You are managing a project for a company that in conjunction with another vendor has been
contracted by a client to develop a customer relationship management (CRM) system for their
business. Early in project execution, the client terminates the other vendor for undisclosed
reasons and asks if your company can complete the entire project. You had recognized and
analyzed this scenario during project planning, and now this opportunity has materialized.
What should you do first?
Top of Form
- **A Check the risk register for a risk response plan**
- **B Accept the opportunity and ask for an addendum to the existing contract**
- **C Seek an expert opinion to determine whether or not to accept the opportunity**
- **D Submit a change request to update the project management plan and baselines**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Risks can either be threats (negative risks) or opportunities (positive risks).
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that you, as the project manager, had recognized and analyzed the
possibility of taking over the entire project during project planning, which implies that this risk
had been documented in the risk register along with its agreed-upon risk response. Keep in mind
that risks can either be threats (negative risks) or opportunities (positive risks). In the scenario
described the risk is considered an opportunity. Realized risks (either negative or positive) should
trigger the Implement Risk Responses process. The risk register serves as an input to the

---

Implement Risk Responses process and records the agreed-upon risk responses for each
individual risk and the nominated owners for each response plan. Therefore, of the available
answer choices, checking the risk register for a risk response plan is what you should do first.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Check the risk register for a risk response plan**
Correct. The realized risk described by the question should trigger the Implement Risk
Responses process. The risk register serves as an input to the Implement Risk Responses
process and records the agreed-upon risk responses for each individual risk.
- **B Accept the opportunity and ask for an addendum to the existing contract**
Incorrect. The question indicates that you, as the project manager, had recognized and
analyzed the possibility of taking over the entire project during project planning, suggesting
that this risk (which is an opportunity, or a positive risk, in this situation) had been
documented in the risk register along with an agreed-upon risk response. It is possible that
the risk response plan involves accepting the opportunity by signing an addendum to the
existing contract, but that is not known from the question. You should first check the risk
register for the agreed-upon risk response plan before accepting the opportunity.
- **C Seek an expert opinion to determine whether or not to accept the opportunity**
Incorrect. The question indicates that the situation described by the question has already
been analyzed which suggests that a response plan has already been developed and a
determination made as to whether or not to accept the opportunity. The previously
agreed-upon risk response plan should be implemented which may or may not entail
accepting the opportunity.
- **D Submit a change request to update the project management plan and baselines**
Incorrect. The fact that the opportunity described by the question had been identified and
analyzed earlier in the project implies that a response plan has already been developed.
The agreed-upon response plan may or may not include accepting the risk and expanding
the project which requires an approved change request to update the project management
plan and baselines. Since the question does not provide a description of the agreed-upon
risk response plan, the best course of action is to check the risk register for the risk
response plan before taking any other action.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 397, 450
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 189 of 200
Question ID: 651308
The project is falling behind schedule and is over budget. Nonetheless, there is pressure from the
project sponsor to complete the project as scheduled. You must determine what the project’s
performance must be from this point onwards to achieve the delivery goals.
Which calculation are you most likely to use?
Top of Form
- **A SPI**
- **B TCPI**
- **C SV**
- **D BAC**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Are you trying to figure out where your project is now or what it must do from this point on?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

In this situation, you are faced with the project not earning the value as planned. Nevertheless,
you are expected to still meet those planned targets. The rate at which your project must perform
to succeed at reaching that target is what you must determine. The current schedule performance
index, or SPI, is less than one. The question states that the project is underperforming. If the SPI
were 1.0, then the project would be on target. Since it is below the 1.0 target, you must figure out
what the SPI rate must be to make up for that lost ground and pull within the target. That

---

calculation is the to-complete performance index or TCPI. The TCPI equation is (BAC – EV) /
(BAC – AC).

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A SPI**
Incorrect. Based on the information provided in the question, the SPI is less than one. If the
project were to continue at that performance rate, the project would miss the schedule
targets. What must be determined is the adjusted schedule performance rate to achieve the
goals, not the current state.
- **B TCPI**
Correct. From this point in the project to the expected end point, the project must perform
better than it has. Since the project is underperforming in terms of schedule, the
to-complete performance index (TCPI) calculates that new rate of production necessary
from this point in the project to the end to meet the predefined targets.
- **C SV**
Incorrect. Knowing the variance between the planned schedule and the actual schedule
performance does not give you enough data to determine the performance rate and
expectations necessary to achieve the schedule targets.
- **D BAC**
Incorrect. The BAC is the target the project sponsor is expecting from your project but does
not indicate the work rate at which your project must perform to reach the target as
planned. The budget at completion (BAC) is needed to calculate the to-complete
performance index but is not enough on its own.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 266
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 190 of 200
Question ID: 612550
- **A project manager has taken over a project that has been in execution for a few months. He ran**
into problems right away. He has had difficulty getting sign off on decisions; he doesn't have the
authority to acquire the equipment necessary for the project; the stakeholders and the project
team have differing opinions about the objectives and the outcome of the project.
What is the most likely source of these problems?
Top of Form
- **A Weak leadership skills**
- **B Lack of a project charter**
- **C Lack of a project management plan**
- **D Lack of a procurement management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which document authorizes the existence of a project and gives the project manager authority?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

- **A project charter is the document that authorizes the existence of a project and provides the**
project manager with the authority to apply organizational resources to project activities. The
project charter also states the purpose, primary objectives, vision, and mission for the project,
aligning the project stakeholders and the project team with the project goals, expectations, and
outcomes. A project sponsor approves the project charter and is supposed to provide support for
the project manager to achieve the project goals. While other answer choices could have been the

---

source of 'some' of the project manager's problems, the lack of a project charter addresses all of
the project manager's problems and is, therefore, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Weak leadership skills**
Incorrect. Leadership skills involve the ability to guide, motivate, and direct a team, as well
as continuously communicate the project vision to the stakeholders and the team. The
scenario suggests the stakeholders and the project team have differing opinions about the
objectives and the outcome of the project. Although weak leadership skills may have led to
that problem, there are other issues with project implying that the project manager's weak
leadership skills are not the main or the only source of the issues.
- **B Lack of a project charter**
Correct. The project charter formally authorizes the existence of a project and would have
provided the project manager with the authority to apply organizational resources to
project activities. A project sponsor approves and signs off the charter and acts as a project
champion who supports the project, the project manager, and is concerned with the
project's success. Therefore, the difficulty the project manager is encountering with
decision making and acquiring computer hardware may have been eliminated if there had
been a charter. The project charter also states the purpose, primary objectives, and vision
for the project and would have provided the project team, as well as the stakeholders, with
the same understanding of such. An approved project charter could have prevented the
issues mentioned in the scenario from happening. Therefore, the lack of a project charter is
the most likely source of the problems.
- **C Lack of a project management plan**
Incorrect. The project management plan describes how the project will be executed,
monitored and controlled, and closed. The problems the project manager is having with the
project are related to his lack of authority, a lack of project goals, and difficulty getting
sponsors to make decisions. These issues represent the lack of a project charter and not the
lack of a project management plan.
- **D Lack of a procurement management plan**
Incorrect. The procurement management plan describes how a project team will acquire
goods and services from outside of the performing organization. the project manager's
problem obtaining the computer hardware is most likely related to his lack of authority to
purchase the equipment, not the lack of a procurement management plan.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 75-76, 81; see also
https://www.projectmanagement.com/blog-post/8417/A-Project-With-No-Project-Charter-
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 191 of 200
Question ID: 626018
- **A senior manager has just been appointed as a project sponsor for a new project the company is**
about to undertake. The newly appointed sponsor starts developing a project charter but is not
sure what information should be included. The sponsor seeks advice from an experienced project
manager.
The project manager responds that at a minimum, the project charter should include which of the
following:
Top of Form
- **A High-level information about the project**
- **B Detailed project scope and schedule**
- **C A list of all project stakeholders**
- **D A list of vendors selected for the project**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the purpose of the project charter? This should define its contents.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The type and amount of information in the project charter depends on the complexity of the
project and the information known at the time of its creation. At a minimum, the project charter
should define the high-level information about the project that will be used to elaborate on the
project management plan progressively. Additionally, the project charter should set a clear vision
and mission for the project team and stakeholders allowing the project manager to lead the team
towards the achievement of the project goals. One may argue, that "at a minimum" does not limit

---

the project charter to include high-level information only. They may assume that if the detailed
information about the scope, schedule, stakeholders, vendors, is already available at that point, it
should be included in the charter as well. This assumption is inaccurate because it goes against
the purpose of the project charter which is to authorize the existence of a project, to name the
project manager, and provide the project manager with the authority to apply organizational
resources to project activities. Also, spending the time to develop a detailed scope and schedule,
and list 'all' project stakeholders and selected vendors in the project charter would be an
inefficient use of project resources during project initiation. These activities have dedicated
processes later in the project lifecycle.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A High-level information about the project**
Correct. At a minimum, a project charter should include high-level information about the
project. This information will be used to develop the project management plan.
- **B Detailed project scope and schedule**
Incorrect. Detailed project scope and schedule are not required to be included in the
project charter. Detailed project scope and schedule are created during the development of
the project management plan and its various components.
- **C A list of all project stakeholders**
Incorrect. The project charter may include some of the key project stakeholders. However, a
list of 'all' project stakeholders will be available in the stakeholder register only after the
Identify Stakeholders process is completed.
- **D A list of vendors selected for the project**
Incorrect. Vendors for the project are selected during the Conduct Procurements process.
Selected sellers (vendors) are among the outputs of that process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 83
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 192 of 200
Question ID: 612402
You are managing a project to develop a robotic window washing system. Many of the necessary
parts of the robotic system will be obtained from third-party vendors. At this point in the project,
you have obtained the vendor responses for the electronics required for the robots, selected a
vendor, and awarded a contract.
Which of the following should you do next in Project Procurement Management?
Top of Form
- **A Make-or-buy analysis**
- **B Performance reviews**
- **C Procurement statement of work (SOW)**
- **D Develop source selection criteria**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This question describes activities that occur during Conduct Procurements. The next action
would be a tool used in the Control Procurements process.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

In the scenario described you are in the Conduct Procurements process having completed the
vendor selection process and awarded a contract. The next process in the Project Procurement
Management Knowledge Area is the Control Procurements process where the contract
performance is monitored and controlled. All the answer choices, except performance reviews,
describe tools used during the Plan Procurement Management process which precedes the
Conduct Procurement process. Performance reviews are used to measure, compare, and analyze

---

characteristics of the procured item and compare it against the vendor agreement. It is the only
tool listed from the Control Procurements process making it the correct answer choice.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Make-or-buy analysis**
Incorrect. A make-or-buy analysis is used during the Plan Procurement Management
process to determine whether work or deliverables can best be accomplished by the project
team or should be purchased from outside sources. In this scenario, you have obtained
vendor responses, selected a vendor, and awarded a contract which are all activities
performed in the Conduct Procurements process. Since the Plan Procurement Management
process precedes the Conduct Procurements process, a make-or-buy analysis would have
already been completed at this point in the project life cycle.
- **B Performance reviews**
Correct. According to the scenario, you have obtained vendor responses, selected a vendor,
and awarded a contract, all of which are activities that are performed as part of the
Conduct Procurements process. The next step in the Project Procurement Management
Knowledge Area would be the Control Procurement process where contract progress is
monitored using performance reviews.
- **C Procurement statement of work (SOW)**
Incorrect. The SOW describes the item being procured and is shared with prospective
vendors so that the vendors can determine if they are capable of producing the deliverable.
The procurement SOW is developed during the Plan Procurement Management process
which precedes the activities of obtaining vendor responses, selecting a vendor and
awarding a contract, described in the scenario. Therefore, this is not the correct answer.
- **D Develop source selection criteria**
Incorrect. Source selection criteria are developed during the Plan Procurement
Management process to be used as evaluation criteria during vendor selection. In the
scenario described, you are in the Conduct Procurements process and have already
selected a vendor. Therefore, the source selection criteria would have already been
developed, making this an incorrect answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 498, 492, 482

PMP Exam 5
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 193 of 200
Question ID: 612523
- **A new startup is running a project to design and build a website for families to share solutions to**
problems encountered when raising children. The resulting knowledge base aims to identify
trends in issues, help families identify common problems, and find solutions that work best for
parents and kids.
Which of the following should be considered the highest priority when planning and designing
how the project team works with the information collected about the children?
Top of Form
- **A Prevalence of flu outbreaks**
- **B Parents' knowledge of problems that exist in their families**
- **C Confidentiality of personal data**
- **D User interface requirements**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The electronic data may represent personal information.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

This question is slightly tricky, as it takes the concepts of knowledge management that you need
in your project and extends it to the product of the project, which also requires knowledge
management. In other words, the objective of the project is to build a website used to manage
knowledge. The overarching issue in any knowledge management solution (physical or
electronic) is the segregation of information based on the need to know and legal restrictions.
Therefore, confidentiality will be a major concern with the website under development. Although

---

there may be requirements for handling peak loads that could be caused by flu outbreaks and
other requirements for the system, these other requirements are not critical to the system design.
Therefore, ensuring the confidentiality of personal data will be the highest priority.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Prevalence of flu outbreaks**
Incorrect. Flu outbreaks may increase the number of users on the system, simulating a
system load test. But a load test based on the volume of potential users during a flu
outbreak would create is a secondary concern to another more essential part of the system.
- **B Parents' knowledge of problems that exist in their families**
Incorrect. The system design isn't dependent on the knowledge that the families possess.
The system is being created to help fill in gaps in parent's knowledge, so discoveries or
trends can be identified. Therefore, a parent’s knowledge of problems that exist is not a
major influencer of system design, but this knowledge is exactly the type of data that would
populate the system, once built.
- **C Confidentiality of personal data**
Correct. This system will contain personal data that needs to be protected. Just like a
project knowledge management system, confidential data on a system such as described in
this scenario must be protected.
- **D User interface requirements**
Incorrect. Although user interface requirements are very important, ensuring the
confidentiality of the electronic data in the system is the highest priority system design
concern. Thus, although this choice presents a valid answer, it is not the 'best' answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 101
